Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate

The Unity of the Subject of a Science
Debate on whether a science can have multiple subjects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the unity of the subject of a science and evaluate the logical argument against the majority who allow multiplicity.

Core Idea
A science must have a single subject; multiplicity of subjects would tear it apart.

This passage addresses a foundational issue in the methodology of the sciences: can a single science have more than one subject? The Hanafi school insists on a single subject, while the majority of verifiers allow multiplicity. The author provides a logical proof linking subjects to issues and sciences, and refutes the objections. Understanding this debate clarifies the boundaries and structure of Islamic sciences like usul al-fiqh and fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Understand the concept of mawdu'
Identify that the subject (mawdu') is that about which a science investigates its accidental properties (awarid dhatiyya). The differences among sciences arise from differences in their issues (masail), which in turn depend on the subjects.
This is the foundational premise.
2
Grasp the logical chain
Follow the argument: if one science had multiple subjects, those subjects would generate different issues, leading to different sciences. Thus, a single subject is necessary to maintain the unity of the science.
The chain: multiplicity of subject -> multiplicity of issues -> multiplicity of sciences.
3
Examine the objection and responses
The objection: why not simply stipulate that a science is one despite multiple subjects? The author gives two responses: (1) the majority themselves require a common aspect, so arbitrary stipulation fails; (2) if allowed, one could absurdly combine fiqh and geometry.
This shows the necessity of a rational basis, not mere convention.
4
Analyze the Talwih's refinement
The text from al-Talwih classifies sciences based on whether the investigated (mabhuth anhu) is a relation (idafa) or not. If it is a relation and accidental properties arise from both relata, the subject is both (as in usul al-fiqh). Otherwise, the subject is single.
This provides a nuanced criterion beyond a blanket rule.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: determining the boundaries between sciences. For example, does usul al-fiqh have one subject (proofs and rulings as a relation) or two? The Hanafi position ensures distinct sciences.
This affects how we organize and teach these disciplines.

قَوْلُهُ ) وَاعْلَمُ إلخ ) هَذِهِ قَلَالَهُ مَبَاحِتْ فِي الْمَوْضُوع أَوْرَدَهَا مُخَالِفًا لِجُمْهُورِ المُحَقِّقِينَ يَتَعَجَّبُ مِنْهَا النَّاظِرُ فِيهَا الْوَاقِفُ عَلَى كَلَامِ الْقَوْمِ فِي هَذَا الْمَقَامِ الْأَوَّلُ أَنْ إِطْلَاقَ الْقَوْلِ بِجَوَازِ تَعَدُّدِ الْمَوْضُوعِ ، وَإِنْ كَانَ فَوْقَ الاثْنَيْنِ غَيْرُ صَحِيحٍ بَلْ التَّحْقِيقُ أَنَّ الْمَبْحُوتَ عَنْهُ فِي الْعِلْمِ إِمَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ إِضَافَةٌ بَيْنَ الشَّيْئَيْنِ أَوْ لَا وَعَلَى الْأَوَّلِ إِمَّا أَنْ تَكُونَ الْعَوَارِضُ الَّتِى لَهَا دَخُلْ فِي الْمَبُحُوثِ عَنْهُ بَعْضُهَا نَاشِعًا عَنْ أَحَدِ الْمُضَافَيْن وَبَعْضُهَا نَاشِنًا عَنْ الْمُصَافِ الْآخَرِ أَوْ لَا ، فَإِنْ كَانَ كَذَلِكَ فَمَوْضُوعُ الْعِلْمِ كَلَا الْمُضَافَيْنِ كَمَا وَقَعَ الْبَحْتُ فِي الْأُصُولِ عَنْ إِثْبَاتِ . الأدِلَّةِ لِلْأحْكَامِ وَالْأَحْوَالِ الَّتِي لَهَا دَخُل فِي ذَلِكَ بَعْضُهَا نَاشِ عَنْ الدَّلِيلِ كَالعُمُوم وَالاشْتِرَابِ وَالثَّوَاتُرِ وَبَعْضُهَا عَنْ الْحُكْمِ كَكَوْنِهِ عِبَادَةً أَوْ عُقُوبَةٌ فَمَوْضُوعُهُ الَّا دِلَّهُ وَالْأَحْكَامُ جَمِيعًا وَأَمَّا إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنُ الْمَبْحُوتُ عَنْهُ إضَافَةٌ كَمَا فِي الْفِقْهِ الْبَاحِثِ عَنْ وُجُوبِ فِعْلِ المُكَلفِ وَحُرُمَتِهِ وَغَيْرِ ذَلِكَ أَوْ كَانَ إِضَافَةٌ لَكِنْ لَا دَخَلَ لِلْاحَوَالِ النَّاشِئَةِ عَنْ أَحَدِ الْمُصَافَيْنِ فِي الْمَبُحُوثِ عَنْهُ كَمَا فِي الْمَنْطِقِ الْبَاحِثِ عَنْ إِيصَالِ تَصَوُّرٍ أَوْ تَصْدِيقِ إِلَى تَصَوُّرٍ أَوْ تَصْدِيقِ وَلَا دَخَلَ لِأَحْوَالِ التَّصَوُّرِ وَالتَّصْدِيقِ الْمُوْصَلِ إِلَيْهِ فِي ذَلِكَ عَلَى مَا قَرِّرَهُ الْمُصَنِّفُ فِيمَا سَبَقَ فَالْمَوْضُوعُ لَا يَكُونُ إِلَّا وَاحِدًا ؛ لِأَنَّ اختلاف الْمَوْضُوعِ يُوجِبُ اخْتِلافَ المَسَائِلِ الْمُوجِبَ لِاخْتِلَافِ العِلْمِ ضَرُورَةَ أَنَّ الْعِلْمَ إِنَّمَا يَخْتَلِفُ بِاخْتِلَافِ الْمَعْلُومَاتِ وَهِيَ الْمَسَائِلُ . ترجمہ: یہ تین مباحث میں موضوع میں ذکر کیا ہے ان کو مخالفت کرتے ہوئے جمہور محققین کی کہ تعجب کرتا ہے اس سے نظر کرنے والا اس میں جو واقف ہو قوم کی کلام پر اس مقام میں ۔ کہ بیشک تعدد موضوع کے جواز کے قول کا مطلق ہونا اگر چہ دو سے اوپر ہو صیح نہیں ہے بلکہ تحقیق یہ ہے کہ بیشک مجوٹ عنہ علم میں یا تو وہ اضافت بین اسمین ہوگی یا نہیں ۔ پہلی صورت پر (جب اضافت ہو ) یا تو وہ عوارض جن کو دخل ہے مجوٹ عنہ میں اس طرح ہونگے کہ ان کے بعض پیدا ہونے والے ہوں گے مضافین میں سے ایک سے اور بعض پیدا ہونے والے ہوں گے دوسرے مضاف سے یا ایسے نہیں ہوگا ۔ پس اگر اس طرح ہو تو
Proof: The principle is that the difference and multiplicity in sciences arises from the difference and multiplicity of issues and information, and the difference of issues and information depends on subjects. Now if it is said that multiplicity in the subject of a science is possible, then it necessitates difference of issues and information. And difference of issues and information necessitates difference of sciences. It was assumed to be one science, but multiple sciences emerged. This problem arose because the subject of a single science was declared absolutely multiple. If by 'one science' what is stipulated [is meant] etc.: This phrase answers a presumed question. Question: Why do we not simply stipulate that despite differences in issues, the science remains one? That is, by stipulation it is one, even if its subjects are multiple and even if there is no common aspect among the multiple subjects; then multiplicity of subject would not necessitate multiplicity of science, because its unity is established by stipulation. Answer (1): The author says that this [stipulation] is not considered because here, despite multiplicity of subject without regard to a common aspect, the stipulation of unity of science is established, which is not correct because those who allow multiplicity of subject also require a common aspect; therefore this stipulation is not valid. Answer (2): If we establish such a stipulation, then it becomes difficult to close the door; for example, a person says I consider the science of fiqh and the science of geometry as one science; how will you shut his mouth? Whereas calling them one science is absolutely false. So it is evident that establishing this stipulation that the science is one despite differences in information and issues is self-evidently false. And what about the two examples? The response to the majority's proof: This is that who told you that in medicine, these are independent subjects? They are not discussed in medicine as independent subjects; rather, the subject of medicine, which is the human body, and the discussion of medicines is in terms of their being accidental properties intrinsic to that subject—whether these medicines cause health or disease. Talkwih. His statement 'And know...' etc.: These are three discussions about the subject brought up in opposition to the majority of the verifiers. The one who looks at this and is aware of the words of the people in this place is amazed. First, the absolute statement of the permissibility of multiplicity of subject, even if more than two, is not correct. Rather, the reality is that that which is investigated in a science is either a relation between two things or not. In the first case, either the accidental properties that have a role in the investigated subject are such that some arise from one of the two related things and some from the other related thing, or not. If it is like that, then the subject of the science is both of the two related things, as occurred in usul [al-fiqh] regarding establishing the proofs for rulings and the states that have a role in that—some arise from the proof, like generality, ambiguity, and tawatur, and some from the ruling, like its being an act of worship or a punishment. So its subject is all the proofs and the rulings. But when the investigated subject is not a relation, as in fiqh which investigates the obligation of an action of the mukallaf, its prohibition, etc., or it is a relation but there is no role for the states arising from one of the two related things in the investigated subject, as in logic which investigates the delivery of a concept or judgment to a concept or judgment, and there is no role for the states of the concept and judgment being delivered to in that, according to what the author established earlier, then the subject is only one; because difference of subject necessitates difference of issues, which necessitates difference of science, necessarily, because a science differs only with the difference of known things, which are the issues. Translation: He mentioned these three discussions about the subject opposing the majority of the verifiers—the observer who is aware of the words of the people in this place is amazed. Indeed, the absolute statement of the permissibility of multiplicity of subject, even if more than two, is not correct. Rather, the investigation is that the investigated in the science is either a relation between two names or not. In the first case, either the accidental properties that have a role in the investigated are such that some arise from one of the two related things and some from the other related thing, or not. So if it is like that, then...

Commentary
This passage is an usul dispute and explanation concerning the unity of the subject (mawdu') of a science. The author begins by stating a principle: differences among sciences arise from differences in their issues (masa'il), and differences in issues depend on differences in subjects. Therefore, if a single science were to have multiple subjects, it would entail multiple issues and hence multiple sciences, contradicting the assumption of unity. The author then addresses a potential objection: could one not simply stipulate (istilah) that a science is one despite multiple subjects, even without a common aspect? He gives two answers: first, the majority who allow multiple subjects themselves require a common aspect, so such a stipulation is invalid; second, if arbitrary stipulation were allowed, one could claim that fiqh and geometry are one science, which is absurd. This shows that stipulating unity despite differences is self-evidently false. The text then shifts to a more detailed analysis from Al-Talwih: the investigation of whether a science can have multiple subjects depends on the nature of the investigated subject (al-mabhuth 'anhu). If it is a relation (idafa) between two things, and the accidental properties (awarid) under investigation arise from both sides, then the subject is both—as in usul al-fiqh, which studies proofs and rulings together. If it is not a relation, as in fiqh (which studies actions of the mukallaf), or if it is a relation but only one side's properties are relevant, as in logic, then the subject is single. The conclusion: the subject must be one, because multiplicity of subject necessarily leads to multiplicity of issues and hence to multiplicity of sciences.

Key Terms
الموضوع (al-mawḍūʿ): The subject matter of a science, the primary topic about which the science investigates its accidental properties.
المسائل (al-masāʾil): The issues or derived rulings that constitute the content of a science.
العوارض الذاتية (al-ʿawāriḍ al-dhātiyya): Accidental properties intrinsic to the subject, which are the focus of investigation in a science.
الإضافة (al-iḍāfa): Relation between two things. If the investigated subject is a relation, and accidental properties arise from both relata, the subject is both relata.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason a science must have a single subject?
A) Because the majority of scholars said so.
B) Because difference in subjects necessitates difference in issues, which necessitates difference in sciences.
C) Because sciences are defined by arbitrary stipulation.
D) Because subjects can be multiple if there is no common aspect.

Key Takeaway
A science must have a single subject; apparent multiplicity is resolved by identifying that additional topics are accidental properties or that the subject is a relation unifying two relata.

Multiplicity of Topics and Sciences: The Condition of Proportionality (Tanāsub)
Debate on multiplicity of topics and sciences with condition of proportionality

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two premises on multiplicity of topics and sciences, apply the condition of proportionality (tanasub) to determine whether multiplicity necessitates multiplicity of sciences, and evaluate the Hanafi position against the opposing view.

Core Idea
Multiplicity of topics in a science is permitted only if they share proportionality (tanasub), either essential or accidental.

In this lesson, we explore a foundational debate in uṣūl al-fiqh: does having multiple subjects (mawḍūʿāt) force a science to split into multiple sciences? The passage critically examines two premises and introduces the key concept of tanāsub (proportionality). By understanding this condition, you will see how the Hanafi school preserves the unity of uṣūl al-fiqh despite its four sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two premises and the opponent's question
Read the opening lines: the first premise states that difference of topics necessitates difference of issues (masāʾil); the second states that difference of issues necessitates difference of sciences. The opponent asks for clarification: what does 'ikhtilāf al-masāʾil' mean?
Note the ambiguity: 'difference' can mean mere multiplicity or lack of proportionality.
2
Distinguish the two meanings of 'ikhtilāf al-masāʾil'
If it means mere multiplicity (kathra), then premise 1 is accepted but premise 2 is rejected because every science has many issues. If it means lack of proportionality (ʿadam tanāsub), then premise 1 is not absolute; it only holds when topics themselves lack proportionality.
This distinction is crucial to understanding the Hanafi position.
3
Understand the condition of tanāsub and its two types
Proportionality is the condition that allows multiple topics in one science. It comes in two forms: sharing in an essential attribute (amr dhātī) like quantity in geometry, or sharing in an accidental attribute (amr ʿaraḍī) like health in medicine.
Essential attributes are intrinsic; accidental attributes relate to the purpose of the science.
4
Apply the condition to the examples
In geometry, line, surface, and solid all share the essential attribute of quantity (miqdār), so they form one science. In medicine, body parts, foods, humors, and temperaments all share the accidental attribute of health (the goal of medicine). Thus, multiplicity is permissible.
These examples illustrate how tanāsub unifies apparently diverse topics.
5
Analyze the criticism of the matn's examples and the Hanafi response
The commentator objects: the matn itself offers usul al-fiqh as an example where the essential accidents of four evidence instances (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) are studied, implying four subjects. The author of al-Talwīḥ (Taftazani) argues this proves permissible multiplicity. The response distinguishes between multiplicity in predicates (madaʿmin) and multiplicity in the subject itself; the former is allowed, the latter is not without tanāsub.
This shows the precision needed in defining a science's subject.

پہلا مقدمہ تھا کہ موضوعات کا اختلاف مسائل کے اختلاف کو ستلزم ہے اور دوسرا مقدمہ تھا کہ مسائل کا اختلاف علم کے اختلاف کوستلزم ہے۔ سوال: یہ ہے کہ آپ نے کہا موضوعات کا اختلاف مسائل کے اختلاف کو مستلزم ہے اس سے تمہاری کیا مراد ہے؟ اس لیے کہ اس کے دو معنے ہو سکتے ہیں (۱) مسائل کا اختلاف بمعنی کثرت مسائل کے ہو (۲) مسائل کا اختلاف بمعنی عدم تناسب بین المسائل ہو ۔ اب بتاؤ کہ کونا معنی مراد ہے؟ بالمعنی الاول مراد ہے یا بالمعنی الثانی مراد ہے اگر آپ کثرت مسائل بالمعنی الاول مراد لیتے ہیں تو مقدمہ اولی سو فیصد مسلم ہے کہ اختلاف موضوع مستلزم ہے اختلاف مسائل بمعنی کثرت مسائل کو لیکن دوسرا مقدمہ تسلیم نہیں ہے کہ اختلاف مسائل اختلاف علم کو ستلزم ہو اس لئے کہ ہر علم کے ہزاروں مسائل ہیں کوئی علم بھی ایسا نہیں ہے ج کا صرف ایک ھی مسئلہ ہو لھذا کثرت مسائل کثرت علم کوستلزم نہیں ہے اور اگر اختلاف بالمعنی الثانی مراد ہے پھر مقدمہ اولی کو ہم علی الاطلاق تسلیم نہیں کرتے کہ موضوعات کا اختلاف مسائل کے اختلاف کومستلزم ہوتا ہے بلکہ اسمیں تفصیل ہے کہ اختلاف موضوع کی دو صورتیں ہیں (۱) پہلی صورت یہ ہے کہ موضوعات میں کثرت ہو لیکن آپس میں متناسب نہ ہوں (۲) دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ موضوعات میں کثرت ہو اور آپس میں متناسب بھی ہوں۔ اگر موضوعات میں تعدد اور آپس میں کوئی مناسبت نہ ہو تو اس صورت میں موضوعات کا اختلاف اختلاف مسائل بمعنی عدم تناسب بین المسائل گوستلزم ہوگا۔ اور اگر مسائل آپس میں مناسب ہوں تو پھر یہ قطعا اختلاف مسائل بمعنی عدم تناسب بین المسائل کو تلزم نہیں ہے اور جمہور بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں کہ موضوعات میں تعدد جائز ہے بشرطیکہ ان میں تناسب ہو اور یہ اختلاف مسائل بمعنی عدم تناسب بین المسائل گوستلزم نہیں ہے کہ تم یہ کہو کہ یہ اختلاف علم کو ستلزم ہے۔
تناسب کی صورتیں :۔ تناسب کی دو صورتیں ہیں (۱) ان کا امر ذاتی میں اشتراک ہو (۲) امر عرضی میں اشتراک ہوامر ذاتی میں اشتراک کی مثال جیسے علم ھندسہ کا موضوع تین چیزیں ہیں۔ خط سطح اور جسم تعلیمی لیکن یہ تینوں امر ذاتی میں مشترک ہیں اور وہ ہے مقدار یعنی کم متصل قار الذات جسکے اجزاء مجتمع فی الوجود ہوں۔ امر عرضی میں اشتراک کی مثال ۔ جیسے علم طلب کا موضوع بدن انسانی ہے اور اجزاء بدنی جیسے ناک کان دل وغیرہ ہیں علم طب میں ان سے بھی بحث ہوتی ہے ایسے ہی دوائیں ہیں غذا ئیں ہیں اور ارکان ہیں یعنی صفراء کا غالب ہوتا بدن میں یا سوداء کا غالب ہونا یا بلغم کا غالب ہونا اور ایسے ہی علم طب میں مزاجوں سے بھی بحث کی جاتی ہے الغرض علم طب میں یہ متعدد چیزیں زیر بحث ہیں لیکن یہ سب امر عرضی میں مشترک ہیں اور وہ امر عرضی ہے صحت باقی صحت امر عرضی کیوں ہے؟ اس لیے کہ صحت علم طب کی غرض و غایت ہے اور شئی کی غرض و غایت شئی سے خارج ہوتی ہے اور جو چیز شئی سے خارج ہو وہ عرض کے قبیل سے ہوتی ہے۔ وان ليس لأحد الخ ... باقی تمہیں یہ پریشانی تھی کہ ہر شخص اصطلاح قائم کریگا کہ موضوعات کے تعدد کے باوجود یہ علم واحد ہے مثلاً ایک شخص یہ کہتا ہے کہ علم فقہ اور علم ہندسہ یہ علم واحد ہے کہ یہ اصطلاح قائم کرے کہ علم فقہ اور علم ھندسہ علم واحد ہیں یہ کوئی پریشانی نہیں اس لئے کہ کسی کو یہ حق نہیں ہے کہ یہ اصطلاح قائم کرے کہ علم فقہ اور علم ہندسہ علم واحد ہیں باوجود یکہ موضوع میں تعدد ہے لیکن یہ جائز تب ہو گا جب اس میں تناسب ہوگا حالانکہ ان کے موضوعات میں کوئی تناسب نہیں ہے۔
ماتن کی بیان کردہ مثالوں پر شاریخ کا رد
ثم انه اوردفيما الخ... شارحٌ مصنف پر سوال کر رہے ہیں کہ آپ نے یہ دعوی کیا کہ موضوع میں تعدد جائز نہیں ہے اور جو مثالیں تم نے پیش کی ہیں ان سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ موضوع میں تعدد جائز ہے آپ نے دو مثالیں دی ہیں اصول فقہ کی اور منطق کی۔
مثال اول: یہ ہے کہ فن اصول فقہ کے محمولات یعنی عوارض ذاتیہ کا دلیل کے مفہوم کیلئے اثبات نہیں ہوگا بلکہ مصداق دلیل کیلئے اثبات ہوگا اور اس کا مصداق تو کتاب اللہ ۔ سنت رسول ما اجماع اور قیاس ہے یعنی بعض عوارض ایسے ہوں گے جو مختص ہوں گے صرف کتاب اللہ کے ساتھ۔ یا مختص ہوں گے سنت کے ساتھ یا اجماع کے ساتھ یا قیاس کے ساتھ اور بعض عوارض مشترک ہو نگے دو دو کے درمیان تو چار چیزوں کے عوارض ذاتیہ سے اس علم میں بحث ہوگی اور جن چیزوں کے عوارض ذاتیہ سے بحث ہو وہ اس کا موضوع ہوتی ہیں لہذا اصول فقہ کا موضوع چار چیزیں ہوئیں اور تم نے کہا کہ موضوع میں تعدد نہیں ہوتا۔
سوال:۔ اس صورت میں تو صاحب توضیح بھی تعدد موضوع کے قائل ہیں۔ جواب:۔ صاحب توضیح جس تعداد کے قائل ہیں وہ مضامین کے اعتبار سے ہے لیکن جو تعددان کے علاوہ ہو ان کے قائل نہیں ہیں اور صاحب تلویح جس تعدد کے قائل ہیں وہ قطع نظر مضامین کے ہے کیونکہ مضافین کے اعتبار سے تو موضوع دو ہی ہونگے یعنی مضاف اور مضاف الیہ لیکن علامہ صاحب نے ان مضافین کے علاوہ تعدد ثابت کیا ہے انہی مثالوں سے جن کو مائن نے ذکر کیا تھا۔ علامہ کے اصل اعتراض کا جواب
کہ جیسے علامہ صاحب نے تعدد موضوع اصول فقہ کے لئے ثابت کیا ہے بایں وجہ کہ ادلہ کے اعراض ذاتیہ کو مفہوم ادلہ کے لئے
The first premise was that the difference of topics necessitates the difference of issues. And the second premise was that the difference of issues necessitates the difference of knowledge. Question: What do you mean by saying that the difference of topics necessitates the difference of issues? Because it can have two meanings: (1) difference of issues in the sense of multiplicity of issues, (2) difference of issues in the sense of lack of proportionality between issues. Now tell, which meaning is intended? Is the first meaning intended or the second? If you intend multiplicity of issues in the first sense, then the first premise is 100% accepted—that difference of topics necessitates difference of issues in the sense of multiplicity of issues—but the second premise is not accepted, that difference of issues necessitates difference of knowledge, because every science has thousands of issues; no science has only one issue. Therefore, multiplicity of issues does not necessitate multiplicity of knowledge. And if difference is intended in the second sense, then we do not accept the first premise absolutely that difference of topics necessitates difference of issues. Rather, there is detail: difference of topics has two forms: (1) The first form is that there is multiplicity in the topics but they are not proportional among themselves. (2) The second form is that there is multiplicity in the topics and they are proportional among themselves. If there is multiplicity in topics and no proportion among them, then in that case the difference of topics will necessitate difference of issues in the sense of lack of proportionality between issues. And if the issues are proportional among themselves, then this absolutely does not necessitate difference of issues in the sense of lack of proportionality between issues. And the majority also hold this view: that multiplicity of topics is permissible provided there is proportion among them, and this does not necessitate difference of issues in the sense of lack of proportionality between issues, as you say that this necessitates difference of knowledge. Forms of proportionality: There are two forms of proportionality: (1) They share in an essential matter (amr dhati). (2) They share in an accidental matter (amr 'aradi). Example of sharing in an essential matter: like the subject of geometry being three things: line, surface, and solid body (jism ta'līmī). But these three share in an essential matter, which is quantity (miqdar), i.e., continuous quantity whose parts are concurrent in existence. Example of sharing in an accidental matter: like the subject of medicine being the human body, and its parts such as nose, ear, heart, etc. In medicine, these are discussed, as are medicines, foods, and humors (arkan)—i.e., whether yellow bile, black bile, or phlegm predominates in the body. Similarly, in medicine, temperaments are also discussed. In short, in medicine, these multiple things are under discussion, but they all share in an accidental matter, and that accidental matter is health. Why is health an accidental matter? Because health is the purpose and end of medicine, and the purpose and end of a thing is external to the thing, and whatever is external to the thing belongs to the category of accident. And there is no one for... The rest: You had this concern that everyone would establish a terminology that despite multiplicity of topics, this is a single science. For example, if someone says that the science of fiqh and the science of geometry are one science, and he establishes the terminology that the science of fiqh and the science of geometry are one science, this is not a concern, because no one has the right to establish such a terminology—that the science of fiqh and the science of geometry are one science despite multiplicity of topics—but this would be permissible only if there were proportion between them, whereas their topics have no proportion. The commentators' refutation of the examples given by the matn: Then he brought... The commentator questions the author: You claimed that multiplicity of topics is not permissible, and the examples you presented show that multiplicity of topics is permissible. You gave two examples: one from usul al-fiqh and one from logic. First example: In the art of usul al-fiqh, the predicates (mahmulat), i.e., essential accidents ('awarid dhatiyya), are not proven for the meaning (mafhum) of evidence, but for the instance (misdaq) of evidence. And its instance is the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of the Messenger, consensus, and analogy. So some accidents are specific only to the Book of Allah, or specific to the Sunnah, or to consensus, or to analogy, and some accidents are shared between two of them. Thus, the essential accidents of four things are discussed in this science, and whatever things' essential accidents are discussed are its subject. Therefore, the subject of usul al-fiqh becomes four things, while you said that multiplicity of subjects does not occur. Question: In that case, the author of al-Tawdih also holds multiplicity of subjects. Answer: The author of al-Tawdih holds multiplicity in terms of the predicates (mada'min), but holds no multiplicity besides that. And the author of al-Talwih holds multiplicity without regard to predicates, because in terms of the two genitives (mudaf and mudaf ilayh), the subject would be only two, i.e., mudaf and mudaf ilayh. But 'Allamah [Taftazani] proved multiplicity beyond these genitives from the very examples that the matn [Sadr al-Shariah] mentioned. The answer to 'Allamah's original objection: As 'Allamah proved multiplicity of subject for usul al-fiqh on the grounds that the essential accidents of evidences are for the meaning of evidences.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute about whether a single science can have multiple topics (mawdu'at). The author begins by analyzing two premises: (1) difference in topics necessitates difference in masail (issues), and (2) difference in masail necessitates difference in 'ilm (knowledge). The opponent's question forces clarification: does 'ikhtilaf al-masail' mean mere multiplicity (kathra) or lack of proportionality ('adam tanasub)? If the first meaning, premise 1 is accepted but premise 2 is rejected because every science has many masail. If the second meaning, premise 1 is not absolute: multiplicity of topics only leads to lack of proportionality in masail if the topics themselves lack proportionality. The majority holds that multiplicity of topics is allowed if there is proportionality (tanasub) between them. The author then explains two forms of proportionality: essential (amr dhati) as in geometry where line, surface, and solid all share in the essence of quantity; and accidental (amr 'aradi) as in medicine where all topics (body parts, medicines, humors, temperaments) share in the accidental aim of health. The author then addresses the concern that anyone could arbitrarily declare two sciences as one. He argues that such a declaration is invalid without proportionality, as between fiqh and geometry there is none. The commentators (shurrah) then criticize the matn's own examples: from usul al-fiqh, the 'awarid dhatiyya (essential accidents) are proven for the instances of adillah (Book, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas), making four subject-matters. This contradicts the claim that a subject cannot be multiple. The author responds by distinguishing between multiplicity in terms of predicates (mada'min) and multiplicity in the subject itself. Sadr al-Shariah allows the former, Taftazani allows the latter. The passage ends with a rebuttal that Taftazani's proof of multiplicity from the matn's examples is valid. This is a classic Hanafi usul discussion: the subject of a science must be one in reality (bi al-haqiqa), but can be multiple in appearance (bi al-majaz) if a unifying factor exists. The Hanafi school emphasizes that usul al-fiqh's subject is the adillah (evidences) considered as proving ahkam, which unifies the four sources.

Key Terms
التناسب (al-tanāsub): Proportionality or commonality among the topics of a science, either in essence (dhati) or accident ('aradi), that allows them to be considered part of one science.
العرض الذاتي (al-'araḍ al-dhātī): Essential accident—an attribute that follows directly from the essence of a thing, such as quantity for line, surface, and solid.
مصداق الدليل (miṣdāq al-dalīl): The instances of evidence: the Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas, whose essential accidents are studied in usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under what condition is multiplicity of topics (ta'addud al-mawdu'at) permissible in a single science?
A) When the topics are completely different and unrelated.
B) When the topics share a proportional relationship, either essential or accidental.
C) When the topics are reduced to a single topic through abstraction.
D) When the science is divided into separate branches.

Key Takeaway
Multiplicity of topics does not necessitate multiplicity of sciences if the topics share proportionality (tanasub), either essential or accidental.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
The Haythiyyah Objection and Its Resolution
Analyzing the definition of a science's subject and the role of haythiyyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the concept of haythiyyah to identify and resolve the circularity objection in defining the subject of a science.

Core Idea
The aspect (haythiyyah) qualifies the subject as a universal perspective, not an attribute, thereby avoiding self-priority.

A fundamental challenge in defining any science is specifying its subject without falling into circularity. This passage from a Hanafi usul text presents the famous objection regarding the 'aspect' (haythiyyah) and its resolution. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly delimiting the scope of a science and for avoiding logical errors in legal theory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Pinpoint the exact claim: that if haythiyyah is treated as an attribute investigated in the science, it leads to the impossibility of a thing preceding itself. Understand the example: health/sickness in medicine, motion/rest in physics.
The objection is logical, not empirical.
2
Examine the famous answer
The common response is that haythiyyah refers to potential (imkan) and preparedness (isti'dad), not actual attributes. This removes the circularity because potential is not an investigated attribute.
This answer is considered insufficient by the author; the verified position follows.
3
Analyze the verified position (al-tahqiq)
The subject is defined as that from which essential attributes are investigated under a universal aspect (haythiyyah). This aspect is a universal meaning observed in all investigations, not a mediator for every attribute.
Thus, the haythiyyah is not an additional attribute but the very perspective of investigation.
4
Address the further objection
If haythiyyah is made a restrictive condition, it would seemingly prevent investigating the very attributes (e.g., health in medicine). The resolution is that the haythiyyah is not a separate mediator; it is the perspective itself, so no circularity arises.
The key is that the haythiyyah is not an independent entity causing priority.
5
Map to usul al-fiqh
Apply this understanding to the definition of usul al-fiqh: its subject is the evidences (adilla) from the aspect of how they indicate rulings. The haythiyyah here is the 'aspect of indication' (jihat al-dalalah), not an additional attribute.
This clarifies the scope of usul al-fiqh as a science.

نَعَمُ يَرِدُ الْإِشْكالُ الْمَشْهُورُ ، وَهُوَ أَنَّهُ يَجِبُ أَنْ لَا تَكُونَ الْحَيْثِيَّةُ مِنَ الأعْرَاضِ الْمَبْحُوثِ عَنْهَا فِي الْعِلْمِ ضَرُورَةَ أَنَّهَا لَيْسَتْ مِمَّا تَعْرِضُ لِلْمَوْضُوعِ مِنْ جِهَةِ نَفْسِهَا وَإِلَّا لَزِمَ تَقَدُّمُ الشَّيْء عَلَى نَفْسِهِ ضَرُورَةَ أَنَّ مَا بِهِ يَعْرِضُ الشَّيْء لِلشَّيْء لَا بُدَّ أَنْ يَتَقَدَّمَ عَلَى الْعَارِضِ مَثَلًا لَيْسَتْ الصِّحَّةُ وَالْمَرَضُ مِمَّا يَعْرِضُ لِبَدَنِ الْإِنْسَانِ مِنْ حَيْثُ يَصِحُ وَيَمْرَضُ وَلَا الْحَرَكَةُ وَالسُّكُونُ مِمَّا يَعْرِضُ لِلْجِسْمِ مِنْ حَيْثُ يَتَحَرَّكَ وَيَسْكُنُ ، وَالْمَشْهُورُ فِي جَوَابِهِ أَنَّ الْمُرَادَ مِنْ حَيْثُ إمُكَانُ الصِّحَّةِ وَالْمَرَضِ وَالْحَرَكَةِ وَالسُّكُون وَالاسْتِعْدَادِ لِذَلِكَ : وَهَذَا لَيْسَ مِنْ الْأَعْرَاضِ الْمَبْحُوثِ عَنْهَا فِي الْعِلْمِ وَالتَّحْقِيقُ أَنَّ الْمَوْضُوعَ لَمَّا كَانَ عِبَارَةٌ عَنْ الْمَبْحُوثِ فِي الْعِلْمِ عَنْ أَعْرَاضِهِ الذَّاتِيَّةِ قُيِّدَ بِالْحَيْثِيَّةِ عَلَى مَعْنَى أَنَّ الْبَحْتَ عَنْ الْعَوَارِضِ يَكُونُ بِاعْتِبَارِ الْحَيْثِيَّةِ وَبِالنَّظَرِ إِلَيْهَا أَى يُلاحَظُ فِي جَمِيعِ المَبَاحِثِ هَذَا الْمَعْنَى الْكُلّى لَا عَلَى مَعْنَى أَنْ جَمِيعَ الْعَوَارِضِ الْمَبْحُوثِ عَنْهَا يَكُونُ لُحُوقُهَا لِلْمَوْضُوعِ بِوَاسِطَةِ هَذِهِ الْحَيْثِيَّةِ الْبَتَّةَ . 
ترجمہ: جی ہاں وارد ہوتا ہے مشہور اشکال اور وہ یہ ہے کہ واجب ہے کہ نہ ہو بحثیت علم میں مجوث عنھا کے اعراض سے بوجہ ضروری ہونے اس بات کے کہ بیشک وہ (حیثیت) نہیں ہے ان چیزوں میں سے جو عارض ہوتی ہیں موضوع کو اپنے نفس کی جہت سے وگرنہ لازم آئیگا شئی کا مقدم ہونا اپنے آپ پر بوجہ بدیہی ہونے اس بات کے کہ بیشک وہ شئی کہ جس کے ذریعے سے ایک مئی دوسری شئی کو عارض ہوتی ہے ضروری ہے کہ وہ مقدم ہو عارض پر مثال کے طور پر نہیں ہے صحت اور مرض ان اشیاء میں سے ہے جو لاحق ہوں بدن انسانی کو اس حیثیت سے کہ وہ صحیح ہوتا ہے اور مریض ہوتا ہے اور نہ ہی حرکت اور سکون اس میں سے جو لاحق ہوں جسم کو اس حیثیت سے کہ وہ حرکت کرتا ہے اور سکون کرتا ہے اور مشہور اس کے جواب میں یہ ہے کہ بیشک مراد ہے صحت اور مرض کے امکان کی حیثیت یا حرکت اور سکون کے امکان کی حیثیت اور اس کی استعداد اور یہ نہیں ہے علم میں مجوث عنہا کے اعراض میں سے۔ اور تحقیق یہ ہے کہ بیشک موضوع جب عبارت ہے علم میں مجوث عنہا کے اعراض ذاتیہ سے تو مقید کیا گیا حیثیت کے ساتھ بناء کرتے ہوئے اس معنی پر کہ بحث عوارض سے وہ حیثیت کے اعتبار سے ہوتی ہے اور حیثیت کی طرف دیکھنے سے ہوتی ہے یعنی لحاظ کیا جاتا ہے تمام مباحث میں اس معنی کلی کا نہ کہ اس معنی پر کہ بیشک جمیع عوارض مسحوث عنہا کا لحوق ہوتا ہے موضوع کو اس حیثیت کے واسطہ سے یقینی طور پر ۔ 
حیثیت کو قید بنانے کی صورت میں تقدم اشی علی نفسہ تو لازم نہیں آتا ؟ 
نعم : شارع نے کہا کہ حیثیت کو قید بنانے کی صورت میں ہم پر یہ ماقبل والا اعتراض لازم نہیں آتا لیکن ایک اور مشہور اعتراض لازم آتا ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ جب حیثیت کو قید بنا ئیں گے تو قید کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ان اعراض ذاتیہ سے بحث ہوگی جو حیثیت کے واسطہ سے موضوع کو لاحق ہوں تو اس سے لازم آئیگا کہ علم طب میں خود صحت و مرض سے بحث صحیح نہیں ہونی چاہیے اسی طرح علم طبعی میں حرکت و سکون سے اور علم ہیئت میں خود شکل سے بحث نہیں ہونی چاہیے اس لئے کہ اس سے تقدم الشئی علی نفسہ کی خرابی لازم آتی ہے کیونکہ جب قید ہونے کا معنی یہی ہے کہ علم میں ان عوارض ذاتیہ سے بحث ہوگی جو شئی کو لاحق ہوتے ہیں حیثیت کے واسطہ سے پس اعراض ذاتیہ ذوالواسطہ اور حیثیت واسطہ ہوگی اور ضابطہ ہے کہ واسطہ مقدم ہوتا ہے اور ذو الواسطہ موخر ہوتا ہے تو تقدم الشئی علی نفسہ لازم آئیگا اور یہ باطل ہے جیسا کہ اگر علم طب میں بحث ہو صحت اور مرض سے تو صحت اور مرض عوارض ذاتیہ میں سے بن جائیں گے اور اعراض ذاتیہ یہ ذوالواسطہ ہے کیونکہ یہ بدن کو لاحق ہوں گے صحت اور مرض کے واسطہ سے لہذا صحت اور مرض ذوالواسطہ ہونے کی وجہ سے موخر اور واسطہ ہونے کے اعتبار سے مقدم ہوں گے تو یہی تقدم العنی علی نفسہ ہے اسی طرح علم ہیئت میں اگر شکل سے بحث ہو تو شکل اعراض ذاتیہ میں سے بن جائیگی اور اعراض ذاتیہ ذو الواسطہ ہے کیونکہ یہ جسم کو لاحق ہوں گے شکل کے واسطہ سے تو شکل ذو الواسطہ کے لحاظ سے موخر اور واسطہ کے لحاظ سے مقدم یہی تقدم الشئی علی نفسہ ہے اسی طرح علم طبعی میں اگر حرکت اور سکون سے بحث ہو تو یہ حرکت اور سکون اعراض ذاتی یہ میں سے ہوں گے اور باقی عوارض ذاتیہ ذوالواسطہ ہیں کیونکہ یہ اجسام کو لاحق ہوں گے حرکت اور سکرن کے واسطہ سے اب حرکت
Yes, a famous objection occurs, which is that it is necessary that the aspect (haythiyyah) not be among the attributes investigated in the science, necessarily because it is not among those that attach to the subject from its own perspective; otherwise, it would require the priority of a thing over itself, necessarily because that by which a thing attaches to another thing must precede the attribute. For example, health and sickness are not among those that attach to the human body from the perspective of it being healthy or sick, nor are motion and rest among those that attach to the body from the perspective of it moving or being still. The famous answer to this is that what is intended is the potential for health and sickness and motion and rest, and the preparedness for that. This is not among the attributes investigated in the science. The verified position is that since the subject is defined as that which is investigated in the science regarding its essential attributes, it is qualified by the aspect (haythiyyah) meaning that the investigation of attributes is with consideration of the aspect and by looking to it, i.e., this universal meaning is observed in all investigations, not meaning that all the investigated attributes attach to the subject through this aspect exactly. Regarding making the aspect a restriction: does it not necessitate the priority of a thing over itself? Yes: the commentator said that when we make the aspect a restriction, this previous objection does not arise, but another famous objection arises: if we make the aspect a restriction, its meaning is that only those essential attributes that attach to the subject through the aspect are investigated. This would entail that in medicine, health and sickness themselves should not be investigated; similarly in physics, motion and rest; and in astronomy, shape itself should not be investigated, because that would lead to the problem of priority of a thing over itself. Since the essential attributes are mediated by the aspect, the aspect would precede and the mediated would follow, leading to priority of the thing over itself, which is false. For example, if medicine investigates health and sickness, they become essential attributes, and essential attributes are mediated (they attach to the body through health and sickness), so health and sickness would both be mediated (as attributes) and mediators (as aspects), leading to priority of a thing over itself.
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of a fundamental problem in the definition of a science: the role of the 'aspect' (haythiyyah). The text first presents the famous objection: if the haythiyyah is treated as an attribute investigated in the science, it leads to circularity because the attribute and the aspect would be the same. For example, in medicine, health and sickness are investigated, but they attach to the body from the perspective of the body being healthy or sick; the perspective (haythiyyah) is not an independent attribute. The answer clarifies that the haythiyyah refers to potential (imkan) and preparedness (isti'dad), not actual attributes. The verified position (al-tahqiq) states that the subject of a science is defined by investigating its essential attributes from a specific aspect, and this aspect is a universal meaning considered in all investigations, not that every attribute attaches through that aspect. The text then addresses a further objection: if the haythiyyah is made a restrictive condition (qayd), it would prevent investigating the very attributes that define the science, e.g., health and sickness in medicine, because they would be both the attribute and the mediator. The commentator explains that this objection is avoided by understanding that the haythiyyah is not a separate mediator but the very perspective of investigation.

Key Terms
الحيثية (al-haythiyyah): The aspect or perspective from which the subject of a science is considered, qualifying the investigation of its attributes.
تقدم الشئ على نفسه (taqaddum al-shay' 'ala nafsih): Logical priority of a thing over itself, considered an impossibility in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the 'verified position' (al-tahqiq) state regarding the haythiyyah in defining a science?
A) The haythiyyah is an attribute investigated in the science.
B) The haythiyyah is a universal meaning considered in all investigations, not a mediator for every attribute.
C) The haythiyyah restricts the investigation to only potential attributes.
D) The haythiyyah is the same as the subject itself.

Key Takeaway
The haythiyyah in a science's definition is not an attribute but a universal perspective that frames the investigation of essential attributes, thereby avoiding logical circularity.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

8 min
The Hanafi Position: One Entity as Subject of Multiple Sciences
Rational proof of the diversity of essential attributes in a single entity, using Allah as the prime example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether a single entity can be the subject of multiple sciences and explain the rational proof based on the diversity of essential attributes (ʿaraḍ dhātiyya) of Allah.

Core Idea
A single thing can be the subject of many sciences if it has diverse essential attributes.

This lesson presents a foundational principle in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: the possibility of one thing serving as the subject (mawḍūʿ) for multiple sciences. The majority (al-jumhūr) reject this, insisting each science needs a unique subject. The Hanafi school, following the author of al-Tawḍīḥ, affirms it is possible and actually occurs. The proof hinges on the concept of essential attributes—properties that inhere in a thing per se. Through a rational analysis of Allah’s attributes, the commentator shows that even the absolutely simple Being has multiple essential attributes. If this is true for Allah, it is a fortiori true for created things, allowing a single entity to be studied from different perspectives in different sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two claims
The author makes two claims: (1) it is possible for one thing to be the subject of multiple sciences; (2) this actually occurs in reality. Understand the difference between possibility and actuality.
The proof focuses on the first claim.
2
Analyze the proof of possibility
The possibility is established by showing that a single entity can have different types of essential attributes (ʿaraḍ dhātiyya). If it can have multiple essential attributes, then each type can be studied in a different science.
Essential attributes are predicates that belong to the essence without mediation.
3
Examine the example of Allah's attributes
Allah (al-wāḥid al-ḥaqīqī) is absolutely simple yet possesses four categories of attributes: real (ḥaqīqiyya), relational (iḍāfiyya), privative (salbiyya), and affirmative (wujūdiyya). Each category contains subtypes.
Real attributes like life; relational like knowledge; privative like 'not a substance'; affirmative like 'Provider'.
4
Follow the argument against mediation
The commentator argues that essential attributes must attach to Allah without any mediator, otherwise infinite regress (tasalsul) would occur, which is false. Therefore, these attributes are essential—they belong to the essence per se.
This establishes diversity of essential attributes in a single simple being.
5
Conclude by priority (awlawiyya)
If Allah, the simplest being, has multiple essential attributes, then created beings (which are composite and less simple) can also have multiple essential attributes. Thus, it is possible for any one thing to be the subject of multiple sciences.
This is a rational argument (dalīl ʿaqlī).

کیا ایک چیز دو علوم کا موضوع بن سکتی ہے
تشریح:۔ یہاں سے ماتن نے تیسری بحث موضوع کے متعلق بیان کی ہے کہ ایک شئی دو چیزوں کا موضوع ہو سکتی ہے یا نہیں جمہور کہتے ہیں کہ نہیں ہو سکتی مصنف نے فرمایا کہ ممکن ہے بلکہ واقع ہے اب مصنف نے دو دعوے کیے ہیں (۱) یہ کہ ایک شئی کا کئی علوم کیلئے موضوع بنا ممکن ہے (۲) دوسرا دعوی کہ یہ ایسا واقع ہے اور نفس الامر میں ثابت ہے کہ ایک شئی دوعلموں کا موضوع بن رہی ہے اب پہلے دعوی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ایسا ہو سکتا ہے کہ ایک شئی کے عوارض ذاتیہ کی مختلف انواع ہوں تو ایک نوع سے ایک علم میں بحث ہو اور دوسری نوع سے دوسرے علم میں بحث ہو فلمہ ایسا ہو سکتا ہے کہ مئی واحدد و علموں کا موضوع ہو اب اس بات کی دلیل کہ شئی واحد کے عوارض ذاتیہ کی مختلف انواع ہوں دلیل یہ ہے کہ واحد حقیقی یعنی باری تعالی کے عوارض ذاتیہ کی مختلف انواع ہیں کیونکہ باری تعالی کے صفات چار قسم پر ہیں صفات حقیقیہ جیسے حیات وغیرہ اور صفات اضافیہ اور تصور میں تحقق تو غیر پر موقوف نہ ہو البتہ محقق فی الخارج غیر پر موقوف ہو مثلا واجب الوجود ہونا یہ تصور اور تعقل میں غیر کی محتاج نہیں ہے البتہ تحق في الخارج میں فرق کی محتاج ہے اور صفات سلبیہ وہ صفات باری تعالی کو بلا واسطہ لاحق ہیں یا بالواسطہ اگر یہ صفات بلا واسطہ لاحق ہوں تو ہمارا مدعی ثابت ہو گیا کہ یہ عوارض ذاتیہ ہیں اور اگر یہ صفات بالواسطہ لاحق ہوں تو ہم پوچھتے ہیں کہ واسطہ باری تعالے کا جز ہوگا یا غیر ہو گا جز واسطہ نہیں بن سکتا کیونکہ باری تعالی تو بسیط محض ہیں اس سے باری تعالی کا مرکب ہونا لازم آئیگا اور اگر غیر جز واسطہ ہے تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں یا تو دوسری صفت واسطہ ہوگی یا امر مباین واسطہ ہوگا اب اگر واسطہ امر مباین ہو تو یہ بھی درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں اللہ تعالی کا اپنی صفات میں استعمال من الغیر لازم آئیگا اور میں تلزم ہے احتیاج الی الغیر کو اور احتیاج الی الغیر مستلزم ہے حدوث اور ممکن ہونے کو اور یہ باطل ہے اور اگر واسطہ کوئی صفت ہو تو پھر ہم اس کے بارے میں ایسے ہی بحث کریں گے کہ اگر وہ صفت باری تعالی کو بلا واسطہ لاحق ہے تو وہ عوارض ذاتیہ میں سے ہوگی اگر بالواسطہ لاحق ہوں تو دو حال سے خالی واسطہ امر مباین ہوگا یا کوئی اور صفت ہو گی یہ سلسلہ چلتا رہے گا تو یہ ستلزم تسلسل ہے جو کہ باطل ہے اب لا محالہ کہنا ہو گا کہ وہ صفت بلا واسطہ کے عارض ہے باری تعالی کو اور یہی ہمارا مدعی ہے اب ایسے ہی صفات اضافیہ کے بارے میں بحث کریں گے جیسے صفات حقیقیہ کے بارے میں بحث کی ہے تو یہ بھی باری تعالی کو بالذات لاحق ہونگی اب جب باری تعالی جو واحد حقیقی ہے اس کے عوارض ذاتیہ کے مختلف انواع ممکن ہیں تو مخلوق کیلئے عوارض ذاتیہ کی مختلف انواع بطریق اولی ممکن ہونگی۔

سوال :۔ یہ کہ علوم کا امتیاز تو موضوع سے ہوتا ہے جب دونوں کا موضوع شئی واحد ہے تو پھر امتیاز کیسے ہوگا ؟ جواب :۔ علوم کا اتحاد و اختلاف منی ہے مسائل کے اتحاد و اختلاف پر یعنی اگر مسائل متحد ہوں تو علوم بھی متحد ہوں گے اور اگر مسائل مختلف ہوں گے تو علوم بھی مختلف ہوں گے اور مسائل کا اتحاد و اختلاف جیسے قضیہ کے موضوع سے ثابت ہوتا ہے ایسے ہی محمول سے بھی ثابت ہوتا ہے اور قضیہ کا معمول عوارض ذاتیہ ہیں تو علموں کا امتیاز عوارض ذاتیہ سے ہوگا کہ ایک علم میں عوارض
Can one thing be the subject of two sciences? Explanation: Here the author (matn) has explained the third discussion regarding the subject: whether one thing can be the subject of two things or not. The majority say it cannot. The author (musannif) said it is possible, rather it occurs. Now the author made two claims: (1) that one thing can be made the subject for several sciences is possible; (2) the second claim that this actually occurs and is established in reality that one thing is becoming the subject of two sciences. Now the proof of the first claim is that it is possible that a single thing has different types of essential attributes (arad dhatiyya). Then one type is discussed in one science and another type in another science. Therefore, it is possible that a single thing is the subject of two sciences. Now the proof that a single thing has different types of essential attributes: the proof is that the Real One (Al-Wahid Al-Haqiqi), i.e., Allah Almighty, has different types of essential attributes. Because the attributes of Allah Almighty are of four types: real attributes (sifat haqiqiyya) like life etc., and relative attributes (sifat idafiyya) like knowledge and creation etc. Then each has two types: existential (wujudi) and privative (salbi). Real attributes are those that in their conceptualization and in their external existence do not need another. Relative attributes are those whose conceptualization does not depend on another, but their external existence depends on another; for example, being necessary of existence—this does not need another in conceptualization, but in external existence it needs a distinction. Privative attributes are those that are negated, like Allah Almighty not being a substance, not being an accident. Affirmative attributes are those that are affirmed for Allah Almighty, like being the Owner, being the Provider. Now we discuss regarding the real attributes: whether these attributes attach to Allah without mediation or with mediation. If these attributes attach without mediation, our claim is proven—that they are essential attributes. And if they attach with mediation, we ask: Is the mediator a part of Allah or something other? A part cannot be a mediator because Allah is pure simplicity; this would necessitate composition of Allah. And if the mediator is other than a part, then it is either another attribute or a disparate thing. If the mediator is a disparate thing, then that is not correct either, because in that case Allah's use of something other than Him would be necessary, which entails need of another, and need of another entails contingency and possibility, and that is false. And if the mediator is some attribute, then we will discuss regarding it in the same manner: if that attribute attaches to Allah without mediation, then it is among the essential attributes; if it attaches with mediation, then the mediator is either a disparate thing or another attribute. This chain will continue, and it necessitates infinite regress (tasalsul), which is false. So inevitably it must be said that the attribute attaches to Allah without mediation, and this is our claim. Now similarly we will discuss regarding relative attributes as we discussed regarding real attributes; so they also will attach to Allah per se (bi al-dhat). Now when the Real One, who is the true unitary, has different types of essential attributes possible for Him, then for created beings, different types of essential attributes are possible by way of priority (bi tariq al-awla). If the subject of two sciences is one, how will distinction between them occur? 'Wa yakun' is the answer to an implicit question. Question: The distinction of sciences occurs through their subject; when the subject of both is one thing, then how will distinction occur? Answer: The unity and difference of sciences depend on the unity and difference of their problems (masa'il). If the problems are unified, the sciences will also be unified; if the problems are different, the sciences will also be different. And the unity and difference of problems is established just as through the subject of a proposition, similarly through the predicate. And the predicate of a proposition consists of essential attributes. So the distinction of sciences occurs through essential attributes: that in one science these attributes
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Al-Tawdih by Sadr al-Shariah. It addresses whether one thing can serve as the subject (mawdu) of multiple sciences. The commentator first presents the view of the majority (al-jumhur) who say it is not possible, then defends the author's (al-musannif) position that it is possible and actually occurs. The proof is based on the diversity of essential attributes (al-arad al-dhatiyya) that a single entity can have. To demonstrate this, the commentator uses the example of Allah, the Real One (al-wahid al-haqiqi), whose attributes are classified into four types: real (haqiqiyya), relative (idafiyya), existential (wujudi), and privative (salbi). Through a logical argument, he shows that these attributes must attach to Allah without mediation, thus they are essential attributes (arad dhatiyya). If even Allah, who is absolutely simple, can have multiple essential attributes, then created beings can have multiple such attributes by priority (bi tariq al-awla). The passage then answers a possible objection: if two sciences share the same subject, how are they distinguished? The answer is that sciences are distinguished by their problems (masa'il), which are propositions composed of a subject and a predicate. The predicate consists of essential attributes. Thus, even if the subject is the same, different essential attributes studied in each science differentiate them. This is a fundamental principle in Hanafi usul al-fiqh that allows a single entity to be studied from multiple perspectives in different sciences.

Key Terms
عوارض ذاتیہ ('arad dhatiyya): Essential attributes that attach to a thing per se without mediation.
موضوع (mawdu'): The subject of a science; the entity whose essential attributes are studied.
واحد حقیقی (al-wahid al-haqiqi): The absolutely simple and unitary existent, i.e., Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the core premise used to prove that one thing can have diverse essential attributes?
A) The attributes of angels are also diverse.
B) Allah, the absolutely simple, has multiple distinct essential attributes.
C) The Quran states that everything has multiple attributes.
D) Human beings are composite and thus have multiple attributes.

Key Takeaway
A single entity can be the subject of multiple sciences because it can have diverse essential attributes, as demonstrated by the diversity of Allah's attributes despite His absolute simplicity.

Distinguishing Sciences: The Role of Essential Attributes
Answer to the objection: sciences are distinguished by their problems (masāʾil), whose predicates are essential attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how two sciences that share the same subject are distinguished by their essential attributes (ʿaraḍ dhātiyya) rather than by their subject alone.

Core Idea
Sciences are distinguished by their predicates (essential attributes), not merely by their subjects.

In the previous lesson, we established that one thing can be the subject of multiple sciences. But this raises an important objection: if two sciences share the same subject, how can they be distinguished? This lesson presents the Hanafi answer. The commentator clarifies that sciences are not differentiated by their subjects alone, but by their problems (masāʾil), which are propositions consisting of a subject and a predicate. The predicates are the essential attributes of that subject. Therefore, even if the subject is the same, different sets of essential attributes give rise to different sciences. This principle is crucial for understanding the classification of knowledge in the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Formulate the objection
The objector asks: if two sciences have the same subject (mawḍūʿ), how can they be distinguished? Distinguishing sciences by subject seems to imply that a shared subject would collapse them into one.
This objection arises naturally from the majority view that sciences are defined by their subjects.
2
Understand the Hanafi response
The commentator answers that the unity or difference of sciences depends on the unity or difference of their problems (masāʾil), i.e., the propositions studied. Each proposition has a subject and a predicate.
Masāʾil are the specific questions or propositions that constitute a science.
3
Identify the role of predicates
The predicates of these propositions are the essential attributes (ʿaraḍ dhātiyya). Even if the subject is the same, different predicates define different sciences.
For instance, the predicate 'purifying' belongs to fiqh, while the predicate 'composed of H2O' belongs to physics.
4
Apply the principle to a fiqh example
Consider water: in fiqh, the essential attribute studied is its property of being ṭāhir (pure) and muṭahhir (purifying). In physics, the essential attribute is its chemical structure. Both are essential attributes of water, but they belong to different sciences.
This shows how the same subject yields distinct sciences.

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Al-Tawdih by Sadr al-Shariah. It addresses whether one thing can serve as the subject (mawdu) of multiple sciences. The commentator first presents the view of the majority (al-jumhur) who say it is not possible, then defends the author's (al-musannif) position that it is possible and actually occurs. Key Terms
مسائل (masāʾil): The problems or propositions of a science; they consist of a subject and a predicate.
قضیہ (qaḍiyya): A proposition or statement that forms a unit of scientific knowledge.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate

Distinguishing Sciences: Predicates Alone Cannot Suffice
Refutation of predicate-based science distinction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that sciences are distinguished by their subjects, and evaluate the objection that predicates alone could serve as a criterion.

Core Idea
Sciences are distinguished by their subjects, not by their predicates.

In this passage, the commentator responds to a claim that sciences can be differentiated by their predicates (mahmulat) alone. The Hanafi school insists that the subject (mawdu') is the only stable criterion; otherwise, fiqh would splinter into countless sub-sciences based on each ruling type. This lesson unpacks the logical argument and the practical implications for organizing Islamic legal knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objection
The author of al-Tawdih reportedly argued that sciences can be distinguished by their predicates. Pinpoint the exact claim as stated in the passage: 'distinction of sciences is also based on predicates.'
This is the view the commentator aims to refute.
2
Understand the Hanafi Refutation
The commentator gives several reasons. The first reason: when scholars study external existents, they first determine the genera and species of realities, then their essential accidents (arad dhatiya). This yields many issues (masa'il) that are united in subject but differ in predicates. Hence, relying on predicates would not provide a unique distinction.
Focus on the logical structure: Subject is known and fixed; predicates are diverse and sought.
3
Apply the Principle to Fiqh
If predicates were the basis, then the act of the obligated person (fi'l al-mukallaf) would be the subject of many sciences—one for obligation, one for prohibition, etc. But fiqh is a single science. Thus, the predicate-based criterion fails.
This shows the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).
4
Distinguish Aspects (Haythiyyat)
The earlier objection about aspects (haythiyya) is addressed: aspects like 'from the perspective of form' or 'from the perspective of nature' are either explanatory (bayaniyya) and not truly distinguishing, or they are restrictive qualifications (qayd) that make the subjects different by consideration. Either way, the principle that sciences are distinguished by subjects is preserved.
This refines the understanding of how a single external object can belong to multiple sciences without violating the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لِلعِلمِ الْوَاحِدِ إلَّا أن يُوضَعَ شَيْءٍ أَوْ أَشْيَاء مُتَنَاسِبَةٌ فَنَبْحَثَ عَنْ جَمِيعِ عَوَارِضِهِ الذَّاتِيَّةِ وَنَطْلُبَهَا وَلَا مَعْنَى لِتَمَايُزِ الْعُلُومِ إِلَّا أَنَّ هَذَا يَنظُرُ فِي أَحْوَالِ شَيْءٍ وَذَاكَ فِي أَخْوَالِ شَيْءٍ آخَرَ مُغَابِرَ لَهُ بِالذَّاتِ أَوْ بِالِاعْتِبَارِ بِأَنْ يُؤْخَذَ فِي أَحَدِ الْعِلْمَيْنِ مُطْلَقًا ، وَفِي الْآخَرِ مُقَيْدًا أَوْ يُؤخَذَ فِي كُلِّ مِنْهُمَا مُقَيَّدًا بِقَيْدٍ آخَرَ وَتِلْكَ الأَحْوَالُ مَجْهُولَةٌ مَطْلُوبَةٌ وَالْمَوْضُوعُ مَعْلُومٌ بَيْنَ الْوُجُودِ فَهُوَ الصَّالِحُ سَبَبًا لِلسَّمَائِزِ . وَأَمَّا ثَالِثًا فَلَانَّهُ مَا مِنْ عِلْمٍ إِلَّا وَيَشْتَمِلُ مَوْضُوعُهُ عَلَى أَعْرَاضٍ ذَاتِيَّةٍ مُتَنَوِّعَةٍ فَلِكُلّ أَحَدٍ أَنْ يَجْعَلَهُ عُلُومًا مُتَعَدِّدَةً بِهَذَا الاعْتِبَارِ مَثَلًا يَجْعَلُ الْبَحْث عَنْ فِعل المُكَلَّفِ مِنْ حَيْثُ الوُجُوبُ عِلْمًا وَمِنْ حَيْثُ الْحُرُمَةِ عِلْمًا آخَرَ إِلَى غَيْرِ ذَلِكَ فَيَكُونُ الْفِقْهُ عُلُومًا مُتَعَدِّدَةً مَوْضُوعُهَا فِعْلُ الْمُكَلَّفِ فَلَا يَنْضَبِطُ الاتِّحَادُ وَالاخْتِلافُ وَتَحْقِيقُ هَذِهِ الْمَبَاحِثِ فِي كِتَاب الْبُرُهَان مِنْ مَنطِقِ الشَّفَاء ..
ترجمہ: اور یہاں نظر ہے بہر حال اولا کیونکہ مبنی ہے اس پر جس کو ذکر کیا ہے کہ ہوتی ہے حیثیت کبھی جز موضوع کا اور کبھی بیان مجوث عنہا کا اور تحقیق تو نے پہچان لیا اس کو جو اس میں (خرابی) ہے بہر حال ثانیا کیونکہ جب وہ ارادہ کرتے ہیں اعیان موجودات کے احوال کی معرفت کا تو وہ وضع کرتے ہیں حقیقتوں کیلئے انواع اور جنسیں اور بحث کرتے ہیں اس سے جس کے ذریعے وہ احاطہ کر لیں اس کے اعراض ذاتیہ کا پس حاصل ہوتے ہیں ان کو ایسے مسائل کثیرہ جو متحد ہوتے ہیں ان کے بحث ہونے میں اس موضوع سے اگر چہ مختلف ہوں ان (مسائل) کے معمولات پر بناتے ہیں وہ اس اعتبار سے ایک علم منفرد کرتے ہیں مدون کرنے میں اور نام رکھنے میں اور جائز قرار دیتے ہیں ہر ایک کیلئے کہ نسبت کر دے وہ اس کی طرف اس چیز کی جس پر مطلع ہو وہ اس موضوع کے احوال میں سے کیونکہ معتبر علم میں وہ بحث کرتا ہے تمام ان چیزوں سے جن کا طاقت انسانی احاطہ کر سکتی ہے موضوع کے اعراض ذاتیہ میں سے پس نہیں ہے معنی علم واحد کا مگر یہ کہ وضع کیا جائے ایک شئی کو یا کئی اشیاء کو جو متناسب ہوں پس بحث کی جائے اس کی تمام عوارض ذاتیہ سے اور طلب کیا جائے ان کو اور نہیں ہے معنی تمایز علوم کا مگر یہی کہ نظر کی جائے ایک شئی کے احوال میں اور وہ دوسری شئی کے احوال میں مغایر ہو اس کے بالذات یا بالاعتبار بایں طور پر کہ
لیا جائے دو علموں میں سے ایک میں مطلق اور دوسرے میں مقید یا لیا جائے ان دو میں سے ہر ایک میں مقید قید آخر کے ساتھ اور وہ احوال مجہول ہیں مطلوب ہیں اور موضوع معلوم ہے وجود کے درمیان پس وہ (موضوع) صلاحیت رکھتا ہے تمایز کے سبب بننے کا اور بہر حال ثالثا کیونکہ نہیں ہے کوئی علم مگر مشتمل ہوتا ہے اس کا موضوع مختلف اعراض ذاتیہ پر پس ہر ایک کو اجازت ہوگی یہ کہ بنادے وہ اس کو علوم متعددہ اس اعتبار سے مثال کے طور پر بنا دیا جائے فعل مکلف سے بحث کرنے کو من حیث الوجوب ایک علم اور من حیث الحرمت دوسرا علم اس کے علاوہ تک پس ہو جائے گی فقہ متعددہ علوم اس کا موضوع فعل مکلف ہوگا پس نہیں منضبط ہو گا اتحاد اور اختلاف اور تحقیق ان کی مباحث کی کتاب البرہان میں ہے فن منطق کی شفاء نامی کتاب میں۔

وہنا نظر :۔ یہاں سے شارع نے تین اعتراضات کئے ہیں۔
اعتراض اول:۔ کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ صاحب توضیح نے شئی واحد کے علوم متعددہ کیلئے موضوع بنے کیلئے دلیل بیان کی ہے کہ حکما نے تصریح کی ہے کہ علم ہیئت کا موضوع اجسام عالم میں من حیث الشکل اور علم السماء والعالم کا موضوع بھی یہی اجسام عالم ہیں من حیث الطبیعت اب اس میں شئی واحد دو علموں کا موضوع بن رہی ہے کیونکہ حیثیت بیانیہ ہے اور یہ موضوع سے خارج ہے تو اس پر شاریخ سوال کر رہے ہیں کہ یہ حیثیت بیانیہ نہیں ہے بلکہ قید ہے گویا من حیث الشکل اور من حیث الطبیعت یہ موضوع کیلئے قید ہیں لہذا اب موضوع مختلف قیودات کے ساتھ مقید ہونے کی وجہ سے اعتبارا مغایر ہوں گے لہذا اس تغایر اعتباری کی وجہ سے شئی واحد علوم متعددہ کا موضوع نہیں بن سکتی۔
جواب:- جواب یہ ہے کہ آپ نے حیثیت کو قید بنا کر اس کا جو معنی بیان کیا ہے وہ معنی حیثیت بیانیہ کی طرف لوٹ جاتا ہے کما مر کیا علوم میں تمایز کامدار محمولات پر رکھا جا سکتا ہے؟
اعتراض ثانی:۔ کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ صاحب توضیح نے کہا ہے کہ علوم میں تمایز کامد الحمولات پر بھی ہے اس پر شاریخ اعتراض کر رہے ہیں کہ علوم میں تمایز کامدار حمولات پر رکھنا صحیح نہیں ہے اور اس کی کئی وجوہ ہیں۔
پہلی وجہ : فلانہم سے بیان کی ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ حکماء نے جب اعیان یعنی موجودات خارجیہ کے احوال معلوم کرنے کا ارادہ کیا تو انہوں نے حقائق یعنی اعیان کی اجناس اور انواع کو متعین کیا پھر اس کے بعد ان کے عوارض ذاتیہ کو ثابت کیا اس سے حکماء کو مسائل کثیرہ حاصل ہوئے اور یہ مسائل کثیر ہ ایسے ہیں جو بحسب الموضوعات متحد ہیں البتہ بحسب الحمولات
For a single science, it is only that a thing or proportionate things are posited, then we investigate all of its essential accidents and seek them. There is no meaning to the distinction of sciences except that this [science] looks at the states of a thing and that [science] looks at the states of another thing which is different from it in essence or by consideration, such that it is taken in one of the two sciences absolutely and in the other qualified, or taken in each of them qualified with a different qualification. Those states are unknown and sought, while the subject is known among existence, so it is suitable to be a cause for distinction. Thirdly, there is no science except that its subject includes diverse essential accidents, so anyone can make it multiple sciences by this consideration. For example, he makes the investigation of the act of the obligated person from the perspective of obligation a science, and from the perspective of prohibition another science, and so on. Then fiqh would be multiple sciences whose subject is the act of the obligated person, so unity and diversity would not be regulated. The verification of these discussions is in the book Al-Burhan from the logic of Al-Shifa. Translation: And here is a consideration, firstly because it is based on what was mentioned that the aspect (haythiyya) is sometimes part of the subject and sometimes a statement about what is discussed... [Urdu continues]... Here the commentator raises three objections. First objection: Its summary is that the author of Al-Tawdih gave evidence that a single thing can be the subject of multiple sciences, saying that the scholars stated that the subject of astronomy is the bodies of the universe from the perspective of form and the subject of the science of the heavens and the world is also these bodies but from the perspective of nature. Now a single thing becomes the subject of two sciences because the aspect is explanatory (bayaniyya) and it is external to the subject. So the commentators question that this aspect is not explanatory but rather a qualification (qayd), meaning that 'from the perspective of form' and 'from the perspective of nature' are qualifications for the subject. Therefore, the subjects, being qualified by different qualifications, are different by consideration, so a single thing cannot be the subject of multiple sciences due to this difference by consideration. Answer: The answer is that when you made the aspect a qualification, the meaning you expressed returns to the meaning of the explanatory aspect, as previously mentioned. Can the distinction of sciences be based on predicates? Second objection: Its summary is that the author of Al-Tawdih said that the distinction of sciences is also based on predicates. The commentators object that basing the distinction of sciences on predicates is not correct, and there are several reasons for this. First reason: It is explained from 'fa-lanahum' that when the scholars intended to know the states of external existents, they determined the genera and species of the realities, then they established their essential accidents. From this, the scholars obtained numerous issues, and these numerous issues are united with respect to subjects, but diverse with respect to predicates.
Source pages p. 416

Commentary
This passage is a continuation of the commentary on al-Tawdih regarding the distinction of sciences (tamayyuz al-'ulum). The author begins by restating the principle that a science is defined by its subject (mawdu') and its essential accidents (arad dhatiyya). The distinction between sciences is based on the subjects being different either in essence or by consideration (e.g., absolute vs. qualified). The author then argues that if we considered different essential accidents of the same subject as separate sciences, then fiqh (whose subject is the act of the obligated person) would fragment into countless sciences based on different rulings (obligation, prohibition, etc.), which is not how scholarship is organized. The author cites Avicenna's Kitab al-Burhan for further detail. The Urdu translation/commentary then introduces three objections by the commentator (the sharh) to the positions of the author of Al-Tawdih. The first objection concerns the aspect (haythiyya): whether it is a mere explanatory qualification (bayaniyya) or a genuine restrictive qualification (qayd). The commentator argues that if it is a qayd, then the subjects become different by consideration, so a single thing cannot be the subject of multiple sciences. The answer is that the supposed qayd reduces to a bayani meaning. The second objection questions whether distinction can be based on predicates (mahmulat). The commentator argues that predicates alone cannot distinguish sciences because multiple sciences can share the same subject and their issues (masa'il) are united in subject but diverse in predicates; thus, relying on predicates would not provide a stable criterion. This second objection is detailed with several reasons, the first of which is given here: when scholars investigate external existents, they first determine the genera and species of realities, then their essential accidents. This yields many issues that are united in subject but differ in predicates, so distinction by predicates is not valid.

Key Terms
موضوع (mawḍūʿ): The subject matter of a science; that which is investigated in terms of its essential accidents.
عرض ذاتي (ʿaraḍ dhātī): Essential accident; a property that is necessary and non-separable from the subject, such as the possibility of being obligated for the act.
حیثیت (haythiyya): Aspect or perspective; the angle from which a subject is considered in a science. It may be either explanatory (bayaniyya) or a restrictive qualification (qayd).
محمول (maḥmūl): Predicate; a property or ruling attributed to the subject. In this context, it refers to the diversity of rulings (e.g., wajib, haram) that could potentially create separate sciences if used as a criterion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the Hanafi position reject predicates as the basis for distinguishing sciences?
A) Because predicates are multiple for the same subject, leading to infinite fragmentation.
B) Because predicates are not essential accidents of the subject.
C) Because the subject is unknown, while predicates are known.
D) Because the opposing view is based on a misunderstanding of the subject.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that sciences are distinguished by their subjects (mawdu'), not by their predicates (mahmulat), ensuring the unity and systematic organization of knowledge like fiqh.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
12 min
The Basmalah as Part of the Quran: Hanafi Usul Dispute
Usul dispute: status of basmalah as Quranic verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the basmalah's status in the Quran, identify the two proofs, and explain the objections and their responses.

Core Idea
The basmalah is one verse from the Quran, repeated for separation and blessing — the later Hanafi position.

This passage addresses a classic usul dispute: is the basmalah (Bismillah) at the start of surahs part of the Quran? Early Hanafis held it is not, while later Hanafis adopted the view that it is one verse repeated. The Shafi'is consider each basmalah a separate verse. The commentator presents proofs and answers objections, clarifying the Hanafi position and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their positions
List the three positions: early Hanafis (famous view of Abu Hanifa), later Hanafis (correct view), and Shafi'is. State what each holds about the basmalah.
Early Hanafis say it is not Quran; later Hanafis say it is one repeated verse; Shafi'is say each basmalah is a separate verse.
2
Examine the Hanafi proofs
Identify the two dalils: (1) Writing in Quranic script without Salafi objection. (2) Hadith: 'It is sent down from Allah'. Analyze the wajh al-dalalah for each.
The script proof relies on silence of the Salaf; the hadith indicates revelation implies Quranicity.
3
Analyze the objections and responses
Three objections: prayer not valid with only basmalah, permissibility for junub to recite, and non-declaration of disbelief for denier. For each, state the objection and the Hanafi answer.
Answers center on doubt (shakk), permissibility for blessing (tabarruk), and obscurity due to Imam Malik's disagreement.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical differences between Hanafi and Shafi'i: recitation aloud in prayer, permissibility for junub to recite basmalah, and the number of verses.
Hanafis do not require basmalah aloud; Shafi'is do. Hanafis allow junub to recite basmalah for blessing.
5
Summarize the tarjih
The later Hanafi view (basmalah is part of the Quran) is the correct (sahih) and relied-upon (mu'tamad) position. Explain why it prevails.
The text states 'sahih qawl' and this is adopted by the muta'akhkhirun.
