قاللفظ بالنسبۃ الی المعنی :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا چوتھا حصہ ہے یہاں سے شارعا تقسیمات اربعہ کی وجہ صر بیان کرتے ہیں اور ان سے برآمد شدہ اقسام کو ذکر کرتے ہیں۔
تقسیم اول: لفظ پہلی تقسیم کے اعتبار سے مخصر ہے چار قسموں میں یعنی خاص عام مشترک مؤول میں تقسیم اول یعنی لفظ کی وضع لاسی کے اعتبار سے تقسیم کی وجہ حصر یہ ہے کہ لفظ دو حال سے خالی نہیں ایک معنی کے لئے وضع کیا گیا ہوگا یا متعدد معانی کے لئے اگر ایک معنی کے لئے وضع ہو پھر دو حال سے خالی نہیں کہ ایک معنی فرد واحد میں منحصر ہوگا یا فرد واحد میں منحصر نہیں ہوگا اگر ایک معنی فرد واحد میں منحصر ہو تو یہ خاص ہے اور اگر ایک معنی فرد واحد میں منحصر نہ ہو بلکہ کئی افراد میں پایا جاتا ہو تو یہ عام ہے اور اگر وضع کئی معانی کے لئے ہو تو پھر دو حال سے خالی نہیں ایک معنی کو دوسرے معنی پر ترجیح حاصل ہوگی یا نہیں اگر ایک معنی کو دوسرے معنی پر ترجیح حاصل ہوگی تو موکول ہے اور اگر ترجیح حاصل نہ ہو تو مشترک ہوگا یہ تقسیم قوم کے اعتبار سے ہے وگر نہ مان بمع نے مؤول کو ذکر نہیں کیا بلکہ اس کی جگہ جمع منکر کو درج کیا۔
تقسیم ثانی:۔ استعمال کے اعتبار سے بھی لفظ کی چار میں ہیں حقیقت مجاز صریح کنا یہ وجہ حصر یہ ہے کہ لفظ دو حال سے خالی نہیں ہے معنی موضوع لہ میں استعمال ہوگا یا غیر موضوع لہ میں استعمال ہوگا اگر معنی موضوع لہ میں استعمال ہو تو حقیقت ورنہ مجاز پھر دونوں دو حال سے خالی نہیں ہیں اگر ان کا معنی ظاہر ہے تو صریح ورنہ کہنا یہ ہے۔
تقسیم ثالث : باعتبار ظہور وفاء کے لفظ کی آٹھ قسمیں ہیں ظاہر نص مسر محکم فی مشکل مجمل متشابہ وجہ حصر یہ ہے کہ لفظ دو حال سے خالی نہیں ہے لفظ کا معنی ظاہر ہوگا یا مخفی اگر لفظ کا معنیٰ ظاہر ہے تو تاویل کا احتمال رکھے گا یا نہیں اگر تاویل کا احتمال رکھے تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں کہ نفس صیغہ سے معنی سمجھ میں آجائے گا یا نفس صیغہ سے معنی سمجھ میں نہیں آئے گا اگر نفس صیغہ سے معنی سمجھ میں آجائے تو ظاہر ہے اگر نفس صیغہ سے معنی سمجھ میں نہ آئے تو نص ہے اگر تاویل کا احتمال نہ رکھے تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں نسخ کا احتمال رکھے گا یا نہیں اگر نسخ کا احتمال رکھتا ہو تو مفسر وگرنہ وہ محکم ہے اور اگر معنی مخفی ہو تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں کہ خفاء غیر کی وجہ سے آئے گا یا نفس صیغہ میں پایا جائے گا اگر تو یہ خفاء غیر کی وجہ سے ہے تو مخفی اور اگر نفس صیغہ سے خفا ہو تو دو حال
He said: 'The word in relation to the meaning': This is the fourth part of the commentary's wording. From here, the commentator explains the reason for the four divisions and mentions the categories derived from them. First division: The word in terms of the first division is limited to four types: khass, 'amm, mushtarak, mu'awwal. The first division, i.e., the division in terms of wad' of the word, the reason for its being limited is that the word is either posited for one meaning or for multiple meanings. If posited for one meaning, then either that meaning is restricted to a single individual or not restricted to a single individual. If the meaning is restricted to a single individual, it is khass; if the meaning is not restricted to a single individual but found in multiple individuals, it is 'amm. If posited for multiple meanings, then either one meaning has preference over another or not. If one meaning has preference, it is mu'awwal; if no preference, it is mushtarak. This division is according to the majority; but the Matn author did not mention mu'awwal; instead he put jamm' (plural) in its place. Second division: In terms of usage, the word also has four types: haqiqah, majaz, sarih, kinayah. The reason for its being limited is that the word is either used in its posited meaning (haqiqah) or in a non-posited meaning (majaz). Then both of these are either clear in meaning (sarih) or not (kinayah). Third division: In terms of clarity and obscurity, the word has eight types: zahir, nass, mufassar, muhkam, khafi, mushkil, mujmal, mutashabih. The reason for its being limited is that the word's meaning is either clear or obscure. If clear, then it either bears possibility of ta'wil or not. If it bears ta'wil, then either the meaning is understood from the word form itself (zahir) or not (nass). If it does not bear ta'wil, then either it bears possibility of naskh (mufassar) or not (muhkam). If the meaning is obscure, then either the obscurity comes from external factors (khafi) or from the word form itself (then it is either mushkil or further ...)
Source pages p. 491

Commentary
This passage is a commentary that enumerates the subcategories of the four divisions of lafz (word) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The commentator systematically explains each division. Under the first division (by wad'), lafz is classified as khass (specific), 'amm (general), mushtarak (homonym), or mu'awwal (interpreted). The reasoning is based on whether the word is posited for one or multiple meanings, and whether the meaning is restricted to one individual. Note: The matn (al-Tawdih) omits mu'awwal and instead includes jamm' (plural), a point the commentator mentions as a difference. Under the second division (by isti'mal), lafz is haqiqah (literal), majaz (figurative), sarih (explicit), or kinayah (implicit). This hinges on usage in the posited meaning and clarity. Under the third division (by zuhur wa khafa'), lafz is classified into eight categories: zahir (clear), nass (explicit), mufassar (detailed), muhkam (unequivocal), khafi (obscure due to external cause), mushkil (difficult), mujmal (ambiguous), and mutashabih (unclear). The reasoning involves a stepwise consideration of clarity, possibility of interpretation (ta'wil), possibility of abrogation (naskh), and source of obscurity. The passage ends incomplete, cutting off during the explanation of the obscure types.

Key Terms
خاص (khass): A word posited for a single specific meaning, restricted to one individual
عام ('amm): A word posited for a meaning that covers multiple individuals without restriction
مشترک (mushtarak): A word posited for multiple meanings with no preference between them
مؤول (mu'awwal): A word posited for multiple meanings but one meaning is preferred due to evidence
حقیقت (haqiqah): A word used in its originally posited meaning
مجاز (majaz): A word used in a meaning other than its posited meaning due to a connection
صریح (sarih): A word whose intended meaning is clear from the word itself
کنایہ (kinayah): A word whose intended meaning is not clear from the word alone, requiring context
ظاہر (zahir): A word whose meaning is clear from its form but bears possibility of interpretation (ta'wil)
نص (nass): A word whose meaning is clear from its form and does not bear ta'wil
مفسر (mufassar): A word whose meaning is clear and bears possibility of abrogation (naskh)
محکم (muhkam): A word whose meaning is clear and cannot be abrogated
خفی (khafi): A word whose meaning is obscure due to an external factor
مشکل (mushkil): A word whose meaning is obscure due to the word itself
مجمل (mujmal): A word whose meaning is ambiguous and requires clarification
متشابہ (mutashabih): A word whose meaning is unclear and cannot be determined

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the four divisions of lafz mentioned in the passage?
A) By wad' (coinage)
B) By isti'mal (usage)
C) By zuhur wa khafa' (clarity/obscurity)
D) By qiyas (analogy)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification of lafz into four perspectives provides a systematic method for determining the legal meaning of a word, each with subcategories based on clear criteria.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

The First Division of Words: Wad' (Coining)
Explaining the first division of words based on wad' (coining).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any given term as khas, 'amm, mushtarak, or mu'awwal by applying the first division's binary criteria.

Core Idea
Words are coined for one meaning or many; one splits into specific/general, many splits into interpreted/ambiguous.

The first division of words is based on their original coining (wad'). This foundational classification organizes all terms into four mutually exclusive categories. Understanding this division is essential for correctly interpreting legal texts, as each category carries different implications for generality and specificity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basis of division
Recognize that the division is based on wad' (coining) – what the word was originally placed to mean.
Do not confuse with later usage or clarity divisions.
2
Apply the first binary split
Determine whether the word was coined for a single meaning or for multiple meanings.
Any word falls into one of these two.
3
Classify single-meaning words
If coined for one meaning, decide if that meaning is confined to one individual instance (khas) or applies to multiple instances ('amm).
Proper names are khas; common nouns like 'man' are 'amm.
4
Classify multiple-meaning words
If coined for multiple meanings, check if one meaning is given preference (mu'awwal) or if all are equal (mushtarak).
Mu'awwal requires a contextual clue (qarinah) for preference; mushtarak has none.
5
Note the Hanafi position on mu'awwal
The Hanafi school includes mu'awwal in this division; some others replace it with 'jam' munkar' (undefined plural).
This reflects differences in usul methodology.

اللفظ سے ہے اس لئے یہ مقدم ہوگا پھر استعمال کا اعتبار ہوگا کیونکہ یہ مؤخر ہوتا ہے اس لحاظ سے دوسری تقسیم ظہور اور خفاء کے اعتبار سے ہوگی اور تیسری تقسیم استعمال کے اعتبار سے ہوگی۔
تقسیمات اربعہ کی وجہ حصر
قاللفظ بالنسبۃ الی المعنی :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا چوتھا حصہ ہے یہاں سے شارعا تقسیمات اربعہ کی وجہ صر بیان کرتے
ہیں اور ان سے برآمد شدہ اقسام کو ذکر کرتے ہیں۔
تقسیم اول: لفظ پہلی تقسیم کے اعتبار سے مخصر ہے چار قسموں میں یعنی خاص عام مشترک مؤول میں تقسیم اول یعنی لفظ کی وضع لاسی کے اعتبار سے تقسیم کی وجہ حصر یہ ہے کہ لفظ دو حال سے خالی نہیں ایک معنی کے لئے وضع کیا گیا ہوگا یا متعدد معانی کے لئے اگر ایک معنی کے لئے وضع ہو پھر دو حال سے خالی نہیں کہ ایک معنی فرد واحد میں منحصر ہوگا یا فرد واحد میں منحصر نہیں ہوگا اگر ایک معنی فرد واحد میں منحصر ہو تو یہ خاص ہے اور اگر ایک معنی فرد واحد میں منحصر نہ ہو بلکہ کئی افراد میں پایا جاتا ہو تو یہ عام ہے اور اگر وضع کئی معانی کے لئے ہو تو پھر دو حال سے خالی نہیں ایک معنی کو دوسرے معنی پر ترجیح حاصل ہوگی یا نہیں اگر ایک معنی کو دوسرے معنی پر ترجیح حاصل ہوگی تو موکول ہے اور اگر ترجیح حاصل نہ ہو تو مشترک ہوگا یہ تقسیم قوم کے اعتبار سے ہے وگر نہ مان بمع نے مؤول کو ذکر نہیں کیا بلکہ اس کی جگہ جمع منکر کو درج کیا۔
تقسیم ثانی:۔ استعمال کے اعتبار سے بھی لفظ کی چار میں ہیں حقیقت مجاز صریح کنا یہ وجہ حصر یہ ہے کہ لفظ دو حال سے خالی
نہیں ہے معنی موضوع لہ میں استعمال ہوگا یا غیر موضوع لہ میں استعمال ہوگا اگر معنی موضوع لہ میں استعمال ہو تو حقیقت ورنہ مجاز پھر دونوں دو حال سے خالی نہیں ہیں اگر ان کا معنی ظاہر ہے تو صریح ورنہ کہنا یہ ہے۔ تقسیم ثالث : باعتبار ظہور وفاء کے لفظ کی آٹھ قسمیں ہیں ظاہر نص مسر محکم فی مشکل مجمل متشابہ وجہ حصر یہ ہے کہ لفظ دو حال سے خالی نہیں ہے لفظ کا معنی ظاہر ہوگا یا مخفی اگر لفظ کا معنیٰ ظاہر ہے تو تاویل کا احتمال رکھے گا یا نہیں اگر تاویل کا احتمال رکھے تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں کہ نفس صیغہ سے معنی سمجھ میں آجائے گا یا نفس صیغہ سے معنی سمجھ میں نہیں آئے گا اگر نفس صیغہ سے معنی سمجھ میں آجائے تو ظاہر ہے اگر نفس صیغہ سے معنی سمجھ میں نہ آئے تو نص ہے اگر تاویل کا احتمال نہ رکھے تو دو حال سے خالی . نہیں نسخ کا احتمال رکھے گا یا نہیں اگر نسخ کا احتمال رکھتا ہو تو مفسر وگرنہ وہ محکم ہے اور اگر معنی مخفی ہو تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں کہ خفاء غیر کی وجہ سے آئے گا یا نفس صیغہ میں پایا جائے گا اگر تو یہ خفاء غیر کی وجہ سے ہے تو مخفی اور اگر نفس صیغہ سے خفا ہو تو دو حال
سے خالی نہیں غور و فکر سے معنی سمجھ میں آئے گا یا نہیں اگر غور و فکر سے معنی سمجھ میں آجائے تو مشکل اگر غور و فکر سے سمجھ میں نہ آئے تو متکلم سے بیان کی امید ہوگی یا نہیں اگر بیان کی امید ہو تو مجمل وگر نہ متشابہ ہے۔ تقسیم رابع : سے برآمد ہونے والی چار اقسام ہیں الدال بطریق عبارتة النص الدال بطريق الشارة النص الدال بطريق دلالت اعص اور الدال بطریق اقتضاء النص وجہ حصر یہ ہے کہ لفظ کی معنی پر دلالت دو حال سے خالی نہیں لفظ معنی پر دلالت کرے گا نظم کے اعتبار سے یا مفہوم کے اعتبار سے اگر دلالت نظم کی جہت سے ہو تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں لفظ کو اسی معنی کے لئے چلایا گیا ہو گا یا نہیں اگر اسی معنی کے لئے چلایا گیا ہو تو عبارۃ النص ہے وگرنہ وہ اشارہ اعص ہے اور اگر مفہوم کے اعتبار سے دال ہو تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں مفہوم لغوی کے اعتبار سے ہوگا یا نہیں اگر مفہوم لغوی کے اعتبار سے دلالت کرے تو یہ دلالت اعص ہے اور اگر مفہوم لغوی کے اعتبار سے دلالت نہ کرے تو یہ اقتضاء النص ہے۔
صاحب عالیہ اتحقیق پر تعریض
والحمد ۃ فی ذلک:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پانچواں حصہ ہے اس میں شارخ نے صاحب غایت اتحقیق پر تعریض کی ہے
مقدمہ : استقراء کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) استقراء تام (۲) استقراء ناقص ۔
استقراء تام :- یہ ہے کہ جزئی کا کلی کے تمام افراد پر حکم لگایا جائے اور یہ حکم قطعی اور یقینی ہوتا ہے لیکن زیادتی کا احتمال موجود ہوتا ہے جیسے یوں کہیں کل حیوان متخیز اب متحیر ہونا ہر اس حیوان کے لئے ثابت ہے جو خارج میں موجود ہو چکا ہے اس میں شبہ نہیں ہے لیکن زیادتی کا احتمال موجود ہے کہ جتنے حیوان بڑھیں گے متحیر بھی زیادہ ہونگے ۔
استقراء ناقص :- یہ ہے کہ جزی کا کلی کے تمام افراد پر حکم لگانا مشکل ہو اس لئے اکثر احکام پر حکم لگایا جاتا ہے استقراء ناقص یقین کا فائدہ نہیں دیتا یعنی جو حکم لگایا جاتا ہے وہ یقینی نہیں ہوتا مثلاً یہ حکم لگایا جائے کہ تمام حیوان کھاتے وقت نچلا جبڑا ہلاتے ہیں یہ حکم کی نہیں ہے کیونکہ بعض حیوان ایسے بھی ہیں کہ کھاتے وقت ان کا اوپر والا جبڑا اہلتا ہے جیسے مگر مچھ ہے اب یہ حکم یقینی نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ حکم اکثر افراد پر ہوتا ہے تمام افراد پر نہیں ہوتا اب تعریض یہ ہے کہ صاحب غایت التحقیق نے کہا کہ ان تقسیمات کی اقسام میں استقراء ناقص ہے ان میں وجوہ حصر سے برآمد ہونے والے اقسام یقینی نہیں بلکہ ان میں مزید اقسام کا اضافہ کیا جا سکتا ہے تو یہ استقراء ناقص ہے شارع نے رد کیا کہ استقراء تام ہے کیونکہ ان تقسیمات میں تمام افراد پر حکم پایا جاتا ہے اور تمام افراد کا ضبط ہوتا ہے خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ ان تقسیمات کی وجوہ حصر میں تمام افراد پر حکم لگانا ممکن ہے اور یہ تقسیمات وجہ
From lafz (word), therefore this will be prior. Then consideration of usage will be because it is later. In this respect, the second division will be based on clarity and obscurity, and the third division based on usage. The reason for the enumeration of the four divisions: [The author says:] 'The word in relation to meaning.' This is the fourth part of the sharh. From here the commentator explains the reason for the four divisions and mentions the categories derived from them. First division: The word according to the first division is summarized into four categories: khas, 'amm, mushtarak, mu'awwal. The reason for enumeration in the first division, i.e., based on wad' (coining), is that a word is either coined for one meaning or for multiple meanings. If coined for one meaning, then it is either confined to a single instance or not confined. If confined to a single instance, it is khas; if not confined but found in many instances, it is 'amm. If coined for multiple meanings, then either one meaning has preference over others (mu'awwal) or not (mushtarak). This division is according to the people (Hanafis); otherwise, Man (?) did not mention mu'awwal but instead entered jam' munkar (?) in its place. Second division: According to usage, the word also has four categories: haqiqah, majaz, sarih, kinayah. The reason for enumeration is that a word is either used in its original meaning (haqiqah) or in a non-original meaning (majaz). Then both are either clear in meaning (sarih) or not (kinayah). Third division: According to clarity and obscurity, the word has eight categories: zahir, nass, mufassar, muhkam, khafi, mushkil, mujmal, mutashabih. The reason for enumeration is that a word's meaning is either clear or hidden. If clear, it either admits ta'wil (interpretation) or not. If it admits ta'wil, then either its meaning is understood from its wording itself (zahir) or not (nass). If it does not admit ta'wil, then either it is subject to naskh (abrogation) (mufassar) or not (muhkam). If the meaning is hidden, then the obscurity comes either from external factors (khafi) or from the wording itself. If from the wording itself, then either it can be understood through reflection (mushkil) or not. If not, then either there is hope for explanation from the speaker (mujmal) or not (mutashabih). Fourth division: The four categories derived are: dalalat bi-tariq 'ibarah al-nass, dalalat bi-tariq isharah al-nass, dalalat bi-tariq dalalah al-nass, and dalalat bi-tariq iqtida' al-nass. The reason for enumeration is that a word's indication of meaning is either through its wording (nazm) or through its implication (mafhum). If through wording, then either the word was intended for that meaning ('ibarah) or not (isharah). If through implication, then either the implication is based on language (dalalah al-nass) or not (iqtida' al-nass). Criticism of Sahib Ghayat al-Tahqiq: [The author says:] 'And praise is in that.' This is the fifth part of the sharh. In it, the commentator criticizes Sahib Ghayat al-Tahqiq. Introduction: Istiqra' (induction) has two types: (1) complete induction (istiqra' tam) and (2) incomplete induction (istiqra' naqis). Complete induction: To apply a ruling of a particular to all individuals of a universal, and this ruling is decisive and certain, but there remains a possibility of increase. For example, saying 'All animals are mobile' — this is established for every animal that has existed in the external world; there is no doubt, but there is possibility of increase as more animals appear. Incomplete induction: It is difficult to apply the ruling of a particular to all individuals of a universal, so the ruling is applied to most cases. Incomplete induction does not yield certainty; the ruling is not certain. For example, the ruling that all animals move their lower jaw when eating is not certain because some animals move their upper jaw, like the crocodile. So this ruling applies to most individuals, not all. Now the criticism is that Sahib Ghayat al-Tahqiq said that in these divisions, the categories involve incomplete induction; the categories derived from the reasons for enumeration are not certain; rather, more categories could be added, so this is incomplete induction. The commentator refutes that it is complete induction because in these divisions, the ruling applies to all individuals, and all individuals are encompassed. The summary is that in the reasons for enumeration of these divisions, it is possible to apply the ruling to all individuals, and these divisions...
Source pages p. 491

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) explaining the four-fold classification of words (alfaz) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh and defending its exhaustive nature. The author first lists the four divisions: First, based on wad' (coining): khas (specific), 'amm (general), mushtarak (homonym), mu'awwal (interpreted). Second, based on isti'mal (usage): haqiqah (literal), majaz (metaphorical), sarih (explicit), kinayah (implicit). Third, based on zuhur (clarity) and khafa' (obscurity): eight categories from zahir to mutashabih. Fourth, based on dalalah (indication): 'ibarah al-nass, isharah al-nass, dalalah al-nass, iqtida' al-nass. For each division, the commentator provides the logical basis (wajh al-hasr) showing that all possibilities are exhausted. Then the passage addresses a criticism by the author of Ghayat al-Tahqiq, who claimed that these divisions are based on incomplete induction (istiqra' naqis) and thus not certain. The commentator defends that it is complete induction (istiqra' tam) because the logical enumeration covers all possibilities without exception. The example of animal movement illustrates the difference between complete and incomplete induction. The commentator argues that in these divisions, each category is defined by a binary opposition that leaves no room for missing categories. This is a typical Hanafi emphasis on rational enumeration (ihata) to establish certainty in usul definitions.

Key Terms
خاص (khas): A word coined for a single meaning confined to one individual instance (e.g., proper name).
عام (amm): A word coined for one meaning that applies to multiple individuals (e.g., 'human').
مشترک (mushtarak): A word coined for multiple meanings with no preference among them (e.g., 'ayn' = eye/spring/coin).
مؤول (mu'awwal): A word coined for multiple meanings where one is given preference by a contextual clue.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A word coined for one meaning that applies to all humans is classified as:
A) Khas
B) 'Amm
C) Mushtarak
D) Mu'awwal

Key Takeaway
The first division uses binary splits to exhaustively classify words into khas, 'amm, mushtarak, or mu'awwal based on their original coining.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
15 min
Second and Third Divisions: Usage and Clarity
Explaining the second and third divisions of words based on usage and clarity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to categorize words according to their usage (haqiqah/majaz/sarih/kinayah) and their clarity (zahir/nass/mufassar/muhkam/khafi/mushkil/mujmal/mutashabih).

Core Idea
Usage and clarity divisions further refine word meaning: literal vs. figurative, clear vs. hidden, each with legal implications.

After the first division based on coining, words are further classified by how they are used (haqiqah/majaz) and by how clear or obscure their meaning is (eight levels from zahir to mutashabih). These divisions are crucial in usul al-fiqh for determining whether a text can be reinterpreted or is definitive.

Guided Path
1
Understand the basis of the second division
The second division is based on isti'mal (usage): is the word used in its original coined meaning (haqiqah) or in a transferred meaning (majaz)? Then within each, is the meaning explicit (sarih) or implicit (kinayah)?
This division appears later because usage follows wad'.
2
Classify by haqiqah and majaz
If the word is used in its original meaning, it is haqiqah; if not, it is majaz. Both can be sarih (explicit) or kinayah (implicit) depending on clarity.
Majaz requires a contextual clue (qarinah) preventing the original meaning.
3
Apprehend the eight categories of the third division
The third division is based on zuhur (clarity) and khafa' (obscurity). The meaning can be clear (zahir, nass, mufassar, muhkam) or hidden (khafi, mushkil, mujmal, mutashabih). Each subcategory depends on whether ta'wil and naskh are possible.
Zahir admits ta'wil; nass does not. Mufassar admits naskh; muhkam does not.
4
Identify the hidden categories
If meaning is hidden, determine if the obscurity comes from external factors (khafi) or internal wording. If internal, check if reflection reveals meaning (mushkil). If not, check if speaker can explain (mujmal) or not (mutashabih).
This hierarchy determines the need for further interpretation.
5
Map each category to legal effect
For each category, note its dalalah strength: zahir is zanni, nass is qat'i; mujmal requires bayan; mutashabih is only known by Allah.
This affects whether the ruling is binding or open to reinterpretation.

From lafz (word), therefore this will be prior. Then consideration of usage will be because it is later. In this respect, the second division will be based on clarity and obscurity, and the third division based on usage. The reason for the enumeration of the four divisions: [The author says:] 'The word in relation to meaning.' This is the fourth part of the sharh. From here the commentator explains the reason for the four divisions and mentions the categories derived from them. First division: The word according to the first division is summarized into four categories: khas, 'amm, mushtarak, mu'awwal. The reason for enumeration in the first division, i.e., based on wad' (coining), is that a word is either coined for one meaning or for multiple meanings. If coined for one meaning, then it is either confined to a single instance or not confined. If confined to a single instance, it is khas; if not confined but found in many instances, it is 'amm. If coined for multiple meanings, then either one meaning has preference over others (mu'awwal) or not (mushtarak). This division is according to the people (Hanafis); otherwise, Man (?) did not mention mu'awwal but instead entered jam' munkar (?) in its place. Second division: According to usage, the word also has four categories: haqiqah, majaz, sarih, kinayah. The reason for enumeration is that a word is either used in its original meaning (haqiqah) or in a non-original meaning (majaz). Then both are either clear in meaning (sarih) or not (kinayah). Third division: According to clarity and obscurity, the word has eight categories: zahir, nass, mufassar, muhkam, khafi, mushkil, mujmal, mutashabih. The reason for enumeration is that a word's meaning is either clear or hidden. If clear, it either admits ta'wil (interpretation) or not. If it admits ta'wil, then either its meaning is understood from its wording itself (zahir) or not (nass). If it does not admit ta'wil, then either it is subject to naskh (abrogation) (mufassar) or not (muhkam). If the meaning is hidden, then the obscurity comes either from external factors (khafi) or from the wording itself. If from the wording itself, then either it can be understood through reflection (mushkil) or not. If not, then either there is hope for explanation from the speaker (mujmal) or not (mutashabih). Fourth division: The four categories derived are: dalalat bi-tariq 'ibarah al-nass, dalalat bi-tariq isharah al-nass, dalalat bi-tariq dalalah al-nass, and dalalat bi-tariq iqtida' al-nass. The reason for enumeration is that a word's indication of meaning is either through its wording (nazm) or through its implication (mafhum). If through wording, then either the word was intended for that meaning ('ibarah) or not (isharah). If through implication, then either the implication is based on language (dalalah al-nass) or not (iqtida' al-nass). Criticism of Sahib Ghayat al-Tahqiq: [The author says:] 'And praise is in that.' Introduction: Istiqra' (induction) has two types: (1) complete induction (istiqra' tam) and (2) incomplete induction (istiqra' naqis). Complete induction: To apply a ruling of a particular to all individuals of a universal, and this ruling is decisive and certain, but there remains a possibility of increase. For example, saying 'All animals are mobile' — this is established for every animal that has existed in the external world; there is no doubt, but there is possibility of increase as more animals appear. Incomplete induction: It is difficult to apply the ruling of a particular to all individuals of a universal, so the ruling is applied to most cases. Incomplete induction does not yield certainty; the ruling is not certain. For example, the ruling that all animals move their lower jaw when eating is not certain because some animals move their upper jaw, like the crocodile. So this ruling applies to most individuals, not all. Now the criticism is that Sahib Ghayat al-Tahqiq said that in these divisions, the categories involve incomplete induction; the categories derived from the reasons for enumeration are not certain; rather, more categories could be added, so this is incomplete induction. The commentator refutes that it is complete induction because in these divisions, the ruling applies to all individuals, and all individuals are encompassed. Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) explaining the four-fold classification of words (alfaz) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh and defending its exhaustive nature. The author first lists the four divisions: First, based on wad' (coining): khas (specific), 'amm (general), mushtarak (homonym), mu'awwal (interpreted). Second, based on isti'mal (usage): haqiqah (literal), majaz (metaphorical), sarih (explicit), kinayah (implicit). Third, based on zuhur (clarity) and khafa' (obscurity): eight categories from zahir to mutashabih. Fourth, based on dalalah (indication): 'ibarah al-nass, isharah al-nass, dalalah al-nass, iqtida' al-nass. For each division, the commentator provides the logical basis (wajh al-hasr) showing that all possibilities are exhausted. Then the passage addresses a criticism by the author of Ghayat al-Tahqiq, who claimed that these divisions are based on incomplete induction (istiqra' naqis) and thus not certain. The commentator defends that it is complete induction (istiqra' tam) because the logical enumeration covers all possibilities without exception. The example of animal movement illustrates the difference between complete and incomplete induction. The commentator argues that in these divisions, each category is defined by a binary opposition that leaves no room for missing categories. This is a typical Hanafi emphasis on rational enumeration (ihata) to establish certainty in usul definitions.

Key Terms
حقیقت (haqiqah): A word used in its original coined meaning (e.g., 'lion' for the animal).
مجاز (majaz): A word used in a non-original meaning with a contextual clue (e.g., 'lion' for a brave man).
ظاہر (zahir): A word whose meaning is clear from wording but admits ta'wil (interpretation).
نص (nass): A word whose meaning is clear and does not admit ta'wil.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A word used in a non-original meaning with a clear contextual clue is classified in the second division as:
A) Haqiqah sarih
B) Majaz sarih
C) Haqiqah kinayah
D) Majaz kinayah

Key Takeaway
The second and third divisions categorize words by usage (literal vs. figurative) and clarity (eight levels), providing a nuanced framework for determining the definitiveness of legal texts.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

The Fourth Division: Modes of Indication (Dalalah)
Explaining the fourth division of words based on modes of indication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the four modes of textual indication: 'ibarah al-nass, isharah al-nass, dalalah al-nass, and iqtida' al-nass.

Core Idea
Words indicate meaning either through their wording or implication; each mode has different evidentiary strength.

The fourth division focuses on how a text conveys its ruling: explicitly through wording ('ibarah), implicitly via context (isharah), through logical entailment (dalalah), or through necessary complement (iqtida'). Recognising these modes is essential for istinbat (derivation of rulings) from primary texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basis of the fourth division
This division is based on the manner of dalalah (indication): does the text indicate meaning through its wording (nazm) or through its implication (mafhum)?
The nazm/mafhum split is the first binary.
2
Classify indications via wording
If through wording, was the word intended for that meaning ('ibarah al-nass) or not (isharah al-nass)? 'Ibarah is the literal meaning intended by the speaker; isharah is a secondary implied meaning from context.
Example: 'Forbidden to you are your mothers' – 'ibarah prohibits marriage; isharah implies respect.
3
Classify indications via implication
If through implication (mafhum), is the implication based on linguistic convention (dalalah al-nass) or necessary for the statement's validity (iqtida' al-nass)?
Dalalah al-nass is like understanding that a son inherits from 'your children' (mafhum muwafaqah).
4
Understand the hierarchy of proof
These four modes have different strengths: 'ibarah is strongest, then isharah, then dalalah, then iqtida'. Hanafi usul uses all four in derivation.
Some later schools only accept 'ibarah and isharah.
5
Apply to a Quranic example
Take the verse 'Wa la tanzur' (and do not approach) – 'ibarah prohibits the act; isharah implies prohibition of its means; dalalah suggests the prohibition of anything similar; iqtida' requires the existence of the act to be meaningful.
Practice with multiple verses.

From lafz (word), therefore this will be prior. Then consideration of usage will be because it is later. In this respect, the second division will be based on clarity and obscurity, and the third division based on usage. The reason for the enumeration of the four divisions: [The author says:] 'The word in relation to meaning.' This is the fourth part of the sharh. From here the commentator explains the reason for the four divisions and mentions the categories derived from them. First division: The word according to the first division is summarized into four categories: khas, 'amm, mushtarak, mu'awwal. The reason for enumeration in the first division, i.e., based on wad' (coining), is that a word is either coined for one meaning or for multiple meanings. If coined for one meaning, then it is either confined to a single instance or not confined. If confined to a single instance, it is khas; if not confined but found in many instances, it is 'amm. If coined for multiple meanings, then either one meaning has preference over others (mu'awwal) or not (mushtarak). This division is according to the people (Hanafis); otherwise, Man (?) did not mention mu'awwal but instead entered jam' munkar (?) in its place. Second division: According to usage, the word also has four categories: haqiqah, majaz, sarih, kinayah. The reason for enumeration is that a word is either used in its original meaning (haqiqah) or in a non-original meaning (majaz). Then both are either clear in meaning (sarih) or not (kinayah). Third division: According to clarity and obscurity, the word has eight categories: zahir, nass, mufassar, muhkam, khafi, mushkil, mujmal, mutashabih. The reason for enumeration is that a word's meaning is either clear or hidden. If clear, it either admits ta'wil (interpretation) or not. If it admits ta'wil, then either its meaning is understood from its wording itself (zahir) or not (nass). If it does not admit ta'wil, then either it is subject to naskh (abrogation) (mufassar) or not (muhkam). If the meaning is hidden, then the obscurity comes either from external factors (khafi) or from the wording itself. If from the wording itself, then either it can be understood through reflection (mushkil) or not. If not, then either there is hope for explanation from the speaker (mujmal) or not (mutashabih). Fourth division: The four categories derived are: dalalat bi-tariq 'ibarah al-nass, dalalat bi-tariq isharah al-nass, dalalat bi-tariq dalalah al-nass, and dalalat bi-tariq iqtida' al-nass. The reason for enumeration is that a word's indication of meaning is either through its wording (nazm) or through its implication (mafhum). If through wording, then either the word was intended for that meaning ('ibarah) or not (isharah). If through implication, then either the implication is based on language (dalalah al-nass) or not (iqtida' al-nass). Criticism of Sahib Ghayat al-Tahqiq: [The author says:] 'And praise is in that.' This is the fifth part of the sharh. In it, the commentator criticizes Sahib Ghayat al-Tahqiq. Introduction: Istiqra' (induction) has two types: (1) complete induction (istiqra' tam) and (2) incomplete induction (istiqra' naqis). Complete induction: To apply a ruling of a particular to all individuals of a universal, and this ruling is decisive and certain, but there remains a possibility of increase. For example, saying 'All animals are mobile' — this is established for every animal that has existed in the external world; there is no doubt, but there is possibility of increase as more animals appear. Incomplete induction: It is difficult to apply the ruling of a particular to all individuals of a universal, so the ruling is applied to most cases. Incomplete induction does not yield certainty; the ruling is not certain. For example, the ruling that all animals move their lower jaw when eating is not certain because some animals move their upper jaw, like the crocodile. So this ruling applies to most individuals, not all. Now the criticism is that Sahib Ghayat al-Tahqiq said that in these divisions, the categories involve incomplete induction; the categories derived from the reasons for enumeration are not certain; rather, more categories could be added, so this is incomplete induction. The commentator refutes that it is complete induction because in these divisions, the ruling applies to all individuals, and all individuals are encompassed. The summary is that in the reasons for enumeration of these divisions, it is possible to apply the ruling to all individuals, and these divisions...
Source pages p. 491

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) explaining the four-fold classification of words (alfaz) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh and defending its exhaustive nature. The author first lists the four divisions: First, based on wad' (coining): khas (specific), 'amm (general), mushtarak (homonym), mu'awwal (interpreted). Second, based on isti'mal (usage): haqiqah (literal), majaz (metaphorical), sarih (explicit), kinayah (implicit). Third, based on zuhur (clarity) and khafa' (obscurity): eight categories from zahir to mutashabih. Fourth, based on dalalah (indication): 'ibarah al-nass, isharah al-nass, dalalah al-nass, iqtida' al-nass. For each division, the commentator provides the logical basis (wajh al-hasr) showing that all possibilities are exhausted. Then the passage addresses a criticism by the author of Ghayat al-Tahqiq, who claimed that these divisions are based on incomplete induction (istiqra' naqis) and thus not certain. The commentator defends that it is complete induction (istiqra' tam) because the logical enumeration covers all possibilities without exception. The example of animal movement illustrates the difference between complete and incomplete induction. The commentator argues that in these divisions, each category is defined by a binary opposition that leaves no room for missing categories. This is a typical Hanafi emphasis on rational enumeration (ihata) to establish certainty in usul definitions.

Key Terms
عبارۃ النص ('ibarah al-nass): The direct meaning intended by the speaker through the wording of the text.
اشارۃ النص (isharah al-nass): A meaning implied by the context but not directly stated.
دلالۃ النص (dalalah al-nass): A meaning derived from the text through linguistic implication (mafhum muwafaqah).
اقتضاء النص (iqtida' al-nass): A meaning that must be added for the text to be coherent (e.g., an omitted condition).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A text stating 'forbidden to you are your mothers' directly forbids marriage; the implication that one must also avoid unlawful relations is an example of:
A) 'Ibarah al-nass
B) Isharah al-nass
C) Dalalah al-nass
D) Iqtida' al-nass

Key Takeaway
The fourth division categorizes how texts indicate rulings: direct ('ibarah), contextual (isharah), linguistic implication (dalalah), and necessary supplement (iqtida').

Complete Induction (Istiqra' Tam) and Defense of the Divisions
Defending the exhaustive nature of the four divisions via complete induction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish complete induction from incomplete induction and evaluate the Hanafi argument that the four divisions are based on complete induction, thereby refuting criticism.

Core Idea
Complete induction yields certainty; the four divisions are exhaustive because they use binary splits that cover all logical possibilities.

After presenting the four divisions, the commentator defends their exhaustive nature against a critic who claimed they were based on incomplete induction. This defense introduces the crucial usul concept of istiqra' tam (complete induction) and demonstrates how logical dichotomies can produce certainty in classification. Understanding this debate is key to appreciating the Hanafi commitment to methodological rigor.

Guided Path
1
Define the two types of induction
Istiqra' tam (complete induction) applies a ruling to all individuals of a universal, yielding certainty but admitting future increase. Istiqra' naqis (incomplete induction) applies to most, not all, and does not yield certainty.
Example: 'All animals move lower jaw' is naqis because crocodiles move upper jaw.
2
Identify the critic's claim
Sahib Ghayat al-Tahqiq argued that the four divisions are based on incomplete induction, so more categories could be added, making the enumeration uncertain.
This challenges the definitiveness of the divisions.
3
Understand the Hanafi response
The commentator refutes by stating that the divisions are based on complete induction because they use binary oppositions (e.g., one meaning vs many, clear vs hidden) that are mutually exclusive and collectively exhaustive, covering all possibilities without exception.
The logical structure itself guarantees exhaustiveness.
4
Apply the concept to a division
Take the first division: either one meaning or many; if one, either confined or not; if many, either preferred or not. These splits cover all possibilities for a word's wad'. No scenario is left out.
This is the key argument: the enumeration is exhaustive because each split is exhaustive.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
If the divisions were incomplete, usul categories would be open-ended, undermining certainty in legal derivation. The Hanafi position preserves definiteness.
This shows the practical importance of the debate.

تقسیمات اربعہ کی وجہ حصر
قاللفظ بالنسبۃ الی المعنی :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا چوتھا حصہ ہے یہاں سے شارعا تقسیمات اربعہ کی وجہ صر بیان کرتے
ہیں اور ان سے برآمد شدہ اقسام کو ذکر کرتے ہیں۔
تقسیم اول: لفظ پہلی تقسیم کے اعتبار سے مخصر ہے چار قسموں میں یعنی خاص عام مشترک مؤول میں تقسیم اول یعنی لفظ کی وضع لاسی کے اعتبار سے تقسیم کی وجہ حصر یہ ہے کہ لفظ دو حال سے خالی نہیں ایک معنی کے لئے وضع کیا گیا ہوگا یا متعدد معانی کے لئے اگر ایک معنی کے لئے وضع ہو پھر دو حال سے خالی نہیں کہ ایک معنی فرد واحد میں منحصر ہوگا یا فرد واحد میں منحصر نہیں ہوگا اگر ایک معنی فرد واحد میں منحصر ہو تو یہ خاص ہے اور اگر ایک معنی فرد واحد میں منحصر نہ ہو بلکہ کئی افراد میں پایا جاتا ہو تو یہ عام ہے اور اگر وضع کئی معانی کے لئے ہو تو پھر دو حال سے خالی نہیں ایک معنی کو دوسرے معنی پر ترجیح حاصل ہوگی یا نہیں اگر ایک معنی کو دوسرے معنی پر ترجیح حاصل ہوگی تو موکول ہے اور اگر ترجیح حاصل نہ ہو تو مشترک ہوگا یہ تقسیم قوم کے اعتبار سے ہے وگر نہ مان بمع نے مؤول کو ذکر نہیں کیا بلکہ اس کی جگہ جمع منکر کو درج کیا۔
تقسیم ثانی:۔ استعمال کے اعتبار سے بھی لفظ کی چار میں ہیں حقیقت مجاز صریح کنا یہ وجہ حصر یہ ہے کہ لفظ دو حال سے خالی
نہیں ہے معنی موضوع لہ میں استعمال ہوگا یا غیر موضوع لہ میں استعمال ہوگا اگر معنی موضوع لہ میں استعمال ہو تو حقیقت ورنہ مجاز پھر دونوں دو حال سے خالی نہیں ہیں اگر ان کا معنی ظاہر ہے تو صریح ورنہ کہنا یہ ہے۔ تقسیم ثالث : باعتبار ظہور وفاء کے لفظ کی آٹھ قسمیں ہیں ظاہر نص مسر محکم فی مشکل مجمل متشابہ وجہ حصر یہ ہے کہ لفظ دو حال سے خالی نہیں ہے لفظ کا معنی ظاہر ہوگا یا مخفی اگر لفظ کا معنیٰ ظاہر ہے تو تاویل کا احتمال رکھے گا یا نہیں اگر تاویل کا احتمال رکھے تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں کہ نفس صیغہ سے معنی سمجھ میں آجائے گا یا نفس صیغہ سے معنی سمجھ میں نہیں آئے گا اگر نفس صیغہ سے معنی سمجھ میں آجائے تو ظاہر ہے اگر نفس صیغہ سے معنی سمجھ میں نہ آئے تو نص ہے اگر تاویل کا احتمال نہ رکھے تو دو حال سے خالی . نہیں نسخ کا احتمال رکھے گا یا نہیں اگر نسخ کا احتمال رکھتا ہو تو مفسر وگرنہ وہ محکم ہے اور اگر معنی مخفی ہو تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں کہ خفاء غیر کی وجہ سے آئے گا یا نفس صیغہ میں پایا جائے گا اگر تو یہ خفاء غیر کی وجہ سے ہے تو مخفی اور اگر نفس صیغہ سے خفا ہو تو دو حال
سے خالی نہیں غور و فکر سے معنی سمجھ میں آئے گا یا نہیں اگر غور و فکر سے معنی سمجھ میں آجائے تو مشکل اگر غور و فکر سے سمجھ میں نہ آئے تو متکلم سے بیان کی امید ہوگی یا نہیں اگر بیان کی امید ہو تو مجمل وگر نہ متشابہ ہے۔ تقسیم رابع : سے برآمد ہونے والی چار اقسام ہیں الدال بطریق عبارتة النص الدال بطريق الشارة النص الدال بطريق دلالت اعص اور الدال بطریق اقتضاء النص وجہ حصر یہ ہے کہ لفظ کی معنی پر دلالت دو حال سے خالی نہیں لفظ معنی پر دلالت کرے گا نظم کے اعتبار سے یا مفہوم کے اعتبار سے اگر دلالت نظم کی جہت سے ہو تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں لفظ کو اسی معنی کے لئے چلایا گیا ہو گا یا نہیں اگر اسی معنی کے لئے چلایا گیا ہو تو عبارۃ النص ہے وگرنہ وہ اشارہ اعص ہے اور اگر مفہوم کے اعتبار سے دال ہو تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں مفہوم لغوی کے اعتبار سے ہوگا یا نہیں اگر مفہوم لغوی کے اعتبار سے دلالت کرے تو یہ دلالت اعص ہے اور اگر مفہوم لغوی کے اعتبار سے دلالت نہ کرے تو یہ اقتضاء النص ہے۔
صاحب عالیہ اتحقیق پر تعریض
والحمد ۃ فی ذلک:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پانچواں حصہ ہے اس میں شارخ نے صاحب غایت اتحقیق پر تعریض کی ہے
مقدمہ : استقراء کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) استقراء تام (۲) استقراء ناقص ۔
استقراء تام :- یہ ہے کہ جزئی کا کلی کے تمام افراد پر حکم لگایا جائے اور یہ حکم قطعی اور یقینی ہوتا ہے لیکن زیادتی کا احتمال موجود ہوتا ہے جیسے یوں کہیں کل حیوان متخیز اب متحیر ہونا ہر اس حیوان کے لئے ثابت ہے جو خارج میں موجود ہو چکا ہے اس میں شبہ نہیں ہے لیکن زیادتی کا احتمال موجود ہے کہ جتنے حیوان بڑھیں گے متحیر بھی زیادہ ہونگے ۔
استقراء ناقص :- یہ ہے کہ جزی کا کلی کے تمام افراد پر حکم لگانا مشکل ہو اس لئے اکثر احکام پر حکم لگایا جاتا ہے استقراء ناقص یقین کا فائدہ نہیں دیتا یعنی جو حکم لگایا جاتا ہے وہ یقینی نہیں ہوتا مثلاً یہ حکم لگایا جائے کہ تمام حیوان کھاتے وقت نچلا جبڑا ہلاتے ہیں یہ حکم کی نہیں ہے کیونکہ بعض حیوان ایسے بھی ہیں کہ کھاتے وقت ان کا اوپر والا جبڑا اہلتا ہے جیسے مگر مچھ ہے اب یہ حکم یقینی نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ حکم اکثر افراد پر ہوتا ہے تمام افراد پر نہیں ہوتا اب تعریض یہ ہے کہ صاحب غایت التحقیق نے کہا کہ ان تقسیمات کی اقسام میں استقراء ناقص ہے ان میں وجوہ حصر سے برآمد ہونے والے اقسام یقینی نہیں بلکہ ان میں مزید اقسام کا اضافہ کیا جا سکتا ہے تو یہ استقراء ناقص ہے شارع نے رد کیا کہ استقراء تام ہے کیونکہ ان تقسیمات میں تمام افراد پر حکم پایا جاتا ہے اور تمام افراد کا ضبط ہوتا ہے خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ ان تقسیمات کی وجوہ حصر میں تمام افراد پر حکم لگانا ممکن ہے اور یہ تقسیمات وجہ
From lafz (word), therefore this will be prior. Then consideration of usage will be because it is later. In this respect, the second division will be based on clarity and obscurity, and the third division based on usage. The reason for the enumeration of the four divisions: [The author says:] 'The word in relation to meaning.' This is the fourth part of the sharh. From here the commentator explains the reason for the four divisions and mentions the categories derived from them. First division: The word according to the first division is summarized into four categories: khas, 'amm, mushtarak, mu'awwal. The reason for enumeration in the first division, i.e., based on wad' (coining), is that a word is either coined for one meaning or for multiple meanings. If coined for one meaning, then it is either confined to a single instance or not confined. If confined to a single instance, it is khas; if not confined but found in many instances, it is 'amm. If coined for multiple meanings, then either one meaning has preference over others (mu'awwal) or not (mushtarak). This division is according to the people (Hanafis); otherwise, Man (?) did not mention mu'awwal but instead entered jam' munkar (?) in its place. Second division: According to usage, the word also has four categories: haqiqah, majaz, sarih, kinayah. The reason for enumeration is that a word is either used in its original meaning (haqiqah) or in a non-original meaning (majaz). Then both are either clear in meaning (sarih) or not (kinayah). Third division: According to clarity and obscurity, the word has eight categories: zahir, nass, mufassar, muhkam, khafi, mushkil, mujmal, mutashabih. The reason for enumeration is that a word's meaning is either clear or hidden. If clear, it either admits ta'wil (interpretation) or not. If it admits ta'wil, then either its meaning is understood from its wording itself (zahir) or not (nass). If it does not admit ta'wil, then either it is subject to naskh (abrogation) (mufassar) or not (muhkam). If the meaning is hidden, then the obscurity comes either from external factors (khafi) or from the wording itself. If from the wording itself, then either it can be understood through reflection (mushkil) or not. If not, then either there is hope for explanation from the speaker (mujmal) or not (mutashabih). Fourth division: The four categories derived are: dalalat bi-tariq 'ibarah al-nass, dalalat bi-tariq isharah al-nass, dalalat bi-tariq dalalah al-nass, and dalalat bi-tariq iqtida' al-nass. The reason for enumeration is that a word's indication of meaning is either through its wording (nazm) or through its implication (mafhum). If through wording, then either the word was intended for that meaning ('ibarah) or not (isharah). If through implication, then either the implication is based on language (dalalah al-nass) or not (iqtida' al-nass). Criticism of Sahib Ghayat al-Tahqiq: [The author says:] 'And praise is in that.' This is the fifth part of the sharh. In it, the commentator criticizes Sahib Ghayat al-Tahqiq. Introduction: Istiqra' (induction) has two types: (1) complete induction (istiqra' tam) and (2) incomplete induction (istiqra' naqis). Complete induction: To apply a ruling of a particular to all individuals of a universal, and this ruling is decisive and certain, but there remains a possibility of increase. For example, saying 'All animals are mobile' — this is established for every animal that has existed in the external world; there is no doubt, but there is possibility of increase as more animals appear. Incomplete induction: It is difficult to apply the ruling of a particular to all individuals of a universal, so the ruling is applied to most cases. Incomplete induction does not yield certainty; the ruling is not certain. For example, the ruling that all animals move their lower jaw when eating is not certain because some animals move their upper jaw, like the crocodile. So this ruling applies to most individuals, not all. Now the criticism is that Sahib Ghayat al-Tahqiq said that in these divisions, the categories involve incomplete induction; the categories derived from the reasons for enumeration are not certain; rather, more categories could be added, so this is incomplete induction. The commentator refutes that it is complete induction because in these divisions, the ruling applies to all individuals, and all individuals are encompassed. The summary is that in the reasons for enumeration of these divisions, it is possible to apply the ruling to all individuals, and these divisions...
Source pages p. 491

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) explaining the four-fold classification of words (alfaz) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh and defending its exhaustive nature. The author first lists the four divisions: First, based on wad' (coining): khas (specific), 'amm (general), mushtarak (homonym), mu'awwal (interpreted). Second, based on isti'mal (usage): haqiqah (literal), majaz (metaphorical), sarih (explicit), kinayah (implicit). Third, based on zuhur (clarity) and khafa' (obscurity): eight categories from zahir to mutashabih. Fourth, based on dalalah (indication): 'ibarah al-nass, isharah al-nass, dalalah al-nass, iqtida' al-nass. For each division, the commentator provides the logical basis (wajh al-hasr) showing that all possibilities are exhausted. Then the passage addresses a criticism by the author of Ghayat al-Tahqiq, who claimed that these divisions are based on incomplete induction (istiqra' naqis) and thus not certain. The commentator defends that it is complete induction (istiqra' tam) because the logical enumeration covers all possibilities without exception. The example of animal movement illustrates the difference between complete and incomplete induction. The commentator argues that in these divisions, each category is defined by a binary opposition that leaves no room for missing categories. This is a typical Hanafi emphasis on rational enumeration (ihata) to establish certainty in usul definitions.

Key Terms
استقراء تام (istiqra' tam): Complete induction: applying a ruling to all individuals of a universal, yielding certainty.
استقراء ناقص (istiqra' naqis): Incomplete induction: applying a ruling to most individuals, yielding probability, not certainty.
تعریض (ta'riz): Criticism or refutation of another's argument.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main difference between complete and incomplete induction according to the passage?
A) Complete induction yields certainty; incomplete does not.
B) Complete induction covers all known individuals; incomplete covers only some.
C) Complete induction is used for animals; incomplete for words.
D) Complete induction allows no possibility of increase; incomplete does.

Key Takeaway
The four word divisions are based on complete induction through logical dichotomies, making them exhaustive and certain for usul al-fiqh.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
12 min
Rationale for Fakhr al-Islam's Division of Lafẓ into Ṣīghah and Lughah
Explanation of the rationale for Fakhr al-Islam's division of word coinage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two components of word coinage according to Hanafi uṣūl and explain why Fakhr al-Islam explicitly distinguished ṣīghah and lughah instead of using the term waḍʿ.

Core Idea
Word meaning requires both matter and form; Fakhr al-Islam's distinction prevents ambiguity about the types of coinage.

This lesson unpacks a subtle yet fundamental distinction in Hanafi legal theory: the division of the word (lafẓ) into form (ṣīghah) and lexeme (lughah). Fakhr al-Islam used this phrasing for the first of his four divisions of words. The commentator provides two opinions on the relationship between these terms and explains why the explicit mention is necessary. You will learn how Hanafi uṣūl treats linguistic coinage as comprising both a morphological pattern and a lexical root, and how this affects the derivation of rulings from texts.

Guided Path
1
Locate the first division title
Identify the phrase 'al-awwal fī wujūh al-naẓm ṣīghah wa lughah' and note that 'wujūh' here means aspects, not ways. This sets the stage for understanding the scope of the first division.
2
Understand the two opinions on ṣīghah and lughah
One opinion treats ṣīghah and lughah as synonyms for 'word'. The other distinguishes them: ṣīghah is the morphological form (pattern of vowels and letters), while lughah is the lexical root (mādah).
The commentator favors the second view as it aligns with the broader discussion of coinage.
3
Recognize the dual aspect of coinage
Coinage (waḍʿ) includes both the matter (mādah) and the form (hayʾah). Just as the root ḍ-r-b was coined for the meaning of 'striking', the form faʿala was coined for past tense. Thus, a word indicates meaning through both components.
This is why Fakhr al-Islam mentioned both ṣīghah and lughah to refer to waḍʿ.
4
Analyze the question and first answer
The question: why not simply say 'waḍʿ'? The first answer: the term 'waḍʿ' alone could be misunderstood to include a deficient type of generic coinage (the second subtype of waḍʿ nawʿī related to majāz). Explicit mention avoids this confusion.
Types of waḍʿ: personal (shakhṣī) and generic (nawʿī). The generic has two subtypes: direct rule and indirect rule (majāz).
5
Analyze the second answer
The second answer is pedagogical: explicitly mentioning form (ṣīghah) first highlights that most legal ḥaqīqahs, especially commands and prohibitions, depend on form rather than root. This teaches a key usul principle.
For example, the imperative form alone conveys obligation, regardless of the root.

لفظ نہیں دلالت کرتا اپنے معنی پر مگر مادہ اور ہیئت کی وضع سے پس تعبیر کی ہے ان دونوں کے ذکر کے ساتھ وضع لفظ سے اور تعبیر کیا دوسری تقسیم کو اپنے قول فی وجوہ استعمال ذالک العظیم و جریانہ فی باب البیان کے ساتھ یعنی لفظ کو منی میں استعمال کرنے کے طرق کے بیان میں اس پر محمول کرتے ہوئے کہ اگر اس کا معنی موضوع لہ میں استعمال کرنے کے طرق کے بیان میں اس پر محمول کرتے ہوئے کہ اگر اس کا معنی موضوع لہ میں استعمال ہے تو وہ حقیقہ ہو گا یا اس کے غیر میں مستعمل ہے تو مجاز ہوگا یا اعظم کو معنی کے بیان اور اظہار میں جاری کرنے کے طرق کے بیان میں بایں طور کہ اگر وہ وضوح کے طریق سے ہے تو صریح ہو گا یا استتار (پوشیدگی ) کے طریق پر ہے تو کنا یہ ہوگا اور تیسری تقسیم کو تعبیر کیا ہے اپنے قول فی وجوہ البیان بذالک اعظم سے یعنی اظہار معنی اور اس کے مراتب کے طرق کے بیان میں اور چوتھی تقسیم کو تعبیر کیا ہے اپنے قول فی معرفتہ وجوہ الوقوف علی المراد والمعانی کے ساتھ یعنی معانی کلام اور مراد متکلم پر سامع کے اطلاع پانے کے طرق کی معرفت کے بیان میں بایں طور کہ وہ اس پر عبارۃ الحصن کے طریق سے مطلع ہوتا ہے یا اشارۃ المص کے طریق سے یا ان دونوں کے غیر سے۔
علامہ فخر الاسلام کے تقسیمات اربعہ میں عنوانات و تعبیرات
تشریح : قولہ وہذا ما قال: یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے شاریخ اس عبارت میں فخر الاسلام کی تقسیم اول کے بارے میں بیان کردہ تعبیر و عنوان کو ذکر کر کے اس کا مفہوم بیان کرتے ہیں جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ فخر الاسلام نے تقسیم اول کا عنوان قائم کیا الاول في وجوه النظم صیفہ والفتہ اس میں وجوہ بمعنی جہات اور اعتبارات کے ہیں یعنی پہلی تقسیم اعظم کے جہات کے بیان میں صیغہ اور لغتہ کے اعتبار سے بیان وجوہ طرق کے معنی میں نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ طرق نظم کا کوئی معنی نہیں ہے یہی راز ہے شاری کا تقسیم اول میں سکوت اختیار کرنے کا اور باقی تینوں اقسام میں وجوہ کی تفسیر طرق کے ساتھ بیان کرنے کا۔ فاضہم ۔ اور صیغہ ولفتہ سے کیا مراد ہے اس میں شاریخ نے دو قول نقل فرمائے ہیں۔ قول اول: کہ صیغہ اور لغت دونوں مترادف ہیں یعنی جو لفظ معنی پر دال ہو اس کو صیغہ بھی کہتے ہیں اور لغتہ بھی اور اس اعتبار سے تقسیم سے مقصود ہوگا کہ تقسیم اول نفس معنی کے اعتبار سے ہے متکلم یا سامع کے اعتبار سے نہیں۔
قول ثانی:۔ صیغہ والہ دونوں مترادف نہیں ہیں بلکہ ان میں فرق ہے کہ صیغہ کہتے ہیں اس بیت اور شکل کو جو لفظ کو باعتبار حرکات و سکنات اور بعض حروف کی بعض پر تقدیم کی وجہ سے حاصل ہو اور لغتہ لفظ موضوع کو کہتے ہیں۔ لیکن یہاں چونکہ لغت کو صیغہ کے مقابل لایا گیا ہے اس لئے اس (لغت) سے مراد فقط مادہ ہے اب صیغہ واقعہ تقسیم سے مراد تقسیم باعتبار الوضع ہوگی وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ ان دونوں (مادہ و ہیئت ) میں واضع کی وضع کو دخل ہے کیونکہ جیسے واضع نے ضرب کے حروف کو مخصوص معنی کے لئے وضع کیا ہے اسی طرح اس نے اس کی ہیئت کو بھی معنی مفنی (گزرا ہوا) کیلئے وضع کیا ہے پس لفظ کی دلالت معنی پر دو چیزوں کے ساتھ ہوتی ہے (۱) وضع مادہ (۲) وضع ہیاۃ ۔ لہذا جب ان دونوں کو وضع میں دخل ہوا تو ان دونوں کو ذکر کر کے وضع مراد لے لیتے ہیں چنانچہ یہاں علامہ فخر الاسلام نے ایسے ہی کیا ہے کہ صیغہ والفتہ (بیا تا اور مادہ) بونکر وضع مراد لیا ہے۔ سوال:۔ جب صیغہ ولفتہ کے عنوان سے مقصود لفظ کی تقسیم وضع المعنی کے اعتبار سے ہے تو علامہ فخر الاسلام نے اس کو وضع للمعنی سے کیوں تعبیر نہیں کیا ؟ جبکہ اس میں اختصار بھی ہے؟
جواب (1):۔ جواب کو سمجھنے سے قبل ایک مقدمہ کا جانا ضروری ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ وضع کی دوقسمیں ہیں (۱) وضع شخصی اور وہ یہ ہے کہ لفظ کو معنی مخصوص کے مقابلہ میں متعین کرنا (۲) وضع نوعی پھر اس کی دو قسمیں ہیں۔
اول: کوئی قاعدہ یا ضابطہ متعین کرنا کہ ہر وہ لفظ جو فلاں کیفیت کے ساتھ متصف ہوگا وہ فلاں معنی مخصوص پر دلالت کرے گا
مثلا یوں کہنا کہ ہر وہ جمع کا صیغہ جو معرف باسلام ہو تو وہ اپنے مسمیات میں سے ہر سمجی پر دلالت کریگا۔
ثانی:۔ اس طرح کا ضابطہ بیان کرنا کہ ہر وہ لفظ جو معنی مخصوص کے لئے وضع کیا گیا ہو قرینہ صارفہ ( یعنی اس معنی کے مراد نہ لینے پر) کے وقت اس کے متعلقات میں سے مخصوص متعلق پر دلالت کرے گا اب وضع نوعی کی یہ دوسری قسم مجاز کے قبیل سے ہے کیونکہ لفظ بیان معنی اصلی سے متجاوز ہو جاتا ہے۔
جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ جب لفظ وضع کو مطلقا ذ کر کیا جاتا ہے تو یہاں وضع کی تیسری قسم مراد نہیں لی جاتی اس لئے کہ یہ پہلی دونوں قسموں سے ناقص ہے البتہ پہلی دونوں قسمیں مراد لی جاسکتی ہیں لیکن کسی کو وہم ہو سکتا ہے کہ شاید دوسری قسم بھی مراد نہ لے
سکیں کیونکہ یہ اول قسم سے ناقص ہے تو اس وہم کے ازالہ کے لئے فخر الاسلام نے وضع کا لفظ ذکر نہیں کیا۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔ جواب (۲): علامہ فخر الاسلام نے جو عنوان ذکر کیا اس سے ایک قاعدہ معلوم ہوا کہ لفظ کی وضع لمعنی میں بہیات اور مادہ دونوں کو دخل ہے پھر بیاہ کو مقدم کر کے اس طرف اشارہ کیا کہ اکثر حقائق معنی پر بیاہ کے واسطہ سے دلالت کرتے ہیں خصوصا امرونہی کہ دین کے اکثر احکام کا مدار انہی پر ہیں اور یہ بات ظاہر ہے کہ ان کا امر و نہی ہونا ہیاۃ اور شکل کے اعتبار سے ہے مادہ تو ان کے درمیان اور ان کے غیر میں برابر تحقق ہوتا ہے خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ اگر فخر الاسلام لفظ وضع پر اکتفاء کرتے اور یہ عنوان ذکر نہ کرتے تو یہ فوائد ولطائف معلوم نہ ہوتے ۔واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔ و عبرعن القسم الثانی:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے ر شارع الام فخرالاسلام کی قسیم ثانی کے عنوان ور تعبیر و
The word does not indicate its meaning except through the coinage of matter (mādah) and form (hayʾah). So he (Fakhr al-Islam) expressed it by mentioning both instead of the word waḍʿ (coinage). And he expressed the second division with his statement: 'fī wujūh istiʿmāl dhālika al-ʿaẓīm wa jarayānihi fī bāb al-bayān' – i.e., concerning the ways of using the word in its meaning, carrying it upon that: if its meaning is used in what it was coined for, then it is ḥaqīqah; or if used in other than that, then it is majāz. Or concerning the ways of giving effect to meaning and its expression: if it is by way of clarity then it is ṣarīḥ, or by way of concealment (purdah) then it is kināyah. And the third division he expressed with his statement: 'fī wujūh al-bayān bi-dhālika al-ʿaẓīm' – i.e., concerning the ways of expressing meaning and its levels. And the fourth division he expressed with his statement: 'fī maʿrifatihi wujūh al-wuqūf ʿalā al-murād wa al-maʿānī' – i.e., concerning the knowledge of the ways by which the listener gains awareness of the meanings of speech and the intent of the speaker: whether he becomes aware by way of ʿibārat al-naṣṣ, or by way of ishārat al-naṣṣ, or other than both.

The titles and expressions of Fakhr al-Islam's four divisions.
Commentary: His statement 'wa hādhā mā qāla': This is the first part of the commentary's expression. The commentator mentions the expression and title stated by Fakhr al-Islam regarding the first division and explains its meaning. The summary is that Fakhr al-Islam set up the title for the first division as 'al-awwal fī wujūh al-naẓm ṣīghah wa lughah'. Here 'wujūh' means aspects and considerations – i.e., the first division concerns aspects of the word (al-ʿaẓīm) with respect to ṣīghah and lughah. It does not mean 'ṭuruq' (ways) because 'ṭuruq al-naẓm' has no meaning. This is the secret of the commentator's silence regarding the first division and his interpreting 'wujūh' as 'ṭuruq' for the remaining three divisions.

What is meant by ṣīghah and lughah? The commentator mentions two opinions.
First opinion: ṣīghah and lughah are synonymous – i.e., each word that indicates a meaning is called ṣīghah and also lughah. According to this, the first division concerns the meaning itself, not the speaker or listener.
Second opinion: ṣīghah and lughah are not synonymous but differ. ṣīghah is the form/shape that the word acquires due to its vowel points, sukūn, and the precedence of some letters over others; while lughah is the coined word itself. But here, since lughah is contrasted with ṣīghah, what is meant by it is only the matter (mādah). Therefore, the intended division is with respect to waḍʿ (coinage). The reason is that coinage applies to both matter and form – just as the coiner (wāḍiʿ) coined the letters of ḍaraba for a specific meaning, so too he coined its form for the meaning of past tense. Thus a word's indication of meaning comes through two things: (1) coinage of matter, (2) coinage of form. So when both are integral to coinage, both are mentioned to refer to coinage. Thus Fakhr al-Islam did this: he mentioned ṣīghah (form) and lughah (matter) to mean coinage.

Question: Since the purpose of the title 'ṣīghah wa lughah' is the division of the word from the perspective of coinage for meaning (waḍʿ al-maʿnā), why did Fakhr al-Islam not express it as 'waḍʿ li al-maʿnā' – especially since that would be more concise?

Answer (1): Before understanding the answer, a premise is necessary: There are two types of waḍʿ (coinage): (1) personal coinage (waḍʿ shakhṣī) – assigning a word to a specific meaning; (2) generic coinage (waḍʿ nawʿī) – which is of two kinds. First: establishing a rule or principle that every word characterized by a certain quality will indicate a specific meaning – e.g., saying: 'Every plural form that is definite with alif lām indicates every individual of its referents.' Second: stating a rule that every word coined for a specific meaning, when there is a qarīnah ṣārifa (indicator diverting from that meaning), will indicate a specific related meaning. This second kind of generic coinage falls under majāz because the word departs from its original meaning.

Essentially, when the word waḍʿ is mentioned absolutely, the third kind (generic coinage of the second type) is not intended because it is deficient relative to the first two. However, the first two can be intended, but one might mistakenly think that the second type is not intended because it is deficient compared to the first. To remove this misapprehension, Fakhr al-Islam did not use the word waḍʿ. And Allah knows best.

Answer (2): From the title chosen by Fakhr al-Islam, we learn a principle: that both form and matter are involved in the coinage of a word for its meaning. Then, by placing 'ṣīghah' (form) first, he indicated that most realities (ḥaqāʾiq) indicate meaning through form – especially commands and prohibitions, upon which most of the rulings of the religion are based. It is evident that these are command and prohibition due to form; matter is found equally between them and others. In summary, if Fakhr al-Islam had sufficed with the word waḍʿ and not stated this title, these benefits and subtleties would not be known. And Allah knows best.

'And he expressed the second division...' This is the second part of the commentary's expression, and the second division's title is...
Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from Al-Tarwīḥ on a subtle point of usul al-fiqh terminology. The commentator explains why Fakhr al-Islam (a Hanafi authority) chose the phrase 'ṣīghah wa lughah' (form and lexeme) for the first division of words, instead of simply saying 'waḍʿ li al-maʿnā' (coinage for meaning). The commentator first clarifies that the word 'wujūh' in the title means 'aspects' not 'ways,' and that ṣīghah and lughah together refer to the dual components of linguistic coinage: the form (hayʾah) and the matter (mādah). Two opinions are given about the relationship between these terms: some consider them synonymous, both meaning 'word'; the more precise view distinguishes them: ṣīghah is the morphological form (e.g., the pattern of vowels and letters), while lughah is the lexical root. Since coinage (waḍʿ) involves both the root and the pattern, mentioning both is necessary to capture the full picture.

Then a question arises: why not just use 'waḍʿ'? The commentator gives two answers. The first is based on the types of waḍʿ: personal (shakhṣī) and generic (nawʿī). Generic coinage includes both a rule for direct indication and a rule for indirect (majāz) indication. Using 'waḍʿ' alone could cause confusion – one might think only the first kind (personal) or only the second kind (generic direct) is meant, or one might mistakenly include the indirect kind which is actually deficient. So Fakhr al-Islam avoided the term.

The second answer is pedagogical: by explicitly mentioning both form and matter, and placing form first, he highlights that most legal realities (especially commands and prohibitions) are conveyed through form, not just root matter. This teaches a principle of usul that the form of a word is crucial for deriving rulings.

Thus, this passage is a model of Hanafi terminological precision and the importance of clarity in legal definitions.

Key Terms
صيغة (ṣīghah): The form or shape of a word, considering its voweling (ḥarakāt, sukūn) and order of letters.
لغة (lughah): The coined word itself, but here specifically the root matter (mādah) in contrast to form.
وضع شخصي (waḍʿ shakhṣī): Assigning a specific word to a specific meaning.
وضع نوعي (waḍʿ nawʿī): Establishing a general rule that certain word patterns indicate specific meanings, or that words with a qarīnah indicate a different meaning (majāz).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason Fakhr al-Islam avoided the term 'waḍʿ' in the first division title?
A) To be more concise.
B) Because 'waḍʿ' alone could be misunderstood to include the deficient type of generic coinage (majāz).
C) To emphasize that lughah is more important than ṣīghah.
D) Because 'waḍʿ' is not a technical term in usul.

Key Takeaway
Fakhr al-Islam’s division of lafẓ into ṣīghah and lughah highlights that word meaning derives from both morphological form and lexical root, and the explicit mention of both components is necessary to exclude ambiguous interpretations of waḍʿ.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

6 min
The Second Division: Haqiqah, Majaz, Sarih, and Kinayah
Defining the second division's categories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between haqiqah and majaz usage, and between sarih and kinayah clarity, applying these categories to a given text.

Core Idea
A composition's usage is either haqiqah or majaz; its clarity is either sarih or kinayah.

In this lesson, we explore the second division of Fakhr al-Islam's framework, which categorizes how a composition (nazm) is used—whether in its literal sense or figuratively—and how clearly it conveys its meaning. This is foundational for understanding text interpretation in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two axes
The division considers two independent aspects: usage (isti'mal) and clarity (wuduh). Usage pertains to whether the word is used literally (haqiqah) or figuratively (majaz). Clarity deals with whether the meaning is clear (sarih) or implicit (kinayah).
These axes are orthogonal; a haqiqah word can be sarih or kinayah depending on context.
2
Define haqiqah and majaz
Haqiqah is a word used in its original, lexically placed meaning. Majaz is a word used in a non-original meaning due to a connection (e.g., "lion" for a brave man).
Hanafi usul recognizes both as valid, with haqiqah being the default.
3
Define sarih and kinayah
Sarih is a word whose meaning is clear directly from its wording. Kinayah is a word that implies its meaning contextually, not directly. For example, "He has a long hand" is kinayah for generosity.
Kinayah often requires additional clues to interpret.
4
Apply to a sample
Take the Arabic word 'أسد' – if used meaning 'lion', it is haqiqah; if meaning 'brave man', it is majaz. If context makes the intended meaning obvious, it is sarih; if ambiguous, it may be kinayah.
Practice by analyzing phrases from the Qur'an and Hadith.

و عبرعن القسم الثانی: یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے ر شارع الام فخرالاسلام کی قسیم ثانی کے عنوان ور تعبیر و ذکر کرنا ہے تقسیم ثانی میں فخر الاسلام کی تعبیر یوں تھی انتقسیم الثانی فی وجوہ استعمال ذلک النظم واستعمالہ اور یہاں وجوہ سے مراد طرق ہیں اب معنی ہوگا یعنی دوسری تقسیم ان طرق کے بیان میں جس میں نظم استعمال ہوتی ہے یعنی نظم معنی موضوع لہ میں استعمال ہے تو حقیقت ور نہ مجاز اور جریانہ سے نظم کا معنی کے بیان واظہار میں جاری ہونے کے طرق مراد ہیں کہ اس کا معنی واضح ہے یا واضح نہیں ہے اگر واضح ہے تو صریح و گر نہ کنایہ ہے۔ وعن الثالث : یہ شرح کی عبارت کا تیسرا حصہ ہے اس میں فخر الاسلام کی تیسری تقسیم کا عنوان اور اس کا مفہوم بیان کیا وہ الفاظ یہ ہیں انتقسیم الثالث فی وجوہ البیان بذلک العظیم اس میں وجوہ بمعنی طرق ہے اور بیان کا مطلب معانی ہیں مطلب یہ ہے کہ تیسری تقسیم معانی کے اظہار اور مراتب کے طرق کے بیان میں ہے یہ آٹھ قسمیں بنتی ہیں۔ د عن الرابع : یہ شرح کی عبارت کا چوتھا حصہ ہے اس میں چوتھی تقسیم کا عنوان اور معنی و مفہوم ذکر کیا ہے اور چوتھی تقسیم کے الفاظ یہ ہیں التقسيم الرابع في وجود الوقوف على المرادوجوہ بمعنی طرق الوقوف سے مراد اطلاع سامع یعنی چوتھی تقسیم سامع کی متکلم کی مراد پر اطلاع پانے کے اعتبار سے ہے کہ سامع عبارت النص سے اطلاع پا رہا ہے یا اشارۃ النص سے یا دلالتہ النص سے یا اقتضاء النص. سے۔
And passing to the second division: This is the second part of the commentary. It mentions the title and explanation of the second division of Fakhr al-Islam. In the second division, Fakhr al-Islam's expression was: 'The second division concerns the modes (wujuh) of using that composition (nazm) and its usage.' Here 'wujuh' means modes. So the meaning is: the second division is about the modes in which the composition is used—whether the composition is used in its original meaning (haqiqah) or not (majaz), and through its usage, the modes of the composition's manifestation and clarification of meaning are meant: whether its meaning is clear (sarih) or not (kinayah). And concerning the third: This is the third part of the commentary. It explains the title and meaning of Fakhr al-Islam's third division. The words are: 'The third division concerns the modes of bayan by that great [Qur'an].' Here 'wujuh' means modes, and 'bayan' means meanings. The meaning is that the third division is about the modes of expressing meanings and their levels. It comprises eight types. And concerning the fourth: This is the fourth part of the commentary. It explains the title and meaning of the fourth division. The words of the fourth division are: 'The fourth division concerns the ways of stopping (wuquf) at what is intended.' 'Wujuh' means modes; 'wuquf' means the listener's access. So the fourth division is from the perspective of the listener's access to the speaker's intent: whether the listener accesses through ibarat al-nass, isharat al-nass, dalalat al-nass, or iqtida' al-nass.
Source pages p. 496

Commentary
This passage explains three successive divisions from the framework of Fakhr al-Islam. The second division categorizes the usage (isti'mal) of a composition (nazm) as either haqiqah (literal) or majaz (figurative), and further as sarih (clear) or kinayah (implicit). The third division concerns the modes of bayan (expression of meaning) and its levels, which the commentator notes consist of eight types (likely referring to the well-known eight categories of bayan in Hanafi usul, such as 'ibarah, isharah, dalalah, iqtida', etc.). The fourth division shifts perspective to the listener (sam'), describing how the listener grasps the speaker's intent through four well-known methods: ibarat al-nass (direct expression), isharat al-nass (indication), dalalat al-nass (implication), and iqtida' al-nass (requirement). This is standard Hanafi taxonomy.

Key Terms
حقيقة (ḥaqīqah): Literal meaning; a word used in its originally placed meaning.
مجاز (majāz): Figurative meaning; a word used in a meaning other than its original due to a connection.
صريح (ṣarīḥ): Clear, explicit; a word whose meaning is evident from its wording without need for context.
كناية (kināyah): Implicit, allusive; a word that conveys its meaning indirectly via context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which two independent aspects does the second division classify?
A) Amm and khass
B) Haqiqah/majaz and sarih/kinayah
C) Mujmal and mubayyan
D) Ibara and isharah

Key Takeaway
A composition's usage is either haqiqah or majaz; its clarity is either sarih or kinayah; these are independent axes.

The Third Division: Modes of Bayan and Their Eight Types
Defining the third division's eight types of bayan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the eight types of bayan (expression of meaning) and explain their hierarchy in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Bayan has eight levels, from clear to ambiguous, guiding how meanings are expressed and understood.

The third division explores the modes of bayan, which refer to how meanings are expressed in texts. The commentator notes that these modes are eight types, likely referring to the well-known hierarchy in Hanafi usul: from the clearest (ibarat al-nass) to the most ambiguous. Understanding these levels is crucial for usul al-fiqh reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Understand the term bayan
Bayan literally means 'clarification' or 'expression'. In this division, it refers to the modes by which a text conveys meaning. The division examines these modes in terms of clarity and strength.
Do not confuse with the later fourth division which shifts to the listener's perspective.
2
Note the eight types
The text explicitly states that the third division comprises eight types. In Hanafi usul, these are typically: ibarat al-nass, isharat al-nass, dalalat al-nass, iqtida' al-nass, and further subdivisions. The exact list varies by scholar.
The source does not enumerate them; we will focus on the concept of a hierarchy.
3
Relate to the fourth division
The fourth division's four modes (ibarah, isharah, dalalah, iqtida') are often considered part of this eightfold classification. The remaining four may include types like 'tanbih al-nass' or 'mafhum', etc.
In advanced study, you will memorize the eight; here, recognize the system.
4
Apply the hierarchy
When interpreting a text, identify which mode of bayan is used. For example, the most explicit is ibarat al-nass, which gives a clear ruling. Less explicit modes require more reasoning.
Practice by classifying a few Qur'anic verses into these modes (e.g., c2:275 for ibarat).

The Fourth Division: The Listener's Access to the Speaker's Intent
Defining the fourth division's four modes of listener access

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and differentiate the four modes of listener's access to textual meaning: ibarat al-nass, isharat al-nass, dalalat al-nass, and iqtida' al-nass.

Core Idea
A listener understands the speaker's intent through four channels: direct expression, indication, implication, and requirement.

The fourth division examines how the listener (sam') acquires knowledge of the speaker's intent. The text identifies four distinct modes: ibarat al-nass (direct wording), isharat al-nass (indication from context), dalalat al-nass (implication by logical necessity), and iqtida' al-nass (requirement for validity). These categories are fundamental in Hanafi usul for analyzing the dalalat (indications) of a text.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the listener's perspective
Unlike the earlier divisions that focus on the text itself or the speaker, the fourth division looks at how the listener (or interpreter) arrives at the intended meaning. It is about access (wuquf).
Wuquf means 'stopping' at comprehension.
2
List the four modes
The text lists: ibarat al-nass, isharat al-nass, dalalat al-nass, iqtida' al-nass. Memorize these in order of strength.
They are sometimes called the four 'dalalat al-nass' categories.
3
Define each mode
Ibarat: direct meaning from wording; Isharah: implied meaning from context; Dalalah: necessary logical implication; Iqtida': a condition required for the statement to hold.
Each has specific conditions and effects.
4
Apply to an example
Use the verse 'فمن شهد منكم الشهر فليصمه' (2:185). Ibarat: fasting is obligatory for those who witness the month. Isharah: travelers are exempt. Dalalah: if one is too ill to fast, it implies permission to break. Iqtida': the obligation is contingent on ability and presence.
Practice with other verses.

Commentary
This passage explains three successive divisions from the framework of Fakhr al-Islam. The second division categorizes the usage (isti'mal) of a composition (nazm) as either haqiqah (literal) or majaz (figurative), and further as sarih (clear) or kinayah (implicit). The third division concerns the modes of bayan (expression of meaning) and its levels, which the commentator notes consist of eight types (likely referring to the well-known eight categories of bayan in Hanafi usul, such as 'ibarah, isharah, dalalah, iqtida', etc.). The fourth division shifts perspective to the listener (sam'), describing how the listener grasps the speaker's intent through four well-known methods: ibarat al-nass (direct expression), isharat al-nass (indication), dalalat al-nass (implication), and iqtida' al-nass (requirement). This is standard Hanafi taxonomy.

Key Terms
عبارة النص (‘ibārat al-naṣṣ): The direct expression of the text conveying its primary meaning.
اشارة النص (ishārat al-naṣṣ): The indication of the text; a meaning implied by the context or arrangement.
دلالة النص (dalālat al-naṣṣ): The implication of the text; a meaning derived by logical necessity.
اقتضاء النص (iqtidā’ al-naṣṣ): The requirement of the text; something not stated but necessary for the text to be valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
