Definitions of Mushtarak and 'Aam
Defining mushtarak and 'aam in the first division

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify mushtarak and 'aam based on their definitions and apply the conditions to classify words.

Core Idea
A word's placement for meaning determines its usul category: mushtarak (multiple placements) vs 'aam (single placement for unrestricted many).

This lesson introduces the first division of words in Hanafi usul: mushtarak (homonym) and 'aam (general). Understanding these definitions is foundational for interpreting legal texts. We will parse the precise conditions that distinguish 'aam from similar terms like indefinite plurals and numerals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories in the first division
The passage divides words based on placement: mushtarak for multiple placements, and 'aam for a single placement for many unrestricted.
2
Understand the definition of mushtarak
A word placed for several distinct meanings with separate placements, like 'ayn (eye, gold, scale tongue).
Mushtarak requires multiple independent wad' acts.
3
Understand the definition of 'aam
A word placed with one placement for a many that is unrestricted (ghayr mahsur) and encompasses all applicable individuals.
Key conditions: single placement, many, unrestricted, encompassment.
4
Parse the exclusions in the definition
The definition explicitly excludes mushtarak, proper nouns (e.g., Zayd), numerals (e.g., mi'ah), and indefinite plurals (e.g., rijal).
Each clause eliminates a category that might be confused with 'aam.
5
Apply to examples
Practice classifying words as mushtarak, 'aam, or other by checking the conditions.
Use the criteria systematically.

التَّقْسِيمُ الْأَوَّلُ ) أى الَّذِى بِاعْتِبَارِ وَضْعِ اللَّفْظِ لِلْمَعْنَى اللَّفْظُ إِن وُضِعَ لِلْكَثِيرِ وَضُعًا مُتَعَدِّدًا فَمُشْتَرَكْ كَالْعَيْنِ مَثَلًا وُضِعَ تَارَةً لِلْبَاصِرَةِ ، وَتَارَةً لِلذَّهَبِ ، وَتَارَةٌ لِعَيْنِ الْمِيزَانِ) أَو وَضُعًا وَاحِدًا ) أَى وُضِعَ لِلْكَثِيرِ وَضُعًا وَاحِدًا وَالكَثِيرُ غَيْرُ مَحْصُورٍ فَعَامٌ إِن اسْتَغْرَقَ جَمِيعَ مَا يَصْلُحُ لَهُ وَإِلَّا فَجَمْعٌ مُنَكَّرٌ وَنَحْوُهُ) فَالْعَامُ لَفَظَ وُضِعَ وَضُعًا وَاحِدًا لِكَثِيرٍ غَيْرِ مَحْصُورٍ ، مُسْتَغْرِقٌ جَمِيعَ مَا يَصْلُحُ لَهُ فَقَوْلُهُ وَضْعًا وَاحِدًا يُخْرِجُ الْمُشْتَرَكَ ، وَالْكَثِيرُ يُخْرِجُ مَا لَمْ يُوضَعُ لِكَثِيرٍ كَزَيْدٍ وَعَمْرٍو وَغَيْرِ مَحْصُورٍ يُخْرِجُ أَسْمَاء الْعَدَدِ ، فَإِنَّ الْمِائَةَ مَثَلًا وُضِعَتْ وَضُعًا وَاحِدًا لِلْمُكَثِيرِ وَهِيَ مُسْتَغْرِقَةٌ جَمِيعَ مَا يَصْلُحُ لَهُ لَكِنَّ الْكَثِيرَ مَحْصُورٌ ، وَقَوْلُهُ مُسْتَغْرِقْ جَمِيعَ مَا يَصْلُحُ لَهُ يُخْرِجُ الْجَمْعَ الْمُنَكَّرَ نَحْوَ رَأَيْت رِجَالًا ،
The first division—i.e., the one with consideration of the placement of the word for the meaning: A word, if placed for many with multiple placements, then it is mushtarak (homonym), like 'ayn for example: it is placed sometimes for the eye (sight), sometimes for gold, sometimes for the tongue of a scale. Or with a single placement—i.e., placed for many with a single placement, and the many are unrestricted (ghayr mahrur), then it is 'aam (general) if it encompasses all that it can apply to; otherwise it is an indefinite plural (jamm' munakkar) and the like. So 'aam is a word placed with a single placement for an unrestricted many, encompassing all that it can apply to. So his saying 'with a single placement' excludes mushtarak; 'many' excludes what is not placed for many, like Zayd and 'Amr; 'unrestricted' excludes numerals, since one hundred, for example, is placed with a single placement for many and encompasses all that it can apply to, but the many is restricted (mahrur); and his saying 'encompasses all that it can apply to' excludes the indefinite plural like 'I saw men' (ra'aytu rijaal).
Source pages p. 497

Commentary
This passage presents the first division of words according to their wad' (placement) for meaning. It defines two key terms: mushtarak (homonym) and 'aam (general). Mushtarak is a word placed for multiple distinct meanings through separate placements, like 'ayn which means eye, gold, or scale tongue. 'Aam is a word placed via a single placement for an unrestricted many (kathir ghayr mahsur) and it must encompass all individuals that it can apply to. The commentator then unpacks the definition of 'aam clause by clause: 'single placement' distinguishes it from mushtarak; 'many' distinguishes it from proper nouns like Zayd; 'unrestricted' distinguishes it from numerals like mi'ah (hundred) which are restricted (mahsur) even though they also encompass many; and 'encompassing all it can apply to' distinguishes it from indefinite plurals like rijaal (men) which do not necessarily include every man. This is standard Hanafi usul terminology: 'aam is considered qat'i (definitive) in the absence of takhsis, unlike the Shafi'i view that 'aam is zanni. The text here does not mention that debate but sets the definition clearly.

Key Terms
مشترك (mushtarak): A word placed for multiple meanings with separate placements.
عام (‘āmm): A word placed with a single placement for an unrestricted many, encompassing all individuals it can apply to.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Which of the following is an example of 'aam according to the definition?
A) 'Ayn (eye/gold/scale)
B) Zayd (proper name)
C) Mi'ah (hundred)
D) Al-nas (the people)

Key Takeaway
A word is 'aam only if it is placed with a single placement for an unrestricted many and encompasses all applicable individuals.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
The First Division of Lafz: Mushtarak, 'Amm, and Khass based on Wad'
Defines the first division of lafz based on wad' for meaning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and classify a word as mushtarak, 'amm, jam' munakkar, or khass based on its wad' characteristics, and explain the intermediate status of jam' munakkar according to Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
A word's legal scope depends on how it was assigned: one assignment to many unlimited gives 'amm; multiple assignments give mushtarak; one assignment to one gives khass.

This passage introduces the foundational division of words in Hanafi usul al-fiqh based on the nature of their linguistic assignment (wad'). Understanding this division is crucial for correctly interpreting legal texts and determining whether a word carries general ('amm) or specific (khass) force. The commentary clarifies subtle distinctions, especially the intermediate category of the indefinite plural (jam' munakkar), which is a point of scholarly difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Basis of Division
Recognize that the division is based on wad' (linguistic assignment) for meaning. The word is considered in terms of how it was assigned: to many or to one, and whether the assignment is single or multiple.
This is the first division mentioned in the text; there are other divisions later.
2
Distinguish Mushtarak from 'Amm
If the word is assigned to many with multiple distinct assignments (wad' muta'addid), it is mushtarak (homonym), e.g., 'ayn. If assigned to many with a single assignment (wad' wahid) and the many are unlimited (ghayr mahsur), it is 'amm (general), provided it encompasses all it is suitable for.
Mushtarak has multiple meanings; 'amm has one meaning covering many individuals.
3
Understand the Conditions for 'Amm and Jam' Munakkar
For 'amm, three conditions: single assignment, many unlimited, comprehensiveness (istighraq). The commentary explains that if comprehensiveness is absent, the word is a jam' munakkar (indefinite plural) like 'ra'aytu rijālan'. Jam' munakkar is intermediate between khass and 'amm according to most Hanafis.
The passage discusses a dispute: some scholars consider jam' munakkar general, but the Hanafi view denies this.
4
Identify Khass and Mu'awwal
If the word is assigned to a single individual (like Zayd) or a single type (like 'rajul'), it is khass. Also, limited plurals (numbers, dual) are khass because the many are restricted. Then, mushtarak may become mu'awwal when a meaning is chosen by ijtihad (ra'y), but this is not part of the wad' division.
Mu'awwal is excluded from the original division because it depends on the mujtahid, not on the original assignment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التَّقْسِيمُ الْأَوَّلُ ) أَى الَّذِى بِاعْتِبَارِ وَضْعِ اللَّفْظِ لِلْمَعْنَى اللَّفْظُ إِن وُضِعَ لِلْكَثِيرِ وَضُعًا مُتَعَدِّدًا فَمُشْتَرَكْ كَالْعَيْنِ مَثَلًا وُضِعَ تَارَةً لِلْبَاصِرَةِ ، وَتَارَةً لِلذَّهَبِ ، وَتَارَةٌ لِعَيْنِ الْمِيزَانِ) أَو وَضُعًا وَاحِدًا ) أَى وُضِعَ لِلْكَثِيرِ وَضُعًا وَاحِدًا وَالكَثِيرُ غَيْرُ مَحْصُورٍ فَعَامٌ إِن اسْتَغْرَقَ جَمِيعَ مَا يَصْلُحُ لَهُ وَإِلَّا فَجَمْعٌ مُنَكَّرٌ وَنَحْوُهُ) فَالْعَامُ لَفَظَ وُضِعَ وَضُعًا وَاحِدًا لِكَثِيرٍ غَيْرِ مَحْصُورٍ ، مُسْتَغْرِقٌ جَمِيعَ مَا يَصْلُحُ لَهُ فَقَوْلُهُ وَضْعًا وَاحِدًا يُخْرِجُ الْمُشْتَرَكَ ، وَالْكَثِيرُ يُخْرِجُ مَا لَمْ يُوضَعُ لِكَثِيرٍ كَزَيْدٍ وَعَمْرٍو وَغَيْرِ مَحْصُورٍ يُخْرِجُ أَسْمَاء الْعَدَدِ ، فَإِنَّ الْمِائَةَ مَثَلًا وُضِعَتْ وَضُعًا وَاحِدًا لِلْمُكَثِيرِ وَهِيَ مُسْتَغْرِقَةٌ جَمِيعَ مَا يَصْلُحُ لَهُ لَكِنَّ الْكَثِيرَ مَحْصُورٌ ، وَقَوْلُهُ مُسْتَغْرِقْ جَمِيعَ مَا يَصْلُحُ لَهُ يُخْرِجُ الْجَمْعَ الْمُنَكَّرَ نَحْوَ رَأَيْت رِجَالًا ، وَهَذَا مَعْنَى قَوْلِهِ وَإِلَّا فَجَمْعٌ مُنَكَّرٌ أَى : وَإِنْ لَمْ يَسْتَغْرِقْ جَمِيعَ مَا يَصْلُحُ لَهُ ، وَقَوْلُهُ وَنَحْوُهُ ، مِثل رَأَيْت جَمَاعَةٌ مِنْ الرِّجَالِ فَعَلَى قَوْل مَنْ لا يَقُولُ بعُمُوم الْجَمْعِ الْمُنكَرِ يَكُونُ الْجَمْعُ الْمُنَكَّرُ وَاسِطَةٌ بَيْنَ الْخَاصٌ وَالْعَامِّ عَلَى قَوْلِ مَنْ يَقُولُ بِعُمُومِهِ يُرَادُ بِالْجَمْعِ الْمُنَكَّرِ هَاهُنَا الْجَمْعُ الْمُنَكَّرُ الَّذِي تَدُلُّ الْقَرِينَةُ عَلَى أَنَّهُ غَيْرُ عَامٌ ، فَإِنَّ هَذَا يَكُونُ وَاسِطَةٌ بَيْنَ الْعَامٌ ، وَالْخَاصٌ نَحْوَ رَأَيْت الْيَوْمَ رِجَالًا فَإِنَّ مِنْ الْمَعْلُومِ أَنَّ جَمِيعَ الرِّجَالِ غَيْرُ مَرُنِيٍّ [؟] . ( وَإِنْ كَانَ ) أَى : الْكَثِيرُ) مَحْصُورًا) كَالْعَدَدِ وَالتَّثْنِيَةِ ( أَوْ وُضِعَ لِلْوَاحِدِ فَخَاصٌ ) سَوَاءٌ كَانَ الْوَاحِدُ بِاعْتِبَارِ الشَّخْصِ كَزَيْدٍ ، أَوْ بِاعْتِبَارِ النَّوْعِ كَرَجُلٍ وَفَرَسٍ ( ثُمَّ الْمُشْتَرَكَ إِنْ تُرْجَحَ بَعْضُ مَعَانِيهِ بِالرَّأْي يُسَمَّى مُؤَوَّلًا ) وَأَصْحَابُنَا قَسَّمُوا اللَّفْظَ بِاعْتِبَارِ الصِّيغَةِ ، وَاللُّغَةِ أَى بِاعْتِبَارِ الْوَضْعِ عَلَى الْخَاصٌ وَالْعَامِّ ، وَالْمُشْتَرَكِ وَالْمُزَوَّلِ [؟] ، وَإِنَّمَا لَمْ أُورِدُ الْمُؤَوَّلَ فِي الْقِسْمَةِ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ لَيْسَ بِاعْتِبَارِ الْوَضْعِ ، بَلْ بِاعْتِبَارِ رَأْيِ الْمُجْتَهِدِ .
The first division — i.e., that which concerns the assignment of the word to meaning. The word, if assigned to many with multiple assignments, it is mushtarak, like 'ayn, for example, assigned sometimes to the eye, sometimes to gold, and sometimes to the eye of a scale. Or with a single assignment — i.e., assigned to many with a single assignment, and the many are unlimited: then it is 'amm if it encompasses all that it is suitable for; otherwise it is a indefinite plural (jam' munakkar) and the like. So 'amm is a word assigned with a single assignment to many unlimited individuals, encompassing all that it is suitable for. His saying 'with a single assignment' excludes mushtarak; 'the many' excludes what was not assigned to many like Zayd and 'Amr; 'unlimited' excludes number terms, for example, a hundred is assigned with a single assignment to many and encompasses all that it is suitable for, but the many are limited. His saying 'encompassing all that it is suitable for' excludes the indefinite plural, like 'ra'aytu rijālan' (I saw men). And this is the meaning of his saying 'otherwise it is a indefinite plural' — i.e., if it does not encompass all that it is suitable for. And his saying 'and the like' — like 'ra'aytu jamā'atan min al-rijāl' (I saw a group of men). According to the one who does not hold the generality of the indefinite plural, the indefinite plural is an intermediate between the specific and the general; according to the one who holds its generality, what is meant here by the indefinite plural is the indefinite plural that the context indicates is not general, for this is an intermediate between the general and the specific, like 'ra'aytu al-yawma rijālan' (I saw men today) — for it is known that all men are not seen. (And if it — i.e., the many — is limited, like numbers and the dual, or if it is assigned to one, it is specific (khāss), whether the one is a specific individual like Zayd or a generic type like 'man' and 'horse'. Then mushtarak: if some of its meanings are preferred by ra'y (personal reasoning), it is called 'mu'awwal'. And our companions divided the word by form and language — i.e., by assignment — into specific, general, common, and mu'awwal? [قرينة؟]. And I did not include mu'awwal in the division, because it is not due to assignment but due to the opinion of the mujtahid.
Source pages p. 497

Commentary
This passage presents the first division of lafz (word) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh based on wad' (linguistic assignment) for meaning. The commentator expands on the matn. The division considers whether the word is assigned to many or one. If assigned to many with multiple different assignments (wad' muta'addid), it is mushtarak (homonym), like 'ayn which can mean eye, gold, or scale pointer. If assigned to many with a single assignment (wad' wahid), it may be: (a) 'amm (general) if the many are unlimited (ghayr mahsur) and the word encompasses all individuals it is suitable for, e.g., 'al-nas' (people); (b) if it does not encompass all, it is a jam' munakkar (indefinite plural), like 'rijalan' (men) without qualification. The commentator clarifies that according to scholars who deny the generality of indefinite plurals, such a plural is intermediate between khass and 'amm; according to those who affirm its generality, the indefinite plural here is restricted by context (qarina) to be non-general. If the many are limited (mahsur) like numbers (e.g., 'mi'a' = hundred) or duals, or if the word is assigned to one (specific individual like Zayd or generic type like 'rajul'), then it is khass (specific). Finally, mushtarak may become mu'awwal (interpreted) if one meaning is preferred by ra'y (personal reasoning of the mujtahid). The Hanafis (our imams) divided lafz by form and language into khass, 'amm, mushtarak, and mu'awwal — but mu'awwal is excluded from this division because it is based on ijtihad, not on original wad'.

Key Terms
مشترك (mushtarak): A word assigned to multiple meanings with multiple distinct assignments, e.g., 'ayn.
عام ('amm): A word assigned with a single assignment to many unlimited individuals, encompassing all it is suitable for.
جمع منكر (jam' munakkar): An indefinite plural that does not encompass all individuals suitable; a middle category between khass and 'amm.
خاص (khass): A word assigned to a single individual (e.g., Zayd) or a single type (e.g., 'man'), with limited or single denotation.
مؤول (mu'awwal): A mushtarak word whose meaning is chosen by a mujtahid's ra'y, not by wad'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a correct statement?
A) Mushtarak is a word with a single assignment to many.
B) Jam' munakkar is an intermediate category between khass and 'amm.
C) Numbers like 'mi'a' (hundred) are 'amm because they refer to many.
D) Mu'awwal is included in the division based on wad'.

Key Takeaway
The division of lafz by wad' into mushtarak, 'amm, khass, and mu'awwal is the foundation for interpreting legal texts: the scope of a word determines the scope of the ruling.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
Definition and Conditions of 'Amm in Hanafi Usul
Classification of words by form and scope in Hanafi usul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'amm according to Hanafi usul, identify its four conditions, and distinguish it from indefinite plural, khass, mushtarak, and mu'awwal.

Core Idea
A general word requires single coinage for multiple unrestricted individuals and must encompass all it can apply to.

Not every word that refers to multiple things is 'amm (general). The Hanafi school imposes strict conditions: single coinage (wad' wahid), for multiple unlimited individuals (kathir ghayr mahsur), and encompassing all potential referents (istighraq). This lesson breaks down the definition, contrasts it with other word categories like indefinite plural, and explains why the indefinite plural is not automatically 'amm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four-part word classification in Hanafi usul
The passage divides words based on coinage (wad') into khass (particular), 'amm (general), mushtarak (common), and mu'awwal (interpreted). Mu'awwal is not part of the basic division because it depends on ijtihad, not coinage.
Hanafi classification differs from some other schools; memorize these four categories.
2
Parse the definition of 'amm
The definition is: 'a word coined with a single coinage for multiple unrestricted individuals, encompassing all that it can apply to.' Break down each element: single coinage excludes mushtarak; multiple excludes khass; unrestricted excludes limited plurals like numbers; encompassing all excludes indefinite plural.
The condition 'mustaghriq li-jami' ma yasluh lahu' is critical.
3
Examine the condition of istighraq (encompassing all)
A word is 'amm only if it covers every individual that can fall under its meaning. For example, 'al-rijal' (the men) is 'amm because it includes all men. If a word does not cover all, like 'rijalan' (men, indefinite), it is not 'amm.
This distinguishes 'amm from indefinite plural.
4
Distinguish indefinite plural as an intermediate category
The indefinite plural (جمع منكر) like 'rijalan' is not 'amm; it is an intermediate between khass and 'amm. In Hanafi view, it does not automatically indicate generality; context (qarina) may specify it, but by itself it is not general.
This is a key Hanafi position.
5
Understand the dispute over the indefinite plural
Some scholars (e.g., Shafi'i) hold that indefinite plurals are general by their form. Hanafis argue that without context, they do not encompass all. The practical consequence: in legal texts, a phrase like 'saw men' does not prove all men were seen.
This affects how legal rules are derived from such phrases.

Source Text

وَهَذَا مَعْنَى قَوْلِهِ وَإِلَّا فَجَمْعٌ مُنَكَّرٌ أَى : وَإِنْ لَمْ يَسْتَغْرِقْ جَمِيعَ مَا يَصْلُحُ لَهُ ، وَقَوْلُهُ وَنَحْوُهُ ، مِثل رَأَيْت جَمَاعَةٌ مِنْ الرِّجَالِ فَعَلَى قَوْل مَنْ لا يَقُولُ بعُمُوم الْجَمْعِ الْمُنكَرِ يَكُونُ الْجَمْعُ الْمُنَكَّرُ وَاسِطَةٌ بَيْنَ الْخَاصٌ وَالْعَامِّ عَلَى قَوْلِ مَنْ يَقُولُ بِعُمُومِهِ يُرَادُ بِالْجَمْعِ الْمُنَكَّرِ هَاهُنَا الْجَمْعُ الْمُنَكَّرُ الَّذِي تَدُلُّ الْقَرِينَةُ عَلَى أَنَّهُ غَيْرُ عَامٌ ، فَإِنَّ هَذَا يَكُونُ وَاسِطَةٌ بَيْنَ الْعَامٌ ، وَالْخَاصٌ نَحْوَ رَأَيْت الْيَوْمَ رِجَالًا فَإِنَّ مِنْ الْمَعْلُومِ أَنَّ جَمِيعَ الرِّجَالِ غَيْرُ مَرُنِيٍّ . ( وَإِنْ كَانَ ) أَى : الْكَثِيرُ) مَحْصُورًا) كَالْعَدَدِ وَالتَّثْنِيَةِ ( أَوْ وُضِعَ لِلْوَاحِدِ فَخَاصٌ ) سَوَاءٌ كَانَ الْوَاحِدُ بِاعْتِبَارِ الشَّخْصِ كَزَيْدٍ ، أَوْ بِاعْتِبَارِ النَّوْعِ كَرَجُلٍ وَفَرَسٍ ( ثُمَّ الْمُشْتَرَكَ إِنْ تُرْجَحَ بَعْضُ مَعَانِيهِ بِالرَّأْي يُسَمَّى مُؤَوَّلًا ) وَأَصْحَابُنَا قَسَّمُوا اللَّفْظَ بِاعْتِبَارِ الصِّيغَةِ ، وَاللُّغَةِ أَى بِاعْتِبَارِ الْوَضْعِ عَلَى الْخَاصٌ وَالْعَامِّ ، وَالْمُشْتَرَكِ وَالْمُزَوَّلِ ، وَإِنَّمَا لَمْ أُورِدُ الْمُؤَوَّلَ فِي الْقِسْمَةِ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ لَيْسَ بِاعْتِبَارِ الْوَضْعِ ، بَلْ بِاعْتِبَارِ رَأْيِ الْمُجْتَهِدِ .
ترجمہ: یعنی وہ کہ جو لفظ کے معنی کے لیے وضع کے اعتبار سے ہے (لفظ اگر وضع کیا گیا ہو کثیر کے لیے وضع متعدد کے ساتھ پس مشترک ہے ) جیسا کہ عین مثال کے طور پر وضع کیا گیا ہے کبھی باصرہ کے لیے اور کبھی سونے کے لیے اور کبھی ترازو کے کانٹے کے لیے ۔ ( یا وضع واحد کے ساتھ ) یعنی وضع کیا گیا ہو کثیر کے لیے وضع واحد کے ساتھ ( اور وہ کثیر غیر محصور ہوں پس وہ عام ہے اگر مستغرق ہو تمام ان افراد کو جن کے لیے وہ صلاحیت رکھتا ہے وگر نہ پس وہ جمع منکر ہے اور اس کی مثل ہے ) پاس عام ایسا لفظ ہے جو وضع کیا گیا ہے وضع واحد کے ساتھ کثیر غیر محصور افراد کے لیے جو کہ مستغرق ہو تمام ان افراد کو جن کی وہ صلاحیت رکھتا ہے۔ پس اس کا قول وضع واحد ہو نکال دیتا ہے مشترک کو اور اس کا قول الکثیر نکال دیتا ہے اس لفظ کو جو کثیر کے لیے وضع نہ کیا گیا ہو۔ جیسا کہ زید اور عمرو اور اس کا قول غیر محصور خارج کر دیتا ہے اسماء عدد کو کیونکہ لفظ ملئہ مثال کے طور پر وضع کیا گیا ہے وضع واحد کے ساتھ کثیر کے لیے اور وہ مستغرق ہے جمیع بما تصلح لہ کو لیکن کثیر محصور ہیں اور اس کا قول مستغرق جمیع ، ا صلح لہ خارج کر دیتا ہے جمع منکر کو جیسے راآیت رجالا اور یہی معنی ہے اس کے قول والا جمع منکر (وگرنہ پس وہ جمع منکر ہے ) کا یعنی اور
اگر نہ ہو مستغرق جمیع ما یصلح لہ کو اور اس کا قول ونحوہ جیسا کہ رایت جماعة من الرجال ہے پس اس شخص کے قول کے مطابق جو نہیں قول کرتا جمع منکر کے عام ہونے کا ہوگا جمع منکر واسطہ عام اور خاص کے درمیان جیسے رایت الیوم رجالا ( دیکھا میں نے آج کے دن رجال کو) بے شک یقین سے یہ بات ہے کہ بے شک تمام آدمی نہیں دیکھے جاسکتے (اور اگر ہوں وہ ) یعنی کثیر محصور جیسا کہ عدد اور تثلیہ ہے یا وضع کیا گیا ہو فرد واحد کے لیے پس خاص ہے ) برابر ہے کہ واحد باعتبار شخص کے ہو جیسے زید ہے یا باعتبار نوع کے ہو جیسے رجل اور فرس ہے۔ یا باعتبار جنس کے ہو جیسے انسان ہے (پھر مشترک اگر ترجیح پا جائیں اس کے بعض معانی رائے کے ساتھ تو نام رکھا جاتا ہے مؤول ) اور ہمارے اصحاب نے تقسیم کیا ہے لفظ کو باعتبار صیغہ اور لغت کے یعنی با عتبار وضع کے خاص اور عام اور مشترک اور مؤوّل کی طرف اور سوائے اس کے نہیں کہ میں نے نہیں ذکر کیا موول کو تقسیم میں کیونکہ وہ نہیں ہے باعتبار وضع کے بلکہ باعتبار مجتہد کی رائے کے ہے۔
تقسیمات اربعہ کی تفصیل
تشریح: التقسيم الاول : تقسیمات اربعہ کو اجمالا بیان کرنے کے بعد اب تفصیلاً بیان کرتے ہیں لفظ کی پہلی تقسیم خاص و عام اور مشترک مؤوّل کی طرف ہے عام کا اصولیوں کے نزدیک اور مصنف کے ہاں فرق ہے۔
وجہ حضر : ۔ لفظ کی وضع دو حال سے خالی نہیں معنی واحد کے لیے ہوگی یا کثیر معافی کے لیے ہو گی اگر لفظ کی وضع معانی کثیرہ کے لیے ہو تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں وضع ایک ہوگی یا وضع متعدد ہو گی اگر وضع متعدد ہو تو مشترک ہے جیسے لفظ عین ہے گھٹنا ہونا ، آنکھ ترازو کے کانٹے ہر ایک کے لیے علیحدہ وضع کیا گیا ہے اور اگر وضع متعدد نہ ہو تو وہ کثیر معانی محصور ہوں گے یا غیر محصور ہوں کے یعنی متعین ہوں گے یا نہیں ؟ اگر وہ معانی غیر محصور ہوں تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں لفظ جمیع ما تصلح لہ کو مستغرق ہوگا یا نہیں؟ اگر تمام افراد کو مستغرق ہو تو عام ہے۔ اگر تمام کو مستغرق نہ ہوتو جمع منکر ہے جیسے رجال اور اگر وہ معانی محصور ہوں جیسے لفظ ملائکہ یہ خاص ہے اور اگر لفظ کی وضع ایک معنی کے لیے ہو تو بھی خاص ہے پھر ایک معنی فرد کے اعتبار سے ہو تو خاص فردی ہے۔ اور اگر ایک معنی نوع کے اعتبار سے ہو تو خاص نوعی ہے اور اگر جنس کے اعتبار سے ہو تو خاص جنسی ہے۔
فالعام : ماتن فرماتے ہیں کہ وجہ خصر سے عام کی تعریف بھی معلوم ہو گئی کہ فالعام لفظ وضع وضعا واحد الكثير غير محصور مستغرق لجميع، ا صلح رہ یعنی عام وہ لفظ ہے جو ایک وضع سے کثیر معانی کے لیے وضع کیا گیا ہو اور کثیر غیر محصور ہوں اور ان تمام افراد کا احاطہ کرنے والا ہو جن پر مشتمل ہونے کی اس میں صلاحیت ہو۔
And this is the meaning of his statement: 'otherwise it is an indefinite plural' i.e., if it does not encompass all that it can apply to. And his statement 'and the like' such as 'I saw a group of men'. According to the view of one who does not hold the indefinite plural as general, the indefinite plural is an intermediate between the particular and the general. According to the view of one who holds it as general, what is meant by the indefinite plural here is the indefinite plural which the context indicates is not general, for this becomes an intermediate between the general and the particular, like 'I saw today men' for it is known that all men were not seen. (And if it [i.e., the plural] is) limited (like a number or a dual) (or it is placed for a single, then it is particular) regardless of whether the single is in terms of person like Zayd, or in terms of type like 'man' or 'horse'. (Then the common word if some of its meanings are given preponderance by opinion, it is called interpreted) And our companions divided the word in terms of form and language i.e., in terms of coinage into particular, general, common, and interpreted. He only did not include the interpreted in the division because it is not by coinage, but by the opinion of the mujtahid. [The Urdu translation and detailed explanation follow, clarifying the division and the conditions of general.]
Source pages p. 498

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory commentary (sharh) on the original matn of Al-Tawdih, dealing with the classification of words in usul al-fiqh. The author begins by explaining the meaning of the phrase 'otherwise it is an indefinite plural' from the base text. He clarifies that an indefinite plural (جمع منكر) is not automatically general; rather, it depends on whether it encompasses all individuals it can apply to (istighraq). If it does not, it is an indefinite plural and serves as an intermediate category between particular and general. The author presents two scholarly views: some deny the generality of the indefinite plural outright, while others hold it as general but interpret context to restrict it. The passage then moves to define particular (خاص) as a word placed for a single meaning, whether an individual (like Zayd) or a type (like man or horse). Next, it discusses the common word (مشترک), which is a word coined for multiple meanings (e.g., 'ayn for eye, gold, or balance tongue). If one of its meanings is given preponderance by a mujtahid's reasoning, it becomes interpreted (مؤول). The Hanafi school (أصحابنا) divides the word into four categories: particular, general, common, and interpreted, based on coinage (وضع). The author notes that he omitted 'مؤول' from the initial division because it is not based on coinage but on ijtihad. The subsequent Urdu text expands on this by providing a detailed breakdown: a word is either for a single meaning (particular) or multiple meanings (common or general). If for multiple meanings, the coinage may be multiple (common) or single. If single, the meanings are either defined (limited, becomes particular like 'angels') or undefined. If undefined, they either encompass all applicable individuals (general) or not (indefinite plural). Finally, the passage reaffirms the definition of 'amm (general) as a word coined with a single coinage for multiple undefined individuals, encompassing all that it can apply to.

Key Terms
العام (al-ʿāmm): A word coined with a single coinage for multiple unrestricted individuals, encompassing all that it can apply to.
الخاص (al-khāṣṣ): A word coined for a single meaning, whether an individual (e.g., Zayd) or a type (e.g., man) or genus (e.g., human).
المشترك (al-mushtarak): A word coined with multiple separate coinages for different meanings, like 'ayn.
المؤول (al-mu'awwal): A mushtarak word where one meaning is given preponderance by a mujtahid's opinion (ra'y), making it interpreted.
الجمع المنكر (al-jamʿ al-munkar): An indefinite plural that does not encompass all potential referents (ghayr mustaghriq).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi division of words presented in this passage, what is the key condition for a word to be classified as 'amm (general)?
A) It must be coined for a single meaning.
B) It must be coined with multiple coinages for multiple meanings.
C) It must be coined with a single coinage for multiple unrestricted individuals and encompass all that it can apply to.
D) It must be an indefinite plural.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, 'amm is a word with single coinage for multiple unrestricted individuals covering all its potential referents; the indefinite plural is an intermediate category, not automatically general.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
The First Division of Lafz: Classification by Wad'
Explaining the fourfold division of lafz based on wad'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any lafz into khass, 'amm, mushtarak, or mu'awwal by applying the Hanafi criterion of wad' (linguistic placement) and explain why mu'awwal is not a separate category by wad'.

Core Idea
Lafz is classified by its wad': one meaning, many unlimited, many limited, or multiple wad' — mu'awwal is ijtihad, not a type.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the first step in understanding a legal text is to identify the type of word (lafz) based on its linguistic placement (wad'). This lesson unpacks the fourfold division — khass, 'amm, mushtarak, mu'awwal — and the logical reasoning (wajh hasr) that justifies this classification. Understanding these categories is essential for deriving rulings from the Qur'an and Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish single vs multiple meaning
Check if the word is placed for one meaning or many. If one, it is khass (specific). If many, proceed.
Khass includes individual (Zayd), type (rajul), genus (insān), and limited many (malā'ikah).
2
Determine number of wad' for many meanings
For many meanings, check if they are assigned by a single placement or multiple placements. If multiple, it is mushtarak. If single, proceed.
Example: 'ayn has multiple wad' (eye, knee, etc.).
3
Check if meanings are limited
If the many meanings are limited (mahsur) in number, it is khass. If unlimited, proceed.
Unlimited meaning not specified to a fixed number.
4
Check istighraq (encompassing)
If the word encompasses all individuals it can apply to (mustaghriq), it is 'amm. If not, it is jamm'e munkar (indefinite plural), which is not 'amm.
Jamm'e munkar like rijāl does not necessarily cover all men.
5
Note mu'awwal's exclusion
Mu'awwal arises when a mushtarak word is given preference by ijtihad; it is not a type by wad', so excluded from the division.
The author's division is based on wad', not ijtihad.

الترويج لحل التوضيح والتلويح
اگر نہ ہو مستغرق جمیع ما یصلح لہ کو اور اس کا قول ونحوہ جیسا کہ رایت جماعة من الرجال ہے پس اس شخص کے قول کے مطابق جو نہیں قول کرتا جمع منکر کے عام ہونے کا ہوگا جمع منکر واسطہ عام اور خاص کے درمیان جیسے رایت الیوم رجالا ( دیکھا میں نے آج کے دن رجال کو) بے شک یقین سے یہ بات ہے کہ بے شک تمام آدمی نہیں دیکھے جاسکتے (اور اگر ہوں وہ ) یعنی کثیر محصور جیسا کہ عدد اور تثلیہ ہے یا وضع کیا گیا ہو فرد واحد کے لیے پس خاص ہے ) برابر ہے کہ واحد باعتبار شخص کے ہو جیسے زید ہے یا باعتبار نوع کے ہو جیسے رجل اور فرس ہے۔ یا باعتبار جنس کے ہو جیسے انسان ہے (پھر مشترک اگر ترجیح پا جائیں اس کے بعض معانی رائے کے ساتھ تو نام رکھا جاتا ہے مؤول ) اور ہمارے اصحاب نے تقسیم کیا ہے لفظ کو باعتبار صیغہ اور لغت کے یعنی با عتبار وضع کے خاص اور عام اور مشترک اور مؤوّل کی طرف اور سوائے اس کے نہیں کہ میں نے نہیں ذکر کیا موول کو تقسیم میں کیونکہ وہ نہیں ہے باعتبار وضع کے بلکہ باعتبار مجتہد کی رائے کے ہے۔
تقسیمات اربعہ کی تفصیل
تشریح: التقسيم الاول : تقسیمات اربعہ کو اجمالا بیان کرنے کے بعد اب تفصیلاً بیان کرتے ہیں لفظ کی پہلی تقسیم خاص و عام اور مشترک مؤوّل کی طرف ہے عام کا اصولیوں کے نزدیک اور مصنف کے ہاں فرق ہے۔
وجہ حصر : ۔ لفظ کی وضع دو حال سے خالی نہیں معنی واحد کے لیے ہوگی یا کثیر معافی کے لیے ہو گی اگر لفظ کی وضع معانی کثیرہ کے لیے ہو تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں وضع ایک ہوگی یا وضع متعدد ہو گی اگر وضع متعدد ہو تو مشترک ہے جیسے لفظ عین ہے گھٹنا ہونا ، آنکھ ترازو کے کانٹے ہر ایک کے لیے علیحدہ وضع کیا گیا ہے اور اگر وضع متعدد نہ ہو تو وہ کثیر معانی محصور ہوں گے یا غیر محصور ہوں کے یعنی متعین ہوں گے یا نہیں ؟ اگر وہ معانی غیر محصور ہوں تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں لفظ جمیع ما تصلح لہ کو مستغرق ہوگا یا نہیں؟ اگر تمام افراد کو مستغرق ہو تو عام ہے۔ اگر تمام کو مستغرق نہ ہوتو جمع منکر ہے جیسے رجال اور اگر وہ معانی محصور ہوں جیسے لفظ ملائکہ یہ خاص ہے اور اگر لفظ کی وضع ایک معنی کے لیے ہو تو بھی خاص ہے پھر ایک معنی فرد کے اعتبار سے ہو تو خاص فردی ہے۔ اور اگر ایک معنی نوع کے اعتبار سے ہو تو خاص نوعی ہے اور اگر جنس کے اعتبار سے ہو تو خاص جنسی ہے۔
فالعام : ماتن فرماتے ہیں کہ وجہ حصر سے عام کی تعریف بھی معلوم ہو گئی کہ فالعام لفظ وضع وضعا واحد الكثير غير محصور مستغرق لجميع، ا صلح رہ یعنی عام وہ لفظ ہے جو ایک وضع سے کثیر معانی کے لیے وضع کیا گیا ہو اور کثیر غیر محصور ہوں اور ان تمام افراد کا احاطہ کرنے والا ہو جن پر مشتمل ہونے کی اس میں صلاحیت ہو۔

فوائد قیود : لفظ [بھنول؟] جنس ہے تمام افراد کو شامل ہے جب کہا وضع وضعا واحدا تو اس سے مشترک نکل گیا جب کثیر کہا تو اس سے اس لفظ کو نکال دیا جو ایک معنی کے لیے وضع کیا گیا ہے یعنی خاص کی ایک قسم کو نکال دیا۔ جب کہا غیر محصور تو خاص کی دوسری قسموں کو نکال دیا۔ مستغرق تجمیع ما تصلح لہ سے جمع منکر خارج ہو گیا۔
فعلى قول سے سوال مقدر کا جواب ہے۔
سوال: بعض لوگ جمع منکر کو عام کہتے ہیں اور ماتن کی تقسیم میں یہ عام سے علیحدہ اور خارج ہو گیا ہے؟
جواب:۔ اصل میں جمع منکر کے بارے میں دو مذہب ہیں (۱) عام ہے (۲) اور بعض کے نزدیک عام نہیں ہے۔ جن لوگوں کا مذہب ہے کہ جمع منکر عام میں داخل ہے ان کے نزدیک جمع منکر عام و خاص کے درمیان واسطہ تب بنتا ہے جب قرینہ ہو کہ تمام افراد پر صادق نہ آسکے مثلا رایت الیوم رجالا سارے آدمی ایک ہی دن میں نہیں دیکھے جا سکتے اب قرینہ موجود ہے کہ رجال تمام افراد کو شامل نہیں ہے۔ یہ عام و خاص کے درمیان واسطہ ہے۔ اور جن کے نزدیک جمع منکر عام میں داخل نہیں ہے ان پر اعتراض نہیں۔
ثم المشترک : ماتن کی تقسیم میں موول کا ذکر نہیں ہے دوسرے لوگوں کی تقسیم میں موول کا ذکر ہے قوم نے جو تقسیم کی ہے اس میں ہے کہ اگر بعض کو بعض پر ترجیح حاصل ہو تو مو ول ہے وگرنہ مشترک ہے۔
سوال :۔ موول کو آپ نے اپنی تقسیم میں شمار کیوں نہیں کیا ؟
جواب:۔ یہ مجتہد کے اجتہاد کا نتیجہ ہے کہ مجتہد بعض کو بعض پر ترجیح دیتا ہے اور مائن نے کہا کہ میں چونکہ لفظ کی اقسام بیان کرتا ہوں اور موول لفظ کی صفت نہیں ہے اس لیے میں نے اس تقسیم میں موول کا ذکر نہیں کیا۔
تلویح
) قَوْلُهُ التَّقْسِيمُ الأوّلُ ( اللفظ المَوْضُوعُ إِمَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ وَضْعُهُ لِكَثِيرٍ ، أَوْ لِوَاحِدٍ وَالْأَوَّلُ إِمَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ وَضَعُهُ لِلْكَثِيرِ بِوَضْعِ كَثِيرٍ أَوْ لَا ، فَإِنْ كَانَ بِوَضْعِ كَثِيرٍ فَهُوَ الْمُشْتَرَكَ وَإِلَّا فَإِمَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ الْكَثِيرُ مَحْصُورًا فِي عَدَدٍ مُعَيَّنٍ بِحَسَبِ دَلَالَةِ اللَّفْظِ أَوْ لَا ، فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ مَحْصُورًا ، فَإِنْ كَانَ اللَّفْظُ مُسْتَغْرِقًا لِجَمِيعِ مَا
The clarification of al-Tawdih and al-Talwih. If it does not encompass all that it is suitable for and his statement and similar, like 'I saw a group of men', then according to the statement of the person who does not say that the indefinite plural (jamm'e munkar) is general, the indefinite plural will be an intermediary between the general and the specific. Like 'ra'aytu al-yawma rijālan' (I saw men today). Undoubtedly it is certain that not all men can be seen. (And if they are) meaning many but limited, like a number and thulayya (?) or placed for a single individual, then it is specific. Regardless of whether the single is in terms of person like Zayd, or in terms of type like rajul and faras, or in terms of genus like insān. (Then the common (mushtarak) if some of its meanings are given preference over others by opinion, then it is called mu'awwal). And our companions have divided the word in terms of form and language, i.e., in terms of placement (wad') into specific, general, common, and mu'awwal. And it is not that I did not mention mu'awwal in the division because it is not by placement but by the mujtahid's opinion. Explanation of the four divisions. Elaboration: The first division: After concisely explaining the four divisions, now we explain in detail. The first division of the word is into specific, general, common, and mu'awwal. There is a difference between the usulis and the author regarding the general. Reason for limitation: The placement of the word is not free from two states: it will be for a single meaning or for multiple meanings. If the word's placement is for multiple meanings, then it is not free from two states: the placement is one or multiple. If the placement is multiple, then it is mushtarak, like the word 'ayn: knee, eye, pointer of a balance, each placed separately. And if the placement is not multiple, then those multiple meanings will be limited or unlimited, i.e., defined or not? If those meanings are unlimited, then it is not free from two states: the word will encompass all that it is suitable for or not? If it encompasses all individuals, then it is general. If it does not encompass all, then it is jamm'e munkar, like rijāl. And if those meanings are limited, like the word malā'ikah, then it is specific. And if the word's placement is for one meaning, then also it is specific. Then one meaning can be in terms of an individual: specific individual; or in terms of a type: specific type; or in terms of a genus: specific genus. Al-'Amm: The author says that from the reason for limitation the definition of 'amm is also known: al-'amm is a word placed with one placement for many unlimited meanings, encompassing all that it is suitable for. Benefits of the restrictions: The word is a genus including all individuals. When it said 'placed with one placement', the mushtarak is excluded. When it said 'many', the word placed for one meaning is excluded, i.e., one type of specific is excluded. When it said 'unlimited', the other types of specific are excluded. With 'encompassing all that it is suitable for', the jamm'e munkar is excluded. 'Alā qawl' is the answer to an implied question. Question: Some people call jamm'e munkar as general, but in the author's division it is separate and excluded from 'amm? Answer: Actually there are two madhhabs regarding jamm'e munkar: (1) it is general, (2) and according to some, it is not general. Those who hold that jamm'e munkar is included in 'amm, according to them jamm'e munkar becomes an intermediary between 'amm and khass when there is a qarīnah that it cannot be true for all individuals, e.g., 'ra'aytu al-yawma rijālan': all men cannot be seen in one day, so the qarīnah shows that rijāl does not include all individuals. Thus it is an intermediary between 'amm and khass. And those according to whom jamm'e munkar is not included in 'amm, there is no objection against them. Then al-Mushtarak: The author's division does not mention mu'awwal. Other people's division mentions mu'awwal. The group's division states that if some meanings are given preference over others, then it is mu'awwal, otherwise mushtarak. Question: Why did you not count mu'awwal in your division? Answer: It is the result of the mujtahid's ijtihad that the mujtahid gives preference to some meanings over others. And the author said: Since I am explaining the types of words, and mu'awwal is not a quality of the word, therefore I did not mention mu'awwal in this division. Al-Talwih: His statement: 'The first division: The placed word either its placement is for many or for one. The first is either its placement is for many by multiple placement or not. If it is by multiple placement, then it is mushtarak. Otherwise, the many either are limited in a specific number according to the word's indication or not. If not limited, then if the word encompasses all that it is suitable for...'
Source pages p. 499

Commentary
This passage is a hanafi usul al-fiqh commentary on the classification of lafz (word) into four categories: khass (specific), 'amm (general), mushtarak (ambiguous/polysemous), and mu'awwal (interpreted). The author explains the logic behind this division based on the nature of wad' (linguistic placement). The key criterion is whether the word is placed for one meaning or many. If for many, whether by multiple placements (mushtarak) or one placement. If one placement for many meanings, then those meanings are either limited (mahsur) or unlimited (ghayr mahsur). If unlimited AND the word encompasses all individuals it can apply to, it is 'amm. If it does not encompass all, it is jamm'e munkar (indefinite plural). If the many meanings are limited, it is khass. The passage then defines 'amm precisely, highlighting the restrictions that exclude mushtarak, khass, and jamm'e munkar. A common dispute is addressed: whether jamm'e munkar is 'amm or not. The Hanafi position (as per the author) is that jamm'e munkar is not 'amm, but some scholars hold it is. The passage explains that when a qarīnah (contextual indicator) prevents the indefinite plural from applying to all individuals, it becomes an intermediary between 'amm and khass. Finally, the passage clarifies why mu'awwal is not included: because it depends on ijtihad, not on the word's placement itself. The Arabic excerpt from al-Talwih reinforces the first division, aligning with the Hanafi usul tradition.

Key Terms
خاص (khass): A word placed for a single meaning, whether that meaning is an individual (zaid), a type (rajul), or a genus (insān), or for multiple limited meanings (like malā'ikah).
عام (amm): A word placed with one wad' for many unlimited meanings, encompassing all individuals it is suitable for.
مشترک (mushtarak): A word placed for multiple meanings by multiple wad' (e.g., 'ayn meaning eye, knee, etc.).
مؤوّل (mu'awwal): A mushtarak word where one meaning is given preference over others by ijtihad (mujtahid's opinion). It is not a type by wad' but by isti'mal (usage).
جمع منکر (jamm'e munkar): An indefinite plural (e.g., rijāl) that does not encompass all individuals it could apply to; it stands between 'amm and khass.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a valid criterion for a word to be classified as 'amm in the Hanafi division?
A) The word is placed for many unlimited meanings.
B) The word is placed by a single wad'.
C) The word encompasses all individuals it can apply to.
D) The word is indefinite (nakirah).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification of lafz into khass, 'amm, mushtarak, and mu'awwal is based on wad', with 'amm requiring single wad', unlimited meanings, and full encompassment of all individuals.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
The Status of Jamm'e Munkar and Mu'awwal: Key Disputes
Addressing the dispute on jamm'e munkar and exclusion of mu'awwal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why jamm'e munkar is not 'amm in the Hanafi school, evaluate the opposing view, and justify why mu'awwal is excluded from the primary division.

Core Idea
Jamm'e munkar is an intermediate category between 'amm and khass; mu'awwal is a product of ijtihad, not a linguistic type.

This lesson delves into two nuanced points from the passage: the disagreement over whether jamm'e munkar (indefinite plural) counts as 'amm, and the exclusion of mu'awwal from the fourfold division. These points highlight the Hanafi school's insistence on precise, wad'-based definitions and its awareness of practical interpretive consequences. Mastering these distinctions sharpens your ability to evaluate different usuli approaches.

Guided Path
1
Understand the qarīnah condition for jamm'e munkar
When an indefinite plural like 'rijāl' is used in a context that makes it impossible to encompass all individuals (e.g., 'I saw men today'), it becomes an intermediary between 'amm and khass. This is the author's response to those who consider jamm'e munkar as 'amm.
The qarīnah is the practical impossibility, not a linguistic marker.
2
Analyze the two madhhabs on jamm'e munkar
Some usulis consider jamm'e munkar as 'amm by default; others (including the Hanafi author) do not. The author's division excludes jamm'e munkar from 'amm, placing it as a separate category when a qarīnah prevents generality.
The dispute is about default classification, not about ruling in specific contexts.
3
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if jamm'e munkar is 'amm, it would obligate rulings for all individuals until specified; if not, it requires a qarīnah to be general, limiting the scope.
This affects interpretation of verses like 'fa rijalun' (then men) in certain contexts.
4
Understand why mu'awwal is excluded
Mu'awwal is not a type of word by wad', but a result of ijtihad on a mushtarak word. The author's division is based on wad', so mu'awwal is omitted.
Other scholars include it, but the Hanafi author argues it belongs to the mujtahid's activity, not the word's inherent classification.

اگر نہ ہو مستغرق جمیع ما یصلح لہ کو اور اس کا قول ونحوہ جیسا کہ رایت جماعة من الرجال ہے پس اس شخص کے قول کے مطابق جو نہیں قول کرتا جمع منکر کے عام ہونے کا ہوگا جمع منکر واسطہ عام اور خاص کے درمیان جیسے رایت الیوم رجالا ( دیکھا میں نے آج کے دن رجال کو) بے شک یقین سے یہ بات ہے کہ بے شک تمام آدمی نہیں دیکھے جاسکتے (اور اگر ہوں وہ ) یعنی کثیر محصور جیسا کہ عدد اور تثلیہ ہے یا وضع کیا گیا ہو فرد واحد کے لیے پس خاص ہے ) برابر ہے کہ واحد باعتبار شخص کے ہو جیسے زید ہے یا باعتبار نوع کے ہو جیسے رجل اور فرس ہے۔ یا باعتبار جنس کے ہو جیسے انسان ہے (پھر مشترک اگر ترجیح پا جائیں اس کے بعض معانی رائے کے ساتھ تو نام رکھا جاتا ہے مؤول ) اور ہمارے اصحاب نے تقسیم کیا ہے لفظ کو باعتبار صیغہ اور لغت کے یعنی با عتبار وضع کے خاص اور عام اور مشترک اور مؤوّل کی طرف اور سوائے اس کے نہیں کہ میں نے نہیں ذکر کیا موول کو تقسیم میں کیونکہ وہ نہیں ہے باعتبار وضع کے بلکہ باعتبار مجتہد کی رائے کے ہے۔
تقسیمات اربعہ کی تفصیل
تشریح: التقسيم الاول : تقسیمات اربعہ کو اجمالا بیان کرنے کے بعد اب تفصیلاً بیان کرتے ہیں لفظ کی پہلی تقسیم خاص و عام اور مشترک مؤوّل کی طرف ہے عام کا اصولیوں کے نزدیک اور مصنف کے ہاں فرق ہے۔
وجہ حصر : ۔ لفظ کی وضع دو حال سے خالی نہیں معنی واحد کے لیے ہوگی یا کثیر معافی کے لیے ہو گی اگر لفظ کی وضع معانی کثیرہ کے لیے ہو تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں وضع ایک ہوگی یا وضع متعدد ہو گی اگر وضع متعدد ہو تو مشترک ہے جیسے لفظ عین ہے گھٹنا ہونا ، آنکھ ترازو کے کانٹے ہر ایک کے لیے علیحدہ وضع کیا گیا ہے اور اگر وضع متعدد نہ ہو تو وہ کثیر معانی محصور ہوں گے یا غیر محصور ہوں کے یعنی متعین ہوں گے یا نہیں ؟ اگر وہ معانی غیر محصور ہوں تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں لفظ جمیع ما تصلح لہ کو مستغرق ہوگا یا نہیں؟ اگر تمام افراد کو مستغرق ہو تو عام ہے۔ اگر تمام کو مستغرق نہ ہوتو جمع منکر ہے جیسے رجال اور اگر وہ معانی محصور ہوں جیسے لفظ ملائکہ یہ خاص ہے اور اگر لفظ کی وضع ایک معنی کے لیے ہو تو بھی خاص ہے پھر ایک معنی فرد کے اعتبار سے ہو تو خاص فردی ہے۔ اور اگر ایک معنی نوع کے اعتبار سے ہو تو خاص نوعی ہے اور اگر جنس کے اعتبار سے ہو تو خاص جنسی ہے۔
فالعام : ماتن فرماتے ہیں کہ وجہ حصر سے عام کی تعریف بھی معلوم ہو گئی کہ فالعام لفظ وضع وضعا واحد الكثير غير محصور مستغرق لجميع، ا صلح رہ یعنی عام وہ لفظ ہے جو ایک وضع سے کثیر معانی کے لیے وضع کیا گیا ہو اور کثیر غیر محصور ہوں اور ان تمام افراد کا احاطہ کرنے والا ہو جن پر مشتمل ہونے کی اس میں صلاحیت ہو۔

فوائد قیود : لفظ [بھنول؟] جنس ہے تمام افراد کو شامل ہے جب کہا وضع وضعا واحدا تو اس سے مشترک نکل گیا جب کثیر کہا تو اس سے اس لفظ کو نکال دیا جو ایک معنی کے لیے وضع کیا گیا ہے یعنی خاص کی ایک قسم کو نکال دیا۔ جب کہا غیر محصور تو خاص کی دوسری قسموں کو نکال دیا۔ مستغرق تجمیع ما تصلح لہ سے جمع منکر خارج ہو گیا۔
فعلى قول سے سوال مقدر کا جواب ہے۔
سوال: بعض لوگ جمع منکر کو عام کہتے ہیں اور ماتن کی تقسیم میں یہ عام سے علیحدہ اور خارج ہو گیا ہے؟
جواب:۔ اصل میں جمع منکر کے بارے میں دو مذہب ہیں (۱) عام ہے (۲) اور بعض کے نزدیک عام نہیں ہے۔ جن لوگوں کا مذہب ہے کہ جمع منکر عام میں داخل ہے ان کے نزدیک جمع منکر عام و خاص کے درمیان واسطہ تب بنتا ہے جب قرینہ ہو کہ تمام افراد پر صادق نہ آسکے مثلا رایت الیوم رجالا سارے آدمی ایک ہی دن میں نہیں دیکھے جا سکتے اب قرینہ موجود ہے کہ رجال تمام افراد کو شامل نہیں ہے۔ یہ عام و خاص کے درمیان واسطہ ہے۔ اور جن کے نزدیک جمع منکر عام میں داخل نہیں ہے ان پر اعتراض نہیں۔
ثم المشترک : ماتن کی تقسیم میں موول کا ذکر نہیں ہے دوسرے لوگوں کی تقسیم میں موول کا ذکر ہے قوم نے جو تقسیم کی ہے اس میں ہے کہ اگر بعض کو بعض پر ترجیح حاصل ہو تو مو ول ہے وگرنہ مشترک ہے۔
سوال :۔ موول کو آپ نے اپنی تقسیم میں شمار کیوں نہیں کیا ؟
جواب:۔ یہ مجتہد کے اجتہاد کا نتیجہ ہے کہ مجتہد بعض کو بعض پر ترجیح دیتا ہے اور مائن نے کہا کہ میں چونکہ لفظ کی اقسام بیان کرتا ہوں اور موول لفظ کی صفت نہیں ہے اس لیے میں نے اس تقسیم میں موول کا ذکر نہیں کیا۔
تلویح
) قَوْلُهُ التَّقْسِيمُ الأوّلُ ( اللفظ المَوْضُوعُ إِمَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ وَضْعُهُ لِكَثِيرٍ ، أَوْ لِوَاحِدٍ وَالْأَوَّلُ إِمَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ وَضَعُهُ لِلْكَثِيرِ بِوَضْعِ كَثِيرٍ أَوْ لَا ، فَإِنْ كَانَ بِوَضْعِ كَثِيرٍ فَهُوَ الْمُشْتَرَكَ وَإِلَّا فَإِمَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ الْكَثِيرُ مَحْصُورًا فِي عَدَدٍ مُعَيَّنٍ بِحَسَبِ دَلَالَةِ اللَّفْظِ أَوْ لَا ، فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ مَحْصُورًا ، فَإِنْ كَانَ اللَّفْظُ مُسْتَغْرِقًا لِجَمِيعِ مَا
The clarification of al-Tawdih and al-Talwih. If it does not encompass all that it is suitable for and his statement and similar, like 'I saw a group of men', then according to the statement of the person who does not say that the indefinite plural (jamm'e munkar) is general, the indefinite plural will be an intermediary between the general and the specific. Like 'ra'aytu al-yawma rijālan' (I saw men today). Undoubtedly it is certain that not all men can be seen. (And if they are) meaning many but limited, like a number and thulayya (?) or placed for a single individual, then it is specific. Regardless of whether the single is in terms of person like Zayd, or in terms of type like rajul and faras, or in terms of genus like insān. (Then the common (mushtarak) if some of its meanings are given preference over others by opinion, then it is called mu'awwal). And our companions have divided the word in terms of form and language, i.e., in terms of placement (wad') into specific, general, common, and mu'awwal. And it is not that I did not mention mu'awwal in the division because it is not by placement but by the mujtahid's opinion. Explanation of the four divisions. Elaboration: The first division: After concisely explaining the four divisions, now we explain in detail. The first division of the word is into specific, general, common, and mu'awwal. There is a difference between the usulis and the author regarding the general. Reason for limitation: The placement of the word is not free from two states: it will be for a single meaning or for multiple meanings. If the word's placement is for multiple meanings, then it is not free from two states: the placement is one or multiple. If the placement is multiple, then it is mushtarak, like the word 'ayn: knee, eye, pointer of a balance, each placed separately. And if the placement is not multiple, then those multiple meanings will be limited or unlimited, i.e., defined or not? If those meanings are unlimited, then it is not free from two states: the word will encompass all that it is suitable for or not? If it encompasses all individuals, then it is general. If it does not encompass all, then it is jamm'e munkar, like rijāl. And if those meanings are limited, like the word malā'ikah, then it is specific. And if the word's placement is for one meaning, then also it is specific. Then one meaning can be in terms of an individual: specific individual; or in terms of a type: specific type; or in terms of a genus: specific genus. Al-'Amm: The author says that from the reason for limitation the definition of 'amm is also known: al-'amm is a word placed with one placement for many unlimited meanings, encompassing all that it is suitable for. Benefits of the restrictions: The word is a genus including all individuals. When it said 'placed with one placement', the mushtarak is excluded. When it said 'many', the word placed for one meaning is excluded, i.e., one type of specific is excluded. When it said 'unlimited', the other types of specific are excluded. With 'encompassing all that it is suitable for', the jamm'e munkar is excluded. 'Alā qawl' is the answer to an implied question. Question: Some people call jamm'e munkar as general, but in the author's division it is separate and excluded from 'amm? Answer: Actually there are two madhhabs regarding jamm'e munkar: (1) it is general, (2) and according to some, it is not general. Those who hold that jamm'e munkar is included in 'amm, according to them jamm'e munkar becomes an intermediary between 'amm and khass when there is a qarīnah that it cannot be true for all individuals, e.g., 'ra'aytu al-yawma rijālan': all men cannot be seen in one day, so the qarīnah shows that rijāl does not include all individuals. Thus it is an intermediary between 'amm and khass. And those according to whom jamm'e munkar is not included in 'amm, there is no objection against them. Then al-Mushtarak: The author's division does not mention mu'awwal. Other people's division mentions mu'awwal. The group's division states that if some meanings are given preference over others, then it is mu'awwal, otherwise mushtarak. Question: Why did you not count mu'awwal in your division? Answer: It is the result of the mujtahid's ijtihad that the mujtahid gives preference to some meanings over others. And the author said: Since I am explaining the types of words, and mu'awwal is not a quality of the word, therefore I did not mention mu'awwal in this division. Al-Talwih: His statement: 'The first division: The placed word either its placement is for many or for one. The first is either its placement is for many by multiple placement or not. If it is by multiple placement, then it is mushtarak. Otherwise, the many either are limited in a specific number according to the word's indication or not. If not limited, then if the word encompasses all that it is suitable for...'
Source pages p. 499

Commentary
This passage is a hanafi usul al-fiqh commentary on the classification of lafz (word) into four categories: khass (specific), 'amm (general), mushtarak (ambiguous/polysemous), and mu'awwal (interpreted). The author explains the logic behind this division based on the nature of wad' (linguistic placement). The key criterion is whether the word is placed for one meaning or many. If for many, whether by multiple placements (mushtarak) or one placement. If one placement for many meanings, then those meanings are either limited (mahsur) or unlimited (ghayr mahsur). If unlimited AND the word encompasses all individuals it can apply to, it is 'amm. If it does not encompass all, it is jamm'e munkar (indefinite plural). If the many meanings are limited, it is khass. The passage then defines 'amm precisely, highlighting the restrictions that exclude mushtarak, khass, and jamm'e munkar. A common dispute is addressed: whether jamm'e munkar is 'amm or not. The Hanafi position (as per the author) is that jamm'e munkar is not 'amm, but some scholars hold it is. The passage explains that when a qarīnah (contextual indicator) prevents the indefinite plural from applying to all individuals, it becomes an intermediary between 'amm and khass. Finally, the passage clarifies why mu'awwal is not included: because it depends on ijtihad, not on the word's placement itself. The Arabic excerpt from al-Talwih reinforces the first division, aligning with the Hanafi usul tradition.

Key Terms
جمع منکر (jamm'e munkar): An indefinite plural (e.g., rijāl) that does not encompass all individuals it could apply to; it stands between 'amm and khass.
قرینہ (qarīnah): A contextual indicator that specifies or clarifies the intended meaning, e.g., impossibility of encompassing all individuals in 'ra'aytu al-yawma rijālan'.
مؤوّل (mu'awwal): A mushtarak word where one meaning is given preference over others by ijtihad (mujtahid's opinion). It is not a type by wad' but by isti'mal (usage).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the author exclude mu'awwal from the first division of lafz?
A) Because mu'awwal is always synonymous with mushtarak.
B) Because mu'awwal is not based on wad' but on the mujtahid's ijtihad.
C) Because mu'awwal refers to words that are unclear and cannot be categorized.
D) Because mu'awwal is specific to Quranic usage, not general linguistic placement.

Key Takeaway
Jamm'e munkar is not automatically 'amm in Hanafi usul; it may become an intermediary with a qarīnah, while mu'awwal is excluded from the division because it depends on ijtihad, not wad'.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
12 min
Classification of Words: Mushtarak, 'Aam, Khaas, and Jam' Munkar
Defines and classifies words into four categories based on coinage and coverage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a coined word as mushtarak, 'aam, khaas, or jam' munkar according to Hanafi usul criteria.

Core Idea
Hanafi usul divides words by coinage and coverage: mushtarak has multiple coinages, 'aam covers all individuals, khaas is specific, and jam' munkar is intermediate.

This lesson unpacks the first division of coined words in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. You will learn how the author of Talwih classifies words based on whether they are coined for many meanings or one, and how coverage determines generality. A key dispute about the indefinite plural (jam' munkar) will sharpen your understanding of 'aam and khaas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main branches
Start with the basic bifurcation: is the word coined for many meanings (kathir) or for one meaning (wahid)? This determines the first split.
This is the initial decision point in the classification tree.
2
Examine the 'coined for many' branch
If coined for many, check if the coinage itself is multiple (wad' kathir) — if yes, it's mushtarak. If not, the many meanings are covered by a single coinage; then ask whether the many are confined to a specific number (mahsur) or not.
If confined to a number, it's a form of specific (khaas). If not confined, proceed to the next step.
3
Distinguish 'aam from jam' munkar
If the many are not confined, ask: does the word encompass all individuals it can apply to (mustaghriq)? If yes, it's 'aam. If no, it's jam' munkar (the indefinite plural) or similar.
This is where the dispute arises: some consider jam' munkar also as 'aam, but the author separates it.
4
Classify the 'coined for one' branch
Any word coined for a single meaning — whether a specific individual, type, or genus — falls under khaas (specific). Thus the four categories are complete.
Note that mu'awwal (interpreted word) is not a separate category here; it is a result of ijtihad, not a fixed property of the word.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فوائد قیود : لفظ بھنول جنس ہے تمام افراد کو شامل ہے جب کہا وضع وضعا واحدا تو اس سے مشترک نکل گیا جب کثیر کہا تو اس سے اس لفظ کو نکال دیا جو ایک معنی کے لیے وضع کیا گیا ہے یعنی خاص کی ایک قسم کو نکال دیا۔ جب کہا غیر محصور تو خاص کی دوسری قسموں کو نکال دیا۔ مستغرق تجمیع ما تصلح لہ سے جمع منکر خارج ہو گیا۔
فعلى قول سے سوال مقدر کا جواب ہے۔
سوال: بعض لوگ جمع منکر کو عام کہتے ہیں اور ماتن کی تقسیم میں یہ عام سے علیحدہ اور خارج ہو گیا ہے؟

ثم المشترک : ماتن کی تقسیم میں موول کا ذکر نہیں ہے دوسرے لوگوں کی تقسیم میں موول کا ذکر ہے قوم نے جو تقسیم کی ہے اس میں ہے کہ اگر بعض کو بعض پر ترجیح حاصل ہو تو مو ول ہے وگرنہ مشترک ہے۔
سوال :۔ موول کو آپ نے اپنی تقسیم میں شمار کیوں نہیں کیا ؟
جواب:۔ یہ مجتہد کے اجتہاد کا نتیجہ ہے کہ مجتہد بعض کو بعض پر ترجیح دیتا ہے اور مائن نے کہا کہ میں چونکہ لفظ کی اقسام بیان کرتا ہوں اور موول لفظ کی صفت نہیں ہے اس لیے میں نے اس تقسیم میں موول کا ذکر نہیں کیا۔

( قَوْلُهُ التَّقْسِيمُ الأوّلُ ( اللفظ المَوْضُوعُ إِمَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ وَضْعُهُ لِكَثِيرٍ ، أَوْ لِوَاحِدٍ وَالْأَوَّلُ إِمَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ وَضَعُهُ لِلْكَثِيرِ بِوَضْعِ كَثِيرٍ أَوْ لَا ، فَإِنْ كَانَ بِوَضْعِ كَثِيرٍ فَهُوَ الْمُشْتَرَكَ وَإِلَّا فَإِمَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ الْكَثِيرُ مَحْصُورًا فِي عَدَدٍ مُعَيَّنٍ بِحَسَبِ دَلَالَةِ اللَّفْظِ أَوْ لَا ، فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ مَحْصُورًا ، فَإِنْ كَانَ اللَّفْظُ مُسْتَغْرِقًا لِجَمِيعِ مَا يَصْلُحُ لَهُ مِنْ آحَادِ ذَلِكَ الْكَثِيرِ فَهُوَ الْعَامُ وَإِلَّا فَهُوَ الْجَمْعُ الْمُنَكَّرُ وَنَحْوُهُ ، وَإِنْ كَانَ مَحْصُورًا فِي عَدَدٍ مُعَيَّنٍ فَهُوَ مِنْ أَقْسَامِ الْخَاصٌ .
وَالثَّانِي وَهُوَ مَا يَكُونُ وَضْعُهُ لِوَاحِدٍ شَخْصِي أَوْ نَوْعِيٌّ أَوْ جِنْسِيِّ أَيْضًا مِنْ أَقْسَامِ الْخَاصٌ فَيَنْحَصِرُ اللَّفْظُ بِهَذَا التَّقْسِيمِ فِي الْمُشْتَرَكِ وَالْعَامِّ وَالْخَاصٌ وَالْوَاسِطَةِ بَيْنَهُمَا فَالْمُشْتَرَكَ مَا وُضِعَ لِمَعْنَى كَثِيرٍ بِوَضْعِ كَثِيرٍ وَمَعْنَى الْكَفْرَةِ مَا يُقَابِلُ الْوَحْدَةَ لَا مَا يُقَابِلُ الْقِلَّةَ فَيَدْخُلُ فِيهِ الْمُشْتَرَكْ بَيْنَ الْمَعْنَيَيْنِ فَقَط وَهَذَا التَّعْرِيفُ شَامِلٌ لِلْأَسْمَاءِ الَّتِي وُضِعَتْ أَوَّلا لِلْمَعَانِي الْجِنْسِيَّةِ ، ثُمَّ نُقِلَتْ إِلَى الْمَعَانِي الْعَلَمِيَّةِ لِمُنَاسَبَةٍ أَوْ لَا لِمُنَاسَبَةٍ ، بَلْ لِجَمِيعِ الْأَلْفَاظِ الْمَنْقُولَةِ وَالْأَلْفَاظِ الْمَوْضُوعَةِ اصْطِلاح فِى الْمَعْنَى ، وَفِي اصْطِلاح آخَرَ لِمَعُنِّى آخَرَ كَالزَّكَاةِ وَالْفِعْلِ وَالدَّوَرَانِ وَنَحْوِ ذَلِكَ وَلَيْسَتْ مِنْ الْمُشْتَرَكِ عَلَى مَا صَرَّحَ بِهِ الْبَعْضُ .
Benefits of restrictions: The word 'bhinool' is a genus covering all individuals. When it is said 'wad' wada' wahidan' then the mushtarak is excluded. When 'kathir' is said, then that word is excluded which is coined for one meaning, i.e., one category of specific is excluded. When 'ghayr mahsur' is said, the other categories of specific are excluded. 'Mustaghriq li jami' ma tasluhu lahu' excludes the jam' munkar. So 'fa'ala qawl' is the answer to an implied question. Question: Some people call the jam' munkar 'aam, but in the author's division it is separate and excluded from 'aam? Answer: Originally there are two schools regarding jam' munkar: (1) it is 'aam, (2) according to some it is not 'aam. For those who hold that jam' munkar is included in 'aam, for them jam' munkar becomes an intermediate between 'aam and specific only when there is a qarina that it cannot apply to all individuals, e.g., 'I saw men today' – all men cannot be seen in one day, so the qarina exists that 'men' does not include all individuals. This is an intermediate between 'aam and specific. And for those who hold that jam' munkar is not included in 'aam, there is no objection. Then mushtarak: In the author's division mu'awwal is not mentioned; in other people's divisions mu'awwal is mentioned. The division made by the people includes that if some meanings are given preference over others then it is mu'awwal, otherwise it is mushtarak. Question: Why did you not count mu'awwal in your division? Answer: It is the result of the mujtahid's ijtihad that the mujtahid gives preference to some over others. And the author said: Since I am explaining the types of words, and mu'awwal is not a quality of the word itself, therefore I did not mention mu'awwal in this division. His statement: The first division: The coined word is either its coinage is for many (meanings) or for one. The first: either its coinage for many is with multiple coinages or not. If with multiple coinages, then it is mushtarak. Otherwise, either those many are confined to a specific number according to the indication of the word or not. If not confined, then if the word encompasses all that it can apply to from the individuals of that many, then it is 'aam; otherwise it is jam' munkar and the like. And if they are confined to a specific number, then it is from the categories of specific. The second, and it is that which is coined for one – whether individual, specific type, or generic – is also from the categories of specific. So the word is confined in this division to mushtarak, 'aam, specific, and the intermediate between them. Thus mushtarak is that which is coined for many meanings with many coinages. The meaning of 'kathrah' is that which is opposite to singularity (wahdah), not that which is opposite to fewness (qillah). So it includes the mushtarak between only two meanings. And this definition includes the names that were first coined for generic meanings, then transferred to specific meanings with or without appropriateness; rather it includes all transferred words and words coined in one terminology for a meaning and in another terminology for another meaning, like zakah, fi'l, dawaran, and the like. And these are not from mushtarak according to the clarification of some.
Source pages p. 500

Commentary
This passage presents the first division of coined words (alfaz mawdu'a) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author categorizes words based on whether they are coined for many meanings or one, and if many, how the coinage and coverage work. The Urdu commentary first clarifies the restrictions in the classification: the phrase 'wad' wada' wahidan' excludes mushtarak; the restriction 'kathir' excludes words coined for one meaning (i.e., specific words); 'ghayr mahsur' excludes those specific words that are confined to a number; and 'mustaghriq li jami' ma tasluhu lahu' excludes jam' munkar. A key discussion follows on whether jam' munkar (indefinite plural) is considered 'aam. Two positions are noted: one school considers it 'aam, another does not. For those who include it, it becomes an intermediate ('wasita') between 'aam and specific only when a contextual clue (qarina) prevents it from covering all individuals, as in the example 'I saw men today' (since one cannot see all men in one day). The passage then addresses why mu'awwal (interpreted word) is not listed by the author: mu'awwal is a result of ijtihad, not a fixed property of the word itself. The Arabic text from Talwih then gives the formal definition: a word is either coined for many (kathir) or one (wahid). If for many, it is either with multiple coinages (mushtarak) or not. If not, the many meanings are either confined to a number (then it is specific) or not confined. If not confined, the word either covers all individuals (then it is 'aam) or does not (then it is jam' munkar). This division yields four categories: mushtarak, 'aam, specific, and the intermediate (wasita). The definition of mushtarak is refined: it must be coined for many meanings with multiple coinages, and 'kathrah' here means more than one (opposite of singularity), so even a word shared between two meanings qualifies. The definition covers transferred words and those coined differently in different technical terminologies, like zakah (which has both literal and technical meanings), but some scholars exclude such words from mushtarak.

Key Terms
المشترك (al-mushtarak): A word coined for multiple meanings with multiple coinages, e.g., 'ayn (eye, spring, etc.).
العام (al-'aam): A word that encompasses all individuals of what it can apply to within a certain category, e.g., 'al-'ulamau' (the scholars) covers all scholars.
الخاص (al-khaas): A word coined for one meaning, whether specific individual, type, or genus, e.g., 'Muhammad' for a person.
الجمع المنكر (al-jam' al-munkar): An indefinite plural that is not specified to cover all individuals, e.g., 'rijalan' (men) without definite article.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author's first division, what is the defining characteristic of mushtarak?
A) It is coined for many meanings with a single coinage.
B) It is coined for one meaning.
C) It is coined for many meanings with multiple coinages.
D) It covers all individuals of its referents.

Key Takeaway
The first division of coined words in Hanafi usul yields four categories: mushtarak, 'aam, khaas, and jam' munkar, with jam' munkar as an intermediate not always considered 'aam.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

The Division of Words and the Definition of Mushtarak
Defines mushtarak within the division of words and addresses objections regarding transferred words.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi division of words (mushtarak, 'amm, khass, wasita) and apply the defining conditions of mushtarak (wad' kathir, kathra as opposite of wahda) to classify a given word.

Core Idea
Mushtarak: a word placed for multiple meanings with multiple placements; 'multiple' means more than one, not three.

In Hanafi usul, words are classified by how they convey meaning. This lesson unpacks that taxonomy, focusing on the precise definition of mushtarak (the homonym). We'll see how the Hanafi school distinguishes mushtarak from other categories like 'amm and khass, and why a word shared between just two meanings qualifies. We'll also address a key objection about transferred words like 'zakat' or 'fi'l'.

Guided Path
1
Map the word division
Identify the four categories derived from the passage: mushtarak, 'amm, khass, and the intermediate (wasita = jam' munkar). Understand the branching logic based on wad' (placement) and ihata (coverage).
The division is based on whether the word is placed for multiple or single meanings, and whether placements are multiple or single.
2
Define mushtarak precisely
State the definition: 'ما وضع لمعنى كثير بوضع كثير' – a word placed for multiple meanings with multiple placements. Note that 'multiple (kathra)' is opposite of oneness (wahda), not paucity (qilla).
This nuance allows mushtarak to include words shared between only two meanings.
3
Understand the nuance of kathra
Contrast kathra as 'opposite of wahda' vs. 'opposite of qilla'. The former means 'more than one', the latter means 'plural (three or more)'. Hanafis adopt the former, so two meanings suffice.
4
Examine the objection regarding manqulat
The passage raises that the definition might include transferred words (manqul) like 'zakat' (from linguistic purity to obligatory charity) or 'fi'l' (from any action to the verbal noun in grammar). According to some Hanafis, these are not mushtarak because they were originally placed for one meaning and then transferred, not independently placed for each meaning.
This shows the Hanafi insistence on multiple independent placements (wad' kathir).
5
Apply the definition to sample words
Given a word like 'quru' (قرء) with two distinct meanings (menstruation and purity), classify it as mushtarak because it is placed for two meanings with two placements. Contrast with 'zakat', which is manqul and not mushtarak according to the preferred view.

جواب:۔ یہاں کثرت قلت کے مقابلہ میں نہیں بلکہ وحدت کے مقابلہ میں ہے۔ اور قلت کے مقابلہ میں کثرت کا اطلاق جمع پر ہوتا ہے اور وحدت کے مقابلہ میں ایک سے زائد افراد پر اطلاق ہوتا ہے تو دو معانی والا مشترک میں داخل ہوگا۔
کیا مشترک کی تعریف دخول غیر سے مانع نہیں ہے؟
وهذا التعریف: یہ شرح کی عبارت کا تیسرا حصہ ہے غرض اس سے اعتراض نقل کرنا ہے۔ اعتراض:۔ یہ مشترک کی تعریف دخول غیر سے مانع نہیں ہے یہ تعریف ان اسماء پر صادق آتی ہے جن کو پہلے جنس کے لیے وضع کیا گیا ہو پھر علم بنا دیا گیا ہو ۔ اسی طرح ان تمام اصطلاحات پر یہ تعریف صادق آتی ہے کہ ان کو پہلے ایک فن میں وضع کیا گیا پھر دوسرے فن کے لیے وضع کیا گیا ہو مثلاً لفظ اسر حیوان مفترس ہے اب اگر کسی کا نام رکھ دیں تو علم بن گیا یہ مشترک ہوتا
(It is suitable for it from among the individuals of that many, then it is the general; otherwise it is the indefinite plural and its like. And if it is restricted to a specific number, then it is from the divisions of the specific.) And the second: that which is placed for a single personal, specific, or generic meaning also falls under the divisions of the specific. Thus the word is confined, by this division, to the common, the general, the specific, and the intermediate between them. So the common (mushtarak) is that which is placed for multiple meanings with multiple placements. And the meaning of multiplicity (kathra) is that which is opposite to oneness (wahda), not that which is opposite to paucity (qilla). Hence the common between only two meanings enters into it. And this definition includes those nouns that were first placed for generic meanings, then transferred to specific meanings due to suitability or not, rather all transferred words and words placed for one meaning in one technical language and for another meaning in another technical language, like al-zakat, al-fi'l, al-dawaran, and the like. And they are not from the common, as some have explicitly stated.
Translation: His saying 'the first division': a word that is placed either for multiple or for a single meaning. In the first case, either it is placed for multiple meanings with multiple placements or not. If with multiple placements, then it is common; otherwise, either those multiple meanings are restricted to a specific number or not. If not restricted, then if the word encompasses all its individuals it is general, otherwise it is the indefinite plural and its like. If restricted, then it is from the divisions of the specific. The second case is that it is placed for a single meaning – either personal, specific, or generic – this too is from the divisions of the specific. So the word is confined to common, general, specific, and the intermediate, which is the indefinite plural. So the common is that which is placed for multiple meanings with multiple placements. The meaning of multiplicity is opposite to oneness, not opposite to paucity, so it includes the common between only two meanings. This definition includes those nouns first placed for generic meanings then transferred to specific meanings, with or without suitability, rather it includes all transferred words and words placed for one meaning in one technical language and another meaning in another technical language, like zakat, al-fi'l, al-dawaran, and the like. And these are not from the common, as some have explicitly stated.
Commentary: His saying 'the division' is the first part of the commentary. The commentator explains the text: a word is either for a single meaning or multiple meanings. If for multiple meanings and with multiple placements, it is common, like the word 'ayn. If with a single placement, it is either restricted or unrestricted. If unrestricted, it encompasses all its individuals or not; if it does, it's general; if not, it's indefinite plural. If restricted, it's specific. If the word is for a single meaning, it is also specific. The specific can be individual, specific (i.e., type), or generic.
Thus the summary: according to the first division there are four types: specific, general, common, and the intermediate (indefinite plural). 'Fa al-mushtarak' is the second part of the commentary, where the commentator intends to define the common: the common is a word that indicates multiple meanings with multiple placements. Objection: This definition is not comprehensive and exclusive because it excludes the common between only two meanings, since 'multiple' implies at least three. Answer: Here 'multiplicity' is opposite to oneness, not to paucity. In contrast to paucity, multiplicity applies to plural, but opposite to oneness it applies to more than one. Thus the common between two meanings enters.
Is the definition of mushtarak not exclusive (i.e., does it include non-mushtarak)? 'Wa hadha al-ta'rif' is the third part, where an objection is cited: The definition applies to those nouns that were first placed for a genus then made proper nouns, and to technical terms used in different disciplines. For example, the word 'asad' originally for a predatory animal, but if used as a name for a person, it becomes a proper noun. Are these mushtarak? The text says they are not, according to some scholars.
Source pages p. 501

Commentary
This passage from the Hanafi usul work Al-Tarwih (a commentary on Al-Tawdih) deals with the classification of words (alfaz) and the precise definition of mushtarak (the homonym/equivocal word). The author follows the matn of Sadr al-Shariah and expands it.

The passage begins by completing the division: a word is either for multiple meanings or a single meaning. If for multiple meanings and placed for each meaning separately (wad' kathir), it is mushtarak. If for multiple meanings but with a single placement (wad' wahid), then if the meanings are unrestricted (ghayr mahsur), the word either covers all individuals ('amm) or not (jam' munkar). If the multiple meanings are restricted (mahsur) to a specific number, it is from the divisions of khass.

If a word is placed for a single meaning, whether personal, type-specific, or generic, it is also khass. Thus the divisions reduce to: mushtarak, 'amm, khass, and the intermediate (wasita) which is the indefinite plural.

Then the definition of mushtarak is given: 'what is placed for multiple meanings with multiple placements.' An important clarification follows: 'kathra' (multiplicity) here is understood in contrast to 'wahda' (oneness), not to 'qilla' (paucity). Therefore, a word shared between only two meanings qualifies as mushtarak. This is a key nuance in Hanafi usul.

The commentator then addresses an objection (i'tirad) to this definition: it is said to be lacking in man' (exclusivity) because it would include names that were originally generic then became proper nouns (like 'asad' used as a personal name), and technical terms used in different disciplines (like 'zakat' in fiqh vs. language, or 'fi'l' in grammar vs. fiqh). The text responds that according to some scholars (ba'd), such words are not considered mushtarak. This reflects a careful Hanafi position: only words that were independently placed for each meaning from the start (or at least without a single original generic meaning) are mushtarak; transferred meanings (manqulat) are not mushtarak because they are not placed originally with multiple independent placements.

The commentary in Urdu elaborates further: it explains the division, clarifies the objection about two meanings, and reiterates that transferred meanings like 'zakat' and 'fi'l' are not mushtarak. This passage thus provides a detailed definition of mushtarak within the Hanafi taxonomy of words, emphasizing the conditions of wad' kathir and the specific understanding of kathra.

Key Terms
المشترک (al-mushtarak): A word placed for multiple meanings with multiple placements; multiplicity means more than one.
العام (al-‘amm): A word that encompasses all individuals of what it is suitable for without restriction.
الخاص (al-khass): A word placed for a single specific meaning, whether personal, type, or generic.
الجمع المنكر (al-jam‘ al-munkar): An indefinite plural that does not encompass all individuals; it is the intermediate between 'amm and khass.

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul definition in this passage, what is the minimum number of meanings a mushtarak word must have?
A) Three or more
B) Two
C) At least one
D) Any number above zero

Key Takeaway
Mushtarak is defined by multiple independent placements for multiple meanings, with 'multiple' meaning more than one, not three or more.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

The Fourfold Classification of Words: Khas, Amm, Mushtarak, and Jama' Munkar
Explaining the fourfold classification of words based on meaning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a given Arabic word into one of the four categories (khas, amm, mushtarak, jama' munkar) by analyzing its coinage and scope, and explain the Hanafi principle regarding 'amm.

Core Idea
A word's legal meaning depends on its coinage: one meaning (khas), multiple coinages (mushtarak), single coinage covering all (amm), or partial (jama' munkar).

This passage from a Hanafi usul commentary breaks down words by how they are coined. Understanding this classification is essential for interpreting Qur'an and Sunnah correctly. The Hanafi school holds that 'amm is definitive until specified, unlike some other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the word and its coinage
Determine whether the word is coined for a single meaning or multiple meanings. If multiple, check if the coinage is single or multiple.
Coinage refers to the original linguistic assignment of a word to a meaning.
2
Check for mushtarak
If there are multiple independent coinages for different meanings, the word is mushtarak (homonym), e.g., 'عَيْن' meaning eye, spring, etc.
3
Analyze single coinage with multiple meanings
If the coinage is single but the word covers multiple meanings, determine if those meanings are limited (محصور) or unlimited (غير محصور).
If limited, proceed to khas. If unlimited, check coverage.
4
Distinguish 'amm from jama' munkar
If the word covers all individuals of the category (e.g., all men) it is 'amm. If it does not cover all (e.g., some men), it is jama' munkar (indefinite plural).
Example: 'الناس' (the people) is 'amm; 'رجال' (men, indefinite) is jama' munkar.
5
Subclassify khas
If the word is coined for a single meaning or limited meanings, it is khas. Then further classify based on the referent: individual (fardi), species (naw'i), or genus (jinsi).
Example: 'مُحَمَّد' (a proper name) is khas fardi; 'إِنْسَان' (human) as a species is khas naw'i; 'حَيَوَان' (animal) is khas jinsi.
